10008{_}2102{_}I am sure they intend to get hold of it.
10008{_}2103{_}The affair is coming to a head."
10008{_}2104{_}Captain Selover listened almost indifferently.
10008{_}2105{_}"I came back from the islands last year," he piped, "with three hundred thousand dollars' worth of pearls.
10008{_}2106{_}There was sixteen in the crew, and every man of them was blood hungry for them pearls.
10008{_}2107{_}They had three or four shindies and killed one man over the proper way to divide the loot after they had got it.
10008{_}2108{_}They didn't get it.
10008{_}2109{_}Why?"
10008{_}2110{_}He drew his powerful figure to its height and spread his thick arms out in the luxury of stretching.
10008{_}2111{_}"Why?"
10008{_}2112{_}he repeated, exhaling abruptly.
10008{_}2113{_}"Because their captain was Ezra Selover!
10008{_}2114{_}Well, Mr. Eagen," he went on crisply, "Captain Ezra Selover is their captain, _and they know it_!
10008{_}2115{_}They'll talk and palaver and git into dark corners, and sharpen their knives, and perhaps fight it out as to which one's going to work the monkey-doodle business in the doctor's chest, and which one's going to tie up the sacks of them diamonds, but they won't git any farther as long as Captain Ezra is on deck."
10008{_}2116{_}"Yes," I objected, "but they mean business.
10008{_}2117{_}Last night in the squall one of them tried to throw me overboard."
10008{_}2118{_}Captain Selover grinned.
10008{_}2119{_}"What did you do?"
10008{_}2120{_}he asked.
10008{_}2121{_}"Hazed him to his quarters with a belaying pin."
10008{_}2122{_}"Well, that's all settled then, isn't it?
10008{_}2123{_}What more do you want?"
10008{_}2124{_}I stood undecided.
10008{_}2125{_}"I can take care of myself," he went on.
10008{_}2126{_}"You ought to take care of yourself.
10008{_}2127{_}Then there's nothing more to do."
10008{_}2128{_}He mused a moment.
10008{_}2129{_}"You have a gun, of course?"
10008{_}2130{_}he inquired.
10008{_}2131{_}"I forgot to ask."
10008{_}2132{_}"No," said I.
10008{_}2133{_}He whistled.
10008{_}2134{_}"Well, no wonder you feel sort of lost and hopeless!
10008{_}2135{_}Here, take this, it'll make a man of you."
10008{_}2136{_}He gave me a Colt's 45, the barrel of which had been filed down to about two inches of length.
10008{_}2137{_}It was a most extraordinary weapon, but effective at short range.
10008{_}2138{_}"Here's a few loose cartridges," said he.
10008{_}2139{_}"Now go easy.
10008{_}2140{_}This is no warship, and we ain't got men to experiment on.
10008{_}2141{_}Lick 'em with your fists or a pin, if you can; and if you do shoot, for God's sake just wing 'em a little.
10008{_}2142{_}They're awful good lads, but a little restless."
10008{_}2143{_}I took the gun and felt better.
10008{_}2144{_}With it I could easily handle the members of my own watch, and I did not doubt that with the assistance of Percy Darrow even a surprise would hardly overwhelm us.
10008{_}2145{_}I did not count on Dr. Schermerhorn.
10008{_}2146{_}He was quite capable of losing himself in a problem of trajectory after the first shot.
10008{_}2147{_}VI  THE ISLAND   I came on deck one morning at about four bells to find the entire ship's company afoot.
10008{_}2148{_}Even the doctor was there.
10008{_}2149{_}Everybody was gazing eagerly at a narrow, mountainous island lying slate-coloured across the early morning.
10008{_}2150{_}We were as yet some twenty miles distant from it, and could make out nothing but its general outline.
10008{_}2151{_}The latter was sharply defined, rising and falling to a highest point one side of the middle.
10008{_}2152{_}Over the island, and raggedly clasping its sides, hung a cloud, the only one visible in the sky.
10008{_}2153{_}I joined the afterguard.
10008{_}2154{_}"You see?"
10008{_}2155{_}the doctor was exclaiming.
10008{_}2156{_}"It iss as I haf said.
10008{_}2157{_}The island iss there.
10008{_}2158{_}Everything iss as it should be!"
10008{_}2159{_}He was quite excited.
10008{_}2160{_}Percy Darrow, too, was shaken out of his ordinary calm.
10008{_}2161{_}"The volcano is active," was his only comment, but it explained the ragged cloud.
10008{_}2162{_}"You say there's a harbour?"
10008{_}2163{_}inquired Captain Selover.
10008{_}2164{_}"It should be on the west end," said Dr. Schermerhorn.
10008{_}2165{_}Captain Selover drew me one side.
10008{_}2166{_}He, too was a little aroused.
10008{_}2167{_}"Now wouldn't that get you?"
10008{_}2168{_}he squeaked.
10008{_}2169{_}"Doctor runs up against a Norwegian bum who tells him about a volcanic island, and gives its bearings.
10008{_}2170{_}The island ain't on the map at all.
10008{_}2171{_}Doctor believes it, and makes me lay my course for those bearings.
10008{_}2172{_}_And here's the island_!
10008{_}2173{_}So the bum's story was true!
10008{_}2174{_}I'd like to know what the rest of it was!"
10008{_}2175{_}His eyes were shining.
10008{_}2176{_}"Do we anchor or stand off and on?"
10008{_}2177{_}I asked.
10008{_}2178{_}Captain Selover turned to grip me by the shoulder.
10008{_}2179{_}"I have orders from Darrow to get to a good berth, to land, to build shore quarters, and to snug down for a stay of a year at least!"
10008{_}2180{_}We stared at each other.
10008{_}2181{_}"Joyous prospect," I muttered.
10008{_}2182{_}"Hope there's something to do there."
10008{_}2183{_}The morning wore, and we rapidly approached the island.
10008{_}2184{_}It proved to be utterly precipitous.
10008{_}2185{_}The high rounded hills sloped easily to within a hundred feet or so of the water and then fell away abruptly.
10008{_}2186{_}Where the earth ended was a fantastic filigree border, like the fancy paper with which our mothers used to line the pantry shelves.
10008{_}2187{_}Below, the white surges flung themselves against the cliffs with a wild abandon.
10008{_}2188{_}Thousands of sea birds wheeled in the eddies of the wind, thousands of ravens perched on the slopes.
10008{_}2189{_}With our glasses we could make out the heads of seals fishing outside the surf, and a ragged belt of kelp.
10008{_}2190{_}When within a mile we put the helm up, and ran for the west end.
10008{_}2191{_}A bold point we avoided far out, lest there should be outlying ledges.
10008{_}2192{_}Then we came in sight of a broad beach and pounding surf.
10008{_}2193{_}I was ordered to take a surf boat and investigate for a landing and an anchorage.
10008{_}2194{_}The swell was running high.
10008{_}2195{_}We rowed back and forth, puzzled as to how to get ashore with all the freight it would be necessary to land.
10008{_}2196{_}The ship would lie well enough, for the only open exposure was broken by a long reef over which we could make out the seas tumbling.
10008{_}2197{_}But inshore the great waves rolled smoothly, swiftly-- then suddenly fell forward as over a ledge, and spread with a roar across the yellow sands.
10008{_}2198{_}The fresh winds blew the spume back to us.
10008{_}2199{_}We conversed in shouts.
10008{_}2200{_}"We can surf the boat," yelled Thrackles, "but we can't land a load."
10008{_}2201{_}That was my opinion.
10008{_}2202{_}We rowed slowly along, parallel to the shore, and just outside the line of breakers.
10008{_}2203{_}I don't know exactly how to tell you the manner in which we became aware of the cove.
10008{_}2204{_}It was as nearly the instantaneous as can be imagined.
10008{_}2205{_}One minute I looked ahead on a cliff as unbroken as the side of a cabin; the very next I peered down the length of a cove fifty fathoms long by about ten wide, at the end of which was a gravel beach.
10008{_}2206{_}I cried out sharply to the men.
10008{_}2207{_}They were quite as much astonished as I.
10008{_}2208{_}We backed water, watching closely.
10008{_}2209{_}At a given point the cove and all trace of its entrance disappeared.
10008{_}2210{_}We could only just make out the line where the headlands dissolved into the background of the cliffs, and that merely because we knew of its existence.
10008{_}2211{_}The blending was perfect.
10008{_}2212{_}We rowed in.
10008{_}2213{_}The water was still.
10008{_}2214{_}A faint ebb and flow whispered against the tiny gravel beach at the end.
10008{_}2215{_}I noted a practicable way from it to the top of the cliff, and from the cliff down again to the sand beach.
10008{_}2216{_}Everything was perfect.
10008{_}2217{_}The water was a beautiful light green, like semi-opaque glass, and from the indistinctness of its depths waved and beckoned, rose and disappeared with indescribable grace and deliberation long feathery sea growths.
10008{_}2218{_}In a moment the bottom abruptly shallowed.
10008{_}2219{_}The motion of the boat toward the beach permitted us to catch a hasty glimpse of little fish darting, of big fish turning, of yellow sand and some vivid colour.
10008{_}2220{_}Then came the grate of gravel and the scraping of the boat's bottom on the beach.
10008{_}2221{_}We jumped ashore eagerly.
10008{_}2222{_}I left the men, very reluctant, and ascended a natural trail to a high sloping down over which blew the great Trades.
10008{_}2223{_}Grass sprung knee-high.
10008{_}2224{_}A low hill rose at the back.
10008{_}2225{_}From below the fall of the cliff came the pounding of surf.
10008{_}2226{_}I walked to the edge.
10008{_}2227{_}Various ledges, sloping toward me, ran down to the sea.
10008{_}2228{_}Against one of them was a wreck, not so very old, head on, her afterworks gone.
10008{_}2229{_}I recognised the name _Golden Horn_, and was vastly astonished to find her here against this unknown island.
10008{_}2230{_}Far up the coast I could see--with the surges dashing up like the explosion of shells, and the cliffs, and the rampart of hills grown with grass and cactus.
10008{_}2231{_}A bold promontory terminated the coast view to the north, and behind it I could glimpse a more fertile and wooded country.
10008{_}2232{_}The sky was partly overcast by the volcanic murk.
10008{_}2233{_}It fled before the Trades, and the red sun alternately blazed and clouded through it.
10008{_}2234{_}As there was nothing more to be seen here, I turned above the hollow of our cove, skirted the base of the hill, and so down to the beach.
10008{_}2235{_}It occupied a wide semicircle where the hills drew back.
10008{_}2236{_}The flat was dry and grown with thick, coarse grass.
10008{_}2237{_}A stream emerged from a sort of canon on its landward side.
10008{_}2238{_}I tasted it, found it sulphurous, and a trifle worse than lukewarm.
10008{_}2239{_}A little nearer the cliff, however, was a clear, cold spring from the rock, and of this I had a satisfying drink.
10008{_}2240{_}When I arose from my knees, I made out an animal on the hill crest looking at me, but before I could distinguish its characteristics it had disappeared.
10008{_}2241{_}I returned along the tide sands.
10008{_}2242{_}The surf dashed and roared, lifting seaweeds of a blood red, so that in places the water looked pink.
10008{_}2243{_}Seals innumerable watched me from just outside the breakers.
10008{_}2244{_}As the waves lifted to a semi-transparence, I could make out others playing, darting back and forth, up and down like disturbed tadpoles, clinging to the wave until the very instant of its fall, then disappearing as though blotted out.
10008{_}2245{_}The salt smell of seaweed was in my nostrils: I found the place pleasant--  With these few and scattered impressions we returned to the ship.
10008{_}2246{_}It had been warped to a secure anchorage, and snugged down.
10008{_}2247{_}Dr. Schermerhorn and Darrow were on deck waiting to go ashore.
10008{_}2248{_}I made my report.
10008{_}2249{_}The two passengers disappeared.
10008{_}2250{_}They carried lunch and would not be back until night-fall.
10008{_}2251{_}We had orders to pitch a large tent at a suitable spot and to lighten ship of the doctor's personal and scientific effects.
10008{_}2252{_}By the time this was accomplished, the two had returned.
10008{_}2253{_}"It's all right," Darrow volunteered to Captain Selover, as he came over the side.
10008{_}2254{_}"We've found what we want."
10008{_}2255{_}Their clothes were picked by brush and their boots muddy.
10008{_}2256{_}Next morning Captain Selover detailed me to especial work.
10008{_}2257{_}"You'll take two of the men and go ashore under Darrow's orders," said he.
10008{_}2258{_}Darrow told us to take clothes for a week, an axe apiece, and a block and tackle.
10008{_}2259{_}We made up our ditty bags, stepped into one of the surf boats, and were rowed ashore.
10008{_}2260{_}There Darrow at once took the lead.
10008{_}2261{_}Our way proceeded across the grass flat, through the opening of the narrow canon, and so on back into the interior by way of the bed through which flowed the sulphur stream.
10008{_}2262{_}The country was badly eroded.
10008{_}2263{_}Most of the time we marched between perpendicular clay banks about forty feet high.
10008{_}2264{_}These were occasionally broken by smaller tributary arroyos of the same sort.
10008{_}2265{_}It would have been impossible to reach the level of the upper country.
10008{_}2266{_}The bed of the main arroyo was flat, and grown with grasses and herbage of an extraordinary vividness, due, I supposed, to the sulphur water.
10008{_}2267{_}The stream itself meandered aimlessly through the broader bed.
10008{_}2268{_}It steadily grew warmer and the sulphur smell more noticeable.
10008{_}2269{_}Above us we could see the sky and the sharp clay edge of the arroyo.
10008{_}2270{_}I noticed the tracks of Darrow and Dr. Schermerhorn made the day before.
10008{_}2271{_}After a mile of this, the bottom ran up nearly to the level of the sides, and we stepped out on the floor of a little valley almost surrounded by more hills.
10008{_}2272{_}It was an extraordinary place, and since much happened there, I must give you an idea of it.
10008{_}2273{_}It was round and nearly encircled by naked painted hills.
10008{_}2274{_}From its floor came steam and a roaring sound.
10008{_}2275{_}The steam blew here and there among the pines on the floor; rose to eddy about the naked painted hills.
10008{_}2276{_}At one end we saw intermittently a broad ascending canon--deep red and blue-black--ending in the cone of a smoking volcano.
10008{_}2277{_}The other seemed quite closed by the sheer hills; in fact the only exit was the route by which we had come.
10008{_}2278{_}For the hills were utterly precipitous.
10008{_}2279{_}I suppose a man might have made his way up the various knobs, ledges, and inequalities, but it would have required long study and a careful head.
10008{_}2280{_}I, myself, later worked my way a short distance, merely to examine the texture of their marvellous colour.
10008{_}2281{_}This was at once varied and of great body--not at all like the smooth, glossed colour of most rock, but soft and rich.
10008{_}2282{_}You've seen painters' palettes--it was just like that, pasty and _fat_.
10008{_}2283{_}There were reds of all shades, from a veritable scarlet to a red umber; greens, from sea-green to emerald; several kinds of blue, and an indeterminate purple-mauve.
10008{_}2284{_}The whole effect was splendid and barbaric.
10008{_}2285{_}We stopped and gasped as it hit our eyes.
10008{_}2286{_}Darrow alone was unmoved.
10008{_}2287{_}He led the way forward and in an instant had disappeared behind the veil of steam.
10008{_}2288{_}Thrackles and Perdosa hung back murmuring, but at a sharp word from me gathered their courage in their two hands and proceeded.
10008{_}2289{_}We found that the first veil of steam, and a fearful stench of gases, proceeded from a miniature crater whose edge was heavily encrusted with a white salt.
10008{_}2290{_}Beyond, close under the rise of the hill, was another.
10008{_}2291{_}Between the two Percy Darrow had stopped and was waiting.
10008{_}2292{_}He eyed us with his lazy, half-quizzical glance as we approached.
10008{_}2293{_}"Think the place is going to blow up?"
10008{_}2294{_}he inquired, with a tinge of irony.
10008{_}2295{_}"Well, it isn't."
10008{_}2296{_}He turned to me.
10008{_}2297{_}"Here's where we shall stay for a while.
10008{_}2298{_}You and the men are to cut a number of these pine trees for a house.
10008{_}2299{_}Better pick out the little ones, about three or four inches through: they're easier handled.
10008{_}2300{_}I'll be back by noon."
10008{_}2301{_}We set to work then in the roaring, steaming valley with the vapour swirling about us, sometimes concealing us, sometimes half revealing us gigantic, again in the utterness of exposure showing us dwindled pigmies against the magnitudes about us.
10008{_}2302{_}The labour was not difficult.
10008{_}2303{_}By the time Darrow returned we had a pile of the saplings ready for his next direction.
10008{_}2304{_}He was accompanied by the Nigger, very much terrified, very much burdened with food and cooking utensils.
10008{_}2305{_}The assistant was lazily relating tales of voodoos, a glimmer of mischief in his eyes.
10008{_}2306{_}VII  CAPTAIN SELOVER LOSES HIS NERVE   I lived in the place for three weeks.
10008{_}2307{_}We were afoot shortly after daybreak, under way by sun-up, and at work before the heats began.
10008{_}2308{_}Three of us worked on the buildings, and the rest formed a pack train carrying all sorts of things from the shore to the valley.
10008{_}2309{_}The men grumbled fiercely at this, but Captain Selover drove them with slight regard for their opinions or feelings.
10008{_}2310{_}"You're getting double pay," was his only word, "earn it!"
10008{_}2311{_}They certainly earned it during those three weeks.
10008{_}2312{_}The things they brought up were astounding.
10008{_}2313{_}Besides a lot of scientific apparatus and chests of chemical supplies, everything that could possibly be required, had been provided by that omniscient young man.
10008{_}2314{_}After we had built a long, low structure, windows were forthcoming, shelves, tables, sinks, faucets, forges, burners, all cut out, fitted and ready to put together, each with its proper screws, nails, clamps, or pipes ready to our hands.
10008{_}2315{_}When we had finished, we had constructed as complete a laboratory on a small scale as you could find on a college campus, even to the stone pillar down to bed-rock for delicate microscopic experiments, and hot and cold water led from the springs.
10008{_}2316{_}And we were utterly unskilled.
10008{_}2317{_}It was all Percy Darrow.
10008{_}2318{_}I was toward the last engaged in screwing on a fixture for the generation of acetelyne gas.
10008{_}2319{_}"Darrow," said I, "there's one thing you've overlooked; you forgot to bring a cupola and a gilt weather-cock for this concern."
10008{_}2320{_}After the laboratory was completed, we put up sleeping quarters for the two men, with wide porches well screened, and a square, heavy storeroom.
10008{_}2321{_}By the end of the third week we had quite finished.
10008{_}2322{_}Dr. Schermerhorn had turned with enthusiasm to the unpacking of his chemical apparatus.
10008{_}2323{_}Almost immediately at the close of the freight-carrying, he had appeared, lugging his precious chest, this time suffering the assistance of Darrow, and had camped on the spot.
10008{_}2324{_}We could not induce him to leave, so we put up a tent for him.
10008{_}2325{_}Darrow remained with him by way of safety against the men, whose measure, I believe, he had taken.
10008{_}2326{_}Now that all the work was finished, the doctor put in a sudden appearance.
10008{_}2327{_}"Percy," said he, "now we will have the defence built."
10008{_}2328{_}He dragged us with him to the narrow part of the arroyo, just before it rose to the level of the valley.
10008{_}2329{_}"Here we will build the stockade-defence," he announced.
10008{_}2330{_}Darrow and I stared at each other blankly.
10008{_}2331{_}"What for, sir?"
10008{_}2332{_}inquired the assistant.
10008{_}2333{_}"I haf come to be undisturbed," announced the doctor, with owl-like, Teutonic gravity, "and I will not be disturbed."
10008{_}2334{_}Darrow nodded to me and drew his principal aside.
10008{_}2335{_}They conversed earnestly for several minutes.
10008{_}2336{_}Then the assistant returned to me.
10008{_}2337{_}"No use," he shrugged in complete return to his indifferent manner.
10008{_}2338{_}"Stockade it is.
10008{_}2339{_}Better make it of fourteen foot logs, slanted out.
10008{_}2340{_}Dig a trench across, plant your logs three or four feet, bind them at the top.
10008{_}2341{_}That's his specification for it.
10008{_}2342{_}Go at it."
10008{_}2343{_}"But," I expostulated, "what's the _use_ of it?
10008{_}2344{_}Even if the men were dangerous, that would just make them think you _did_ have something to guard."
10008{_}2345{_}"I know that.
10008{_}2346{_}Orders," replied Percy Darrow.
10008{_}2347{_}We built the stockade in a day.
10008{_}2348{_}When it was finished we marched to the beach, and never, save in the three instances of which I shall later tell you, did I see the valley again.
10008{_}2349{_}The next day we washed our clothes, and moved ashore with all our belongings.
10008{_}2350{_}"I'm not going to have this crew aboard," stated Captain Selover positively, "I'm going to clean her."
10008{_}2351{_}He himself stayed, however.
10008{_}2352{_}We rowed in, constructed a hasty fireplace of stones, spread our blankets, and built an unnecessary fire near the beach.
10008{_}2353{_}"Clean her!"
10008{_}2354{_}grumbled Thrackles, "my eye!"
10008{_}2355{_}"I'd rather round the Cape," growled Pulz hopelessly.
10008{_}2356{_}"Come, now, it can't be as bad as all that," I tried to cheer them.
10008{_}2357{_}"It can't be more than a week or ten days' job, even if we careen her."
10008{_}2358{_}"You don't know what you're talking about," said Thrackles.
10008{_}2359{_}"It's worse than the yellow jack.
10008{_}2360{_}It's six weeks at least.
10008{_}2361{_}Mind when we last 'cleaned her'?"
10008{_}2362{_}he inquired of Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2363{_}"You can kiss the Book on it," replied he.
10008{_}2364{_}"Down by the line in that little swab of a sand island.
10008{_}2365{_}My eye, but _don't_ I remember!
10008{_}2366{_}I sweated my liver white."
10008{_}2367{_}They smoked in silence.
10008{_}2368{_}"That's a main queer contrivance of the Perfessor's--that stockade-like," ventured Solomon, after a little.
10008{_}2369{_}"He doesn't want any intrusion," I said.
10008{_}2370{_}"These scientific experiments are very delicate."
10008{_}2371{_}"Quite like," he commented non-committally.
10008{_}2372{_}We slept on the ground that night, and next morning, under Captain Selover's directions, we commenced the task of lightening the ship.
10008{_}2373{_}He detailed the Nigger and Perdosa for special duty.
10008{_}2374{_}"I'll just see to your shore quarters," he squeaked.
10008{_}2375{_}"You empty her."
10008{_}2376{_}All day long we rowed back and forth from the ship to the cove, landing the contents of the hold.
10008{_}2377{_}These, by good fortune, we did not have to carry over the neck of land, for just above the gravel beach was a wide ledge on which we could pile the stores.
10008{_}2378{_}We ate aboard, and so had no opportunity of seeing what Captain Selover and his men were about, until evening.
10008{_}2379{_}Then we discovered that they had collected and lowered to the beach a quantity of stateroom doors from the wreck, and had trundled the galley stove to the edge where it awaited our assistance.
10008{_}2380{_}We hitched a cable to it, and let it down gently.
10008{_}2381{_}The Nigger was immensely pleased.
10008{_}2382{_}After some experiment he got it to draw, and so cooked us our supper on it.
10008{_}2383{_}After supper, Captain Selover rowed himself back to the ship.
10008{_}2384{_}"Eagen," he had said, drawing me aside, "I'm going to leave you with them.
10008{_}2385{_}It's better that one of us--I think as owner I ought to be aboard----"  "Of course, sir," said I, "it's the only proper place for you."
10008{_}2386{_}"I'm glad you think so," he rejoined, apparently relieved.
10008{_}2387{_}"And anyway," he cried, with a burst of feeling, "I hate the gritty feeling of it under my feet!
10008{_}2388{_}Solid oak's the only walking for a man."
10008{_}2389{_}He left me hastily, as though a trifle ashamed.
10008{_}2390{_}I thought he seemed depressed, even a little furtive, and yet on analysis I could discover nothing definite on which to base such a conclusion.
10008{_}2391{_}It was rather a feeling of difference from the man I had known.
10008{_}2392{_}In my fatigue it seemed hardly worth thinking about.
10008{_}2393{_}The men had rolled themselves in their blankets, tired with the long day.
10008{_}2394{_}Next morning Captain Selover was ashore early.
10008{_}2395{_}He had quite recovered his spirits, and offered me a dram of French brandy, which I refused.
10008{_}2396{_}We worked hard again; again the master returned at night to his vessel, this time without a word to any of us; again the men, drugged by toil, turned in early and slept like the dead.
10008{_}2397{_}We became entangled in a mesh of days like these, during which things were accomplished, but in which was no space for anything but the tasks imposed upon us.
10008{_}2398{_}The men for the most part had little to say.
10008{_}2399{_}"Por Dios, eet is too mooch work!"
10008{_}2400{_}sighed Perdosa once.
10008{_}2401{_}"Why don't you kick to the Old Man, then?"
10008{_}2402{_}sneered Thrackles.
10008{_}2403{_}The silence that followed, and the sullenness with which Perdosa readdressed himself to his work, was significant enough of Captain Selover's past relations with the men.
10008{_}2404{_}And how we did clean her!
10008{_}2405{_}We stripped her of every stitch and sliver until she floated high, an empty hull, even her spars and running rigging ashore.
10008{_}2406{_}I understood now the crew's grumbling.
10008{_}2407{_}We literally went at her with a nail brush.
10008{_}2408{_}Captain Selover took charge of us when we had reached this period.
10008{_}2409{_}He and the Nigger and Perdosa had long since finished the installation of the permanent camp.
10008{_}2410{_}They had built us huts from the wreck, collecting stateroom doors for the sides, and hatches for the roofs, huge and solid, with iron rings in them.
10008{_}2411{_}The bronze and iron ventilation gratings to the doors gave us glimpses of the coast through fretwork; the rich inlaying of woods surrounded us.
10008{_}2412{_}We set up on a solid rock the galley stove--with its rails to hold the cooking pots from upsetting, in a sea way.
10008{_}2413{_}In it we burned the debris of the wreck, all sorts of wood, some sweet and aromatic and spicy as an incensed cathedral.
10008{_}2414{_}I have seen the Nigger boiling beans over a blaze of sandal wood fragrant as an Eastern shop.
10008{_}2415{_}First we scrubbed the _Laughing Lass_, then we painted her, and resized and tarred her standing rigging, resized and rove her running gear, slushed her masts, finally careened her and scraped and painted her below.
10008{_}2416{_}When we had quite finished, we had the anchor chain dealt out to us in fathoms, and scraped, pounded and polished that.
10008{_}2417{_}These were indeed days full of labour.
10008{_}2418{_}Being busy from morning until night we knew but little of what was about us.
10008{_}2419{_}We saw the open sea and the waves tumbling over the reef outside.
10008{_}2420{_}We saw the headlands, and the bow of the bay and the surf with its watching seals and the curve of yellow sands.
10008{_}2421{_}We saw the sweep of coast and the downs and the strange huts we had built out of departed magnificence.
10008{_}2422{_}And that was all; that constituted our world.
10008{_}2423{_}In the evening sometimes we lit a big bonfire, sailor fashion, just at the edge of the beach.
10008{_}2424{_}There we sat at ease and smoked our pipes in silence, too tired to talk.
10008{_}2425{_}Even Handy Solomon's song was still.
10008{_}2426{_}Outside the circle of light were mysterious things--strange wavings of white hands, bendings of figures, callings of voices, rustling of feet.
10008{_}2427{_}We knew them for the surf and the wind in the grasses: but they were not the less mysterious for that.
10008{_}2428{_}Logically Captain Selover and I should have passed most of our evenings together.
10008{_}2429{_}As a matter of fact we so spent very few.
10008{_}2430{_}Early in the dusk the captain invariably rowed himself out to his beloved schooner.
10008{_}2431{_}What he did there I do not know.
10008{_}2432{_}We could see his light now in one part of her, now in the other.
10008{_}2433{_}The men claimed he was scrubbing her teeth.
10008{_}2434{_}"Old Scrubs" they called him to his back: never Captain Selover.
10008{_}2435{_}"He has to clean up after his own feet, he's so dirty," sagely proffered Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2436{_}And this was true.
10008{_}2437{_}The seaman's prophecy held good.
10008{_}2438{_}Seven weeks held us at that infernal job--seven weeks of solid, grinding work.
10008{_}2439{_}The worst of it was, that we were kept at it so breathlessly, as though our very existence were to depend on the headlong rush of our labour.
10008{_}2440{_}And then we had fully half the stores to put away again, and the other half to transport painfully over the neck of land from the cove to the beach.
10008{_}2441{_}So accustomed had I become to the routine in which we were involved, so habituated to anticipating the coming day as exactly like the day that had gone, that the completion of our job caught me quite by surprise.
10008{_}2442{_}I had thrown myself down by the fire prepared for the some old half hour of drowsy nicotine, to be followed by the accustomed heavy sleep, and the usual early rising to toil.
10008{_}2443{_}The evening was warm; I half closed my eyes.
10008{_}2444{_}Handy Solomon was coming in last.
10008{_}2445{_}Instead of dropping to his place, he straddled the fire, stretching his arms over his head.
10008{_}2446{_}He let them fall with a sharp exhalation.
10008{_}2447{_}"'Lay aloft, lay aloft,' the jolly bos'n cried.
10008{_}2448{_}_Blow high, blow low, what care we!_   'Look ahead, look astern, look a-windward, look a-lee.'
10008{_}2449{_}_Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e._"  The effect was electrical.
10008{_}2450{_}We all sprang to our feet and fell to talking at once.
10008{_}2451{_}"By God, we're _through_!"
10008{_}2452{_}cried Pulz.
10008{_}2453{_}"I'd clean forgot it!"
10008{_}2454{_}The Nigger piled on more wood.
10008{_}2455{_}We drew closer about the fire.
10008{_}2456{_}All the interests in life, so long held in the background, leaped forward, eager for recognition.
10008{_}2457{_}We spoke of trivialities almost for the first time since our landing, fused into a temporary but complete good fellowship by the relief.
10008{_}2458{_}"Wonder how the old doctor is getting on?"
10008{_}2459{_}ventured Thrackles, after a while.
10008{_}2460{_}"The devil's a preacher!
10008{_}2461{_}I wonder?"
10008{_}2462{_}cried Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2463{_}"Let's make 'em a call," suggested Pulz.
10008{_}2464{_}"Don't believe they'd appreciate the compliment," I laughed.
10008{_}2465{_}"Better let them make first call: they're the longer established."
10008{_}2466{_}This was lost on them, of course.
10008{_}2467{_}But we all felt kindly to one another that evening.
10008{_}2468{_}I carried the glow of it with me over until next morning, and was therefore somewhat dashed to meet Captain Selover, with clouded brows and an uncertain manner.
10008{_}2469{_}He quite ignored my greeting.
10008{_}2470{_}"By God, Eagen," he squeaked, "can you think of anything more to be done?"
10008{_}2471{_}I straightened my back and laughed.
10008{_}2472{_}"Haven't you worked us hard enough?"
10008{_}2473{_}I inquired.
10008{_}2474{_}"Unless you gild the cabins, I don't see what else there can be to do."
10008{_}2475{_}Captain Selover stared me over.
10008{_}2476{_}"And you a naval man!"
10008{_}2477{_}he marvelled.
10008{_}2478{_}"Don't you see that the only thing that keeps this crew from gettin' restless is keeping them busy?
10008{_}2479{_}I've sweat a damn sight more with my brain than you have with your back thinking up things to do.
10008{_}2480{_}I can't see anything ahead, and then we'll have hell to pay.
10008{_}2481{_}Oh, they're a sweet lot!"
10008{_}2482{_}I whistled and my crest fell.
10008{_}2483{_}Here was a new point of view; and also a new Captain Ezra.
10008{_}2484{_}Where was the confidence in the might of his two hands?
10008{_}2485{_}He seemed to read my thoughts, and went on.
10008{_}2486{_}"I don't feel _sure_ here on this cussed land.
10008{_}2487{_}It ain't like a deck where a man has some show.
10008{_}2488{_}They can scatter.
10008{_}2489{_}They can hide.
10008{_}2490{_}It ain't right to put a man ashore alone with such a crew.
10008{_}2491{_}I'm doing my best, but it ain't goin' to be good enough.
10008{_}2492{_}I wisht we were safe in 'Frisco harbour----"  He would have maundered on, but I seized his arm and led him out of possible hearing of the men.
10008{_}2493{_}"Here, buck up!"
10008{_}2494{_}I said to him sternly.
10008{_}2495{_}"There's nothing to be scared of.
10008{_}2496{_}If it comes to a row, there's three of us and we've got guns.
10008{_}2497{_}We could even sail the schooner at a pinch, and leave them here.
10008{_}2498{_}You've stood them off before."
10008{_}2499{_}"Not ashore," protested Captain Selover weakly.
10008{_}2500{_}"Well, they don't know that.
10008{_}2501{_}For God's sake don't let them see you've lost your nerve this way."
10008{_}2502{_}He did not even wince at the accusation.
10008{_}2503{_}"Put up a front."
10008{_}2504{_}He shook his head.
10008{_}2505{_}The sand had completely run out of him.
10008{_}2506{_}Yet I am convinced that if he could have felt the heave and roll of the deck beneath him, he would have faced three times the difficulties he now feared.
10008{_}2507{_}However, I could see readily enough the wisdom of keeping the men at work.
10008{_}2508{_}"You can wreck the _Golden Horn_," I suggested.
10008{_}2509{_}"I don't know whether there's anything left worth salvage; but it'll be something to do."
10008{_}2510{_}He clapped me on the shoulder.
10008{_}2511{_}"Good!"
10008{_}2512{_}he cried, "I never thought of it."
10008{_}2513{_}"Another thing," said I, "you better give them a day off a week.
10008{_}2514{_}That can't hurt them and it'll waste just that much more time."
10008{_}2515{_}"All right," agreed Captain Selover.
10008{_}2516{_}"Another thing yet.
10008{_}2517{_}You know I'm not lazy, so it ain't that I'm trying to dodge work.
10008{_}2518{_}But you'd better lay me off.
10008{_}2519{_}It'll be so much more for the others."
10008{_}2520{_}"That's true," said he.
10008{_}2521{_}I could not recognise the man for what I knew him to be.
10008{_}2522{_}He groped, as one in the dark, or as a sea animal taken out of its element and placed on the sands.
10008{_}2523{_}Courage had given place to fear; decision to wavering; and singleness of purpose to a divided counsel.
10008{_}2524{_}He who had so thoroughly dominated the entire ship, eagerly accepted advice of me--a man without experience.
10008{_}2525{_}That evening I sat apart considerably disturbed.
10008{_}2526{_}I felt that the ground had dropped away beneath my feet.
10008{_}2527{_}To be sure, everything was tranquil at present; but now I understood the source of that tranquillity and how soon it must fail.
10008{_}2528{_}With opportunity would come more scheming, more speculation, more cupidity.
10008{_}2529{_}How was I to meet it, with none to back me but a scared man, an absorbed man, and an indifferent man?
10008{_}2530{_}VIII  WRECKING OF THE GOLDEN HORN   Percy Darrow, unexpected, made his first visit to us the very next evening.
10008{_}2531{_}He sauntered in with a Mexican corn-husk cigarette between his lips, carrying a lantern; blew the light out, and sat down with a careless greeting, as though he had seen us only the day before.
10008{_}2532{_}"Hullo, boys," said he, "been busy?"
10008{_}2533{_}"How are ye, sir?"
10008{_}2534{_}replied Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2535{_}"Good Lord, mates, look at that!"
10008{_}2536{_}Our eyes followed the direction of his forefinger.
10008{_}2537{_}Against the dark blue of the evening sky to northward glowed a faint phosphorescence, arch-shaped, from which shot, with pulsating regularity, long shafts of light.
10008{_}2538{_}They beat almost to the zenith, and back again, a half dozen times, then the whole illumination disappeared with the suddenness of gas turned out.
10008{_}2539{_}"Now I wonder what that might be!"
10008{_}2540{_}marvelled Thrackles.
10008{_}2541{_}"Northern lights," hazarded Pulz.
10008{_}2542{_}"I've seen them almost like that in the Behring Seas."
10008{_}2543{_}"Northern lights your eye!"
10008{_}2544{_}sneered Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2545{_}"You may have seen them in the Behring Seas, but never this far south, and in August, and you can, kiss the Book on that."
10008{_}2546{_}"What do you think, sir?"
10008{_}2547{_}Thrackles inquired of the assistant.
10008{_}2548{_}"Devil's fire," replied Percy Darrow briefly.
10008{_}2549{_}"The island's a little queer.
10008{_}2550{_}I've noticed it before."
10008{_}2551{_}"Debbil fire," repeated the Nigger.
10008{_}2552{_}Darrow turned directly to him.
10008{_}2553{_}"Yes, devil's fire; and devils, too, for all I know; and certainly vampires.
10008{_}2554{_}Did you ever hear of vampires, Doctor?"
10008{_}2555{_}"No," growled the Nigger.
10008{_}2556{_}"Well, they are women, wonderful, beautiful women.
10008{_}2557{_}A man on a long voyage would just smack his lips to see them.
10008{_}2558{_}They have shiny grey eyes, and lips red as raspberries.
10008{_}2559{_}When you meet them they will talk with you and go home with you.
10008{_}2560{_}And then when you're asleep they tear a little hole in your neck with their sharp claws, and they suck the blood with their red lips.
10008{_}2561{_}When they aren't women, they take the shape of big bats like birds."
10008{_}2562{_}He turned to me with so beautifully casual an air that I wanted to clap him on the back with the joy of it.
10008{_}2563{_}"By the way, Eagen, have you noticed those big bats the last few evenings, over by the cliff?
10008{_}2564{_}_I_ can't make out in the dusk whether they are vampires or just plain bats."
10008{_}2565{_}He directed his remarks again to the Nigger.
10008{_}2566{_}"Next time you see any of those big bats, Doctor, just you notice close.
10008{_}2567{_}If they have just plain, black eyes, they're all right; but if they have grey eyes, with red rims around 'em, they're vampires.
10008{_}2568{_}I wish you'd let me know, if you do find out.
10008{_}2569{_}It's interesting."
10008{_}2570{_}"Don' get me near no bats," growled the Nigger.
10008{_}2571{_}"Where's Selover?"
10008{_}2572{_}inquired Darrow.
10008{_}2573{_}"He stays aboard," I hastened to say.
10008{_}2574{_}"Wants to keep an eye on the ship."
10008{_}2575{_}"That's laudable.
10008{_}2576{_}What have you been doing?"
10008{_}2577{_}"We've been cleaning ship.
10008{_}2578{_}Just finished yesterday evening."
10008{_}2579{_}"What next?"
10008{_}2580{_}"We were thinking of wrecking the _Golden Horn_."
10008{_}2581{_}"Quite right.
10008{_}2582{_}Well, if you want any help with your engines or anything of the sort, call on me."
10008{_}2583{_}He arose and began to light his lantern.
10008{_}2584{_}"I hope as how you're getting on well there above, sir?"
10008{_}2585{_}ventured Handy Solomon insinuatingly.
10008{_}2586{_}"Very well, I thank you, my man," replied Percy Darrow drily.
10008{_}2587{_}"Remember those vampires, Doctor."
10008{_}2588{_}He swung the lantern and departed without further speech.
10008{_}2589{_}We followed the spark of it until it disappeared in the arroyo.
10008{_}2590{_}Behind us bellowed the sea; over against us in the sky was the dull threatening glow of the volcano; about us were mysterious noises of crying birds, barking seals, rustling or rushing winds.
10008{_}2591{_}I felt the thronging ghosts of all the old world's superstition swirling madly behind us in the eddies that twisted the smoke of our fire.
10008{_}2592{_}We wrecked the _Golden Horn_.
10008{_}2593{_}Forward was a rusted-out donkey engine, which we took to pieces and put together again.
10008{_}2594{_}It was no mean job, for all the running parts had to be cleaned smooth, and with the exception of a rudimentary knowledge on the part of Pulz and Perdosa, we were ignorant.
10008{_}2595{_}In fact we should not have succeeded at all had it not been for Percy Darrow and his lantern.
10008{_}2596{_}The first evening we took him over to the cliff's edge he laughed aloud.
10008{_}2597{_}"Jove, boys, how could you guess it _all_ wrong," he wondered.
10008{_}2598{_}With a few brief words he set us right, Pulz, Perdosa, and I listening intently; the others indifferent in the hopelessness of being able to comprehend.
10008{_}2599{_}Of course, we went wrong again in our next day's experiments; but Darrow was down two or three times a week, and gradually we edged toward a practical result.
10008{_}2600{_}His explanations consumed but a few moments.
10008{_}2601{_}After they were finished, we adjourned to the fire.
10008{_}2602{_}Thus we came gradually to a better acquaintance with the doctor's assistant.
10008{_}2603{_}In many respects he remained always a puzzle, to me.
10008{_}2604{_}Certainly the men never knew how to take him.
10008{_}2605{_}He was evidently not only unafraid of them, but genuinely indifferent to them.
10008{_}2606{_}Yet he displayed a certain interest in their needs and affairs.
10008{_}2607{_}His practical knowledge was enormous.
10008{_}2608{_}I think I have told you of the completeness of his arrangements--everything had been foreseen from grindstones to gas nippers.
10008{_}2609{_}The same quality of concrete speculation showed him what we lacked in our own lives.
10008{_}2610{_}There was, as you remember, the matter of Handy Solomon's steel claw.
10008{_}2611{_}He showed Thrackles a kind of lanyard knot that deep-sea person had never used.
10008{_}2612{_}He taught Captain Selover how to make soft soap out of one species of seaweed.
10008{_}2613{_}Me, he initiated in the art of fishing with a white bone lure.
10008{_}2614{_}Our camp itself he reconstructed on scientific lines so that we enjoyed less aromatic smoke and more palatable dinner.
10008{_}2615{_}And all of it he did amusedly, as though his ideas were almost too obvious to need communication.
10008{_}2616{_}We became in a manner intimate with him.
10008{_}2617{_}He guyed the men in his indolent fashion, playing on their credulity, their good nature, even their forbearance.
10008{_}2618{_}They alternately grinned and scowled.
10008{_}2619{_}He left always a confused impression, so that no one really knew whether he cherished rancour against Percy Darrow or kindly feeling.
10008{_}2620{_}The Nigger was Darrow's especial prey.
10008{_}2621{_}The assistant had early discovered that the cook was given to signs, omens, and superstitions.
10008{_}2622{_}From a curious scholar's lore he drew fantastics with which to torment his victim.
10008{_}2623{_}We heard of all the witches, warlocks, incubi, succibi, harpies, devils, imps, and haunters of Avitchi, from all the teachings of history, sacred and profane, Hindu, Egyptian, Greek, mediaeval, Swedenborg, Rosicrucian, theosophy, theology, with every last ounce of horror, mystery, shivers, and creeps squeezed out of them.
10008{_}2624{_}They were gorgeous ghost stories, for they were told by a man fully informed as to all the legendary and gruesome details.
10008{_}2625{_}At first I used to think he might have communicated it more effectively.
10008{_}2626{_}Then I saw that the cool, drawling manner, the level voice, were in reality the highest art.
10008{_}2627{_}He told his stories in a half-amused, detached manner which imposed confidence more readily than any amount of earnest asseveration.
10008{_}2628{_}The mere fact of his own belief in what he said came to matter little.
10008{_}2629{_}He was the vehicle by which was brought accurate knowledge.
10008{_}2630{_}He had read all these things, and now reported them as he had read: each man could decide for himself as to their credibility.
10008{_}2631{_}At last the donkey engine was cleared and reinstalled, atop the cliff.
10008{_}2632{_}The Nigger built under her a fire of black walnut; Captain Selover handed out grog all around; and we started her up with a cheer, just to see the wheels revolve.
10008{_}2633{_}Next we half buried some long hatches, end up, to serve as bitts for the lines, hitched our cables to them, and joyfully commenced the task of pulling the _Golden Horn_ piece by piece up the side of the cliff.
10008{_}2634{_}The stores were badly damaged by the wet, and there was no liquor, for which I was sincerely grateful.
10008{_}2635{_}We broke into the boxes, and arrayed ourselves in various garments--which speedily fell to pieces--and appropriated gim-cracks of all sorts.
10008{_}2636{_}There were some arms, but the ammunition had gone bad.
10008{_}2637{_}Perdosa, out of forty or fifty mis-fires, got one feeble sputter, and a tremendous _bang_ which blew up his piece, leaving only the stock in his hand.
10008{_}2638{_}A few tinned goods were edible; but all the rest was destroyed.
10008{_}2639{_}A lot of hard woods, a thousand feet of chain cable, and a fairly good anchor might be considered as prizes.
10008{_}2640{_}As for the rest, it was foolishness, but we hauled it up just the same until nothing at all remained.
10008{_}2641{_}Then we shut off the donkey engine, and put on dry clothes.
10008{_}2642{_}We had been quite happy for the eight months.
10008{_}2643{_}It was now well along toward spring.
10008{_}2644{_}The winter had been like summer, and with the exception of a few rains of a week or so, we had enjoyed beautiful skies.
10008{_}2645{_}The seals had thinned out considerably, but were now returning in vast numbers ready for their annual domestic arrangements.
10008{_}2646{_}Our Sundays we had mostly spent in resting, or in fishing.
10008{_}2647{_}There were many deep sea fish to be had, of great palatability, but small gameness; they came like so many leaden weights.
10008{_}2648{_}A few of us had climbed some of the hills in a half-hearted curiosity, but from their summits saw nothing to tempt weariness.
10008{_}2649{_}Practically we knew nothing beyond the mile or so of beach on which we lived.
10008{_}2650{_}Captain Selover had made a habit of coming ashore at least once during the day.
10008{_}2651{_}He had contented himself with standing aloof, but I took pains to seem to confer with him, so that the men might suppose that I, as mate, was engaged in carrying out his directions.
10008{_}2652{_}The dread of him was my most potent influence over them.
10008{_}2653{_}During the last few days of our wrecking, Captain Selover had omitted his daily visit.
10008{_}2654{_}The fact made me uneasy, so that at my first opportunity I sculled myself out to the schooner.
10008{_}2655{_}I found him, moist-eyed as usual, leaning against the mainmast doing nothing.
10008{_}2656{_}"We've finished, sir," said I.
10008{_}2657{_}He looked at me.
10008{_}2658{_}"Will you come ashore and have a look, sir?"
10008{_}2659{_}I inquired.
10008{_}2660{_}"I ain't going ashore again," he muttered thickly.
10008{_}2661{_}"What!"
10008{_}2662{_}I cried.
10008{_}2663{_}"I ain't going ashore again," he repeated obstinately, "and that's all there is to it.
10008{_}2664{_}It's too much of a strain on any man.
10008{_}2665{_}Suit yourself.
10008{_}2666{_}You run them.
10008{_}2667{_}I shipped as captain of a vessel.
10008{_}2668{_}I'm no dock walloper.
10008{_}2669{_}I won't _do_ it--for no man!"
10008{_}2670{_}I gasped with dismay at the man's complete moral collapse.
10008{_}2671{_}It seemed incredible.
10008{_}2672{_}I caught myself wondering whether he would recover tone were he again to put to sea.
10008{_}2673{_}"My God, man, but you _must_!"
10008{_}2674{_}I cried at last.
10008{_}2675{_}"I won't, and that's flat," said he, and turned deliberately on his heel and disappeared in the cabin.
10008{_}2676{_}I went ashore thoughtful and a little scared.
10008{_}2677{_}But on reflection I regained a great part of my ease of mind.
10008{_}2678{_}You see, I had been with these men now eight months, during which they had been as orderly as so many primary schoolboys.
10008{_}2679{_}They had worked hard, without grumbling, and had even approached a sort of friendliness about the camp fire.
10008{_}2680{_}My first impression was overlaid.
10008{_}2681{_}As I looked back on the voyage, with what I took to be a clearer vision, I could not but admit that the incidents were in themselves trivial enough--a natural excitement by a superstitious negro, a little tall talk that meant nothing.
10008{_}2682{_}It must have been the glamour of the adventure that had deceived me; that, and the unusual stage setting and costuming.
10008{_}2683{_}Certainly few men would work hard for eight months without a murmur, without a chance to look about them.
10008{_}2684{_}In that, of course, I was deceived by my inexperience.
10008{_}2685{_}I realised later the wonderful effect Captain Selover threw away with his empty brandy bottles.
10008{_}2686{_}The crew might grumble and plot during the watch below; but when Captain Ezra Selover said _work_, they worked.
10008{_}2687{_}He had been saying work, for eight months.
10008{_}2688{_}They had, from force of experience, obeyed him.
10008{_}2689{_}It was all very simple.
10008{_}2690{_}IX  THE EMPTY BRANDY BOTTLE   So there I was at once deprived of my chief support.
10008{_}2691{_}Although no danger seemed imminent, nevertheless the necessity of acting on my own initiative and responsibility oppressed me somewhat.
10008{_}2692{_}Truth to tell, after the first, I was more relieved than dismayed at the captain's resolution to stay aboard.
10008{_}2693{_}His drinking habit was growing on him, and afloat or ashore he was now little more than a figurehead, so that my chief asset as far as he was concerned, was rather his reputation than his direct influence.
10008{_}2694{_}In contact with the men, I dreaded lest sooner or later he do something to lessen or destroy the awe in which they held him.
10008{_}2695{_}Of course Dr. Schermerhorn had been mistaken in his man: A real captain of men would have risen to circumstances wherever he found them.
10008{_}2696{_}But who could have foretold?
10008{_}2697{_}Captain Selover had been a rascal always, but a successful and courageous rascal.
10008{_}2698{_}He had run desperate chances, dominated desperate crews.
10008{_}2699{_}Who could know that a crumble of island beach and six months ashore would turn him into what he had become?
10008{_}2700{_}Yet I believe such cases are not uncommon in other walks of life.
10008{_}2701{_}A man and his work combine to mean something; yet both may be absolutely useless when separated.
10008{_}2702{_}It was the weak link----  I put in some time praying earnestly that the eyes of the crew might be blinded, and that the doctor would finish his experiments before the cauldron could boil up again.
10008{_}2703{_}My first act as real commander was to announce holiday.
10008{_}2704{_}My idea was that the island would keep the men busy for a while.
10008{_}2705{_}Then I would assign them more work to do.
10008{_}2706{_}They proposed at once a tour into the interior.
10008{_}2707{_}We started up the west coast.
10008{_}2708{_}After three or four miles along a mesa formation where often we had to circle long detours to avoid the gullies, we came upon another short beach, and beyond it a series of ledges on which basked several hundred seals.
10008{_}2709{_}They did not seem alarmed.
10008{_}2710{_}In fact one old bull, scarred by many battles, made toward us.
10008{_}2711{_}We left him, scaled the cliff, and turned up a broad, pleasant valley toward the interior.
10008{_}2712{_}There the later lava flow had been deflected.
10008{_}2713{_}All that showed of the original eruption were occasional red outcropping rocks.
10008{_}2714{_}Soil and grass had overlaid the mineral.
10008{_}2715{_}Scattered trees were planted throughout the flat.
10008{_}2716{_}Cacti and semi-tropical bushes mingled with brush on the rounded side hills.
10008{_}2717{_}A number of brilliant birds fluttered at our approach.
10008{_}2718{_}Suddenly Handy Solomon, who was in advance, stopped and pointed to the crest of the hill.
10008{_}2719{_}A file of animals moved along the sky line.
10008{_}2720{_}"Mutton!"
10008{_}2721{_}said he, "or the devil's a preacher!"
10008{_}2722{_}"Sheep!"
10008{_}2723{_}cried Thrackles.
10008{_}2724{_}"Where did they come from?"
10008{_}2725{_}"_Golden Horn_," I suggested.
10008{_}2726{_}"Remember that wide, empty deck forward?
10008{_}2727{_}They carried sheep there."
10008{_}2728{_}The men separated, intending fresh meat.
10008{_}2729{_}The affair was ridiculous.
10008{_}2730{_}These sheep had become as wild as deer.
10008{_}2731{_}Our surrounding party with its silly bared knives could only look after them open-mouthed, as they skipped nimbly between its members.
10008{_}2732{_}"Get a gun of the Old Man, Mr. Eagen," suggested Pulz, "and we'll have something besides salt horse and fish."
10008{_}2733{_}I nodded.
10008{_}2734{_}We continued.
10008{_}2735{_}The island was like this as far as we went.
10008{_}2736{_}When we climbed a ridge, we found ourselves looking down on a spider-web of other valleys and canons of the same nature, all diverging to broad downs and a jump into the sea, all converging to the outworks that guarded the volcano with its canopy of vapour.
10008{_}2737{_}On our way home we cut across the higher country and the heads of the canons until we found ourselves looking down on the valley and Dr. Schermerhorn's camp.
10008{_}2738{_}The steam from the volcanic blowholes swayed below us.
10008{_}2739{_}Through its rifts we saw the tops of the buildings.
10008{_}2740{_}Presently we made out Percy Darrow, dressed in overalls, his sleeves rolled back, and carrying a retort.
10008{_}2741{_}He walked, very preoccupied, to one of the miniature craters, where he knelt and went through some operation indistinguishable at the distance.
10008{_}2742{_}I looked around to see my companions staring at him fascinated, their necks craned out, their bodies drawn back into hiding.
10008{_}2743{_}In a moment he had finished, and carried the retort carefully into the laboratory.
10008{_}2744{_}The men sighed and stood erect, once more themselves.
10008{_}2745{_}As we turned away Perdosa voiced what must have been in the minds of all.
10008{_}2746{_}"A man could climb down there," said he.
10008{_}2747{_}"Why should he want to?"
10008{_}2748{_}I demanded sharply.
10008{_}2749{_}"_Quien sabe_?"
10008{_}2750{_}shrugged he.
10008{_}2751{_}We turned in silence toward the beach.
10008{_}2752{_}Each brooded his thoughts.
10008{_}2753{_}The sight of that man dressed in overalls, carrying on some mysterious business, brought home to each of us the fact that our expedition had an object, as yet unknown to us.
10008{_}2754{_}The thought had of late dropped into the background.
10008{_}2755{_}For my part I had been so immersed in the adventure and the labour and the insistent need of the hour that I had forgotten why I had come.
10008{_}2756{_}Dr. Schermerhorn's purpose was as inscrutable to me as at first.
10008{_}2757{_}What had I accomplished?
10008{_}2758{_}The men, too, seemed struck with some such idea.
10008{_}2759{_}There were no yarns about the camp fire that night.
10008{_}2760{_}Percy Darrow did not appear, for which I was sincerely sorry.
10008{_}2761{_}His presence might have created a diversion.
10008{_}2762{_}For some unknown reason all my old apprehensions, my sense of impending disaster, had returned to me strengthened.
10008{_}2763{_}In the firelight the Nigger's sullen face looked sinister, Pulz's nervous white countenance looked vicious.
10008{_}2764{_}Thrackles' heavy, bulldog expression was threatening, Perdosa's Mexican cast fit for knife work in the back.
10008{_}2765{_}And Handy Solomon, stretched out, leaning on his elbow, with his red headgear, his snaky hair, his hook nose, his restless eye and his glittering steel claw--the glow wrote across his aura the names of Kid, Morgan, Blackbeard.
10008{_}2766{_}They sat smoking, staring into the fire with mesmerised eyes.
10008{_}2767{_}The silence got on my nerves I arose impatiently and walked down the pale beach, where the stars glimmered in splashes along the wettest sands.
10008{_}2768{_}The black silhouette of the hills against the dark blue of the night sky; the white of breakers athwart the indistinct heave of the ocean, a faint light marking the position of the _Laughing Lass_--that was everything in the world.
10008{_}2769{_}I made out some object rolled about in the edge of the wash. At the cost of wet feet I rescued it.
10008{_}2770{_}It was an empty brandy bottle.
10008{_}2771{_}[Illustration: "These sheep had become as wild as deer"]     X  CHANGE OF MASTERS   The next day we continued our explorations by land, and so for a week after that.
10008{_}2772{_}I thought it best not to relinquish all authority, so I organised regular expeditions, and ordered their direction.
10008{_}2773{_}The men did not object.
10008{_}2774{_}It was all good enough fun to them.
10008{_}2775{_}The net results were that we found a nesting place of sea birds--too late in the season for eggs; a hot spring near enough camp to be useful; and that was about all.
10008{_}2776{_}The sheep were the only animals on the island, although there were several sorts of birds.
10008{_}2777{_}In general, the country was as I have described it--either volcanic or overlaid with fertile earth.
10008{_}2778{_}In any case it was canon and hill.
10008{_}2779{_}We soon grew tired of climbing and turned our attention to the sea.
10008{_}2780{_}With the surf boat we skirted the coast.
10008{_}2781{_}It was impregnable except in three places: our own beach, that near the seal rookery, and on the south side of the island.
10008{_}2782{_}We landed at each one of these places.
10008{_}2783{_}But returning close to the coast we happened upon a cave mouth more or less guarded by an outlying rock.
10008{_}2784{_}The day was calm, so we ventured in.
10008{_}2785{_}At first I thought it merely a gorge in the rock, but even while peering for the end wall we slipped under the archway and found ourselves in a vast room.
10008{_}2786{_}Our eyes were dazzled so we could make out little at first.
10008{_}2787{_}But through the still, clear water the light filtered freely from below, showing the bottom as through a sea glass.
10008{_}2788{_}We saw the fish near the entrance, and coral and sea growths of marvellous vividness.
10008{_}2789{_}They waved slowly as in a draught of air.
10008{_}2790{_}The medium in which they floated was absolutely invisible, for, of course, there were no reflections from its surface.
10008{_}2791{_}We seemed to be suspended in mid-air, and only when the dipping oars made rings could we realise that anything sustained us.
10008{_}2792{_}Suddenly the place let loose in pandemonium.
10008{_}2793{_}The most fiendish cries, groans, shrieks, broke out, confusing themselves so thoroughly with their own echoes that the volume of sound was continuous.
10008{_}2794{_}Heavy splashes shook the water.
10008{_}2795{_}The boat rocked.
10008{_}2796{_}The invisible surface was broken into facets.
10008{_}2797{_}We shrank, terrified.
10008{_}2798{_}From all about us glowed hundreds of eyes like coals of fire--on a level with us, above us, almost over our heads.
10008{_}2799{_}Two by two the coals were extinguished.
10008{_}2800{_}Below us the bottom was clouded with black figures, darting rapidly like a school of minnows beneath a boat.
10008{_}2801{_}They darkened the coral and the sands and the glistening sea growths just as a cloud temporarily darkens the landscape--only the occultations and brightenings succeeded each other much more swiftly.
10008{_}2802{_}We stared stupefied, our thinking power blurred by the incessent whirl of motion and noise.
10008{_}2803{_}Suddenly Thrackles laughed aloud.
10008{_}2804{_}"Seals!"
10008{_}2805{_}he shouted through his trumpeted hands.
10008{_}2806{_}Our eyes were expanding to the twilight.
10008{_}2807{_}We could make out the arch of the room, its shelves, and hollows, and niches.
10008{_}2808{_}Lying on them we could discern the seals, hundreds and hundreds of them, all staring at us, all barking and bellowing.
10008{_}2809{_}As we approached, they scrambled from their elevations, and, diving to the bottom, scurried to the entrance of the cave.
10008{_}2810{_}We lay on our oars for ten minutes.
10008{_}2811{_}Then silence fell.
10008{_}2812{_}There persisted a tiny _drip, drip, drip_ from some point in the darkness.
10008{_}2813{_}It merely accentuated the hush.
10008{_}2814{_}Suddenly from far in the interior of the hill there came a long, hollow _boo-o-o-m_!
10008{_}2815{_}It reverberated, roaring.
10008{_}2816{_}The surge that had lifted our boat some minutes before thus reached its journey's end.
10008{_}2817{_}The chamber was very lofty.
10008{_}2818{_}As we rowed cautiously in, it lost nothing of its height, but something in width.
10008{_}2819{_}It was marvellously coloured, like all the volcanic rocks of this island.
10008{_}2820{_}In addition some chemical drip had thrown across its vividness long gauzy streamers of white.
10008{_}2821{_}We rowed in as far as the faintest daylight lasted us.
10008{_}2822{_}The occasional reverberating _boom_ of the surges seemed as distant as ever.
10008{_}2823{_}This was beyond the seal rookery on the beach.
10008{_}2824{_}Below it we entered an open cleft of some size to another squarer cave.
10008{_}2825{_}It was now high tide; the water extended a scant ten fathoms to end on an interior shale beach.
10008{_}2826{_}The cave was a perfectly straight passage following the line of the cleft.
10008{_}2827{_}How far in it reached we could not determine, for it, too, was full of seals, and after we had driven them back a hundred feet or so their fiery eyes scared us out.
10008{_}2828{_}We did not care to put them at bay.
10008{_}2829{_}The next day I rowed out to the _Laughing Lass_ and got a rifle.
10008{_}2830{_}I found the captain asleep in his bunk, and did not disturb him.
10008{_}2831{_}Perdosa and I, with infinite pains, tracked and stalked the sheep, of which I killed one.
10008{_}2832{_}We found the mutton excellent.
10008{_}2833{_}The hunting was difficult, and the quarry, as time went on, more and more suspicious, but henceforward we did not lack for fresh meat.
10008{_}2834{_}Furthermore we soon discovered that fine trolling was to be had outside the reef.
10008{_}2835{_}We rigged a sail for the extra dory, and spent much of our time at the sport.
10008{_}2836{_}I do not know the names of the fish.
10008{_}2837{_}They were very gamy indeed, and ran from five to an indeterminate number of pounds in weight.
10008{_}2838{_}Above fifty pounds our light tackle parted, so we had no means of knowing how large they may have been.
10008{_}2839{_}Thus we spent very pleasantly the greater part of two weeks.
10008{_}2840{_}At the end of that time I made up my mind that it would be just as well to get back to business.
10008{_}2841{_}Accordingly I called Perdosa and directed him to sort and clear of rust the salvaged chain cable.
10008{_}2842{_}He refused flatly.
10008{_}2843{_}I took a step toward him.
10008{_}2844{_}He drew his knife and backed away.
10008{_}2845{_}"Perdosa," said I firmly, "put up that knife."
10008{_}2846{_}"No," said he.
10008{_}2847{_}I pulled the saw-barrelled Colt's 45 and raised it slowly to a level with his breast.
10008{_}2848{_}"Perdosa," I repeated, "drop that knife."
10008{_}2849{_}The crisis had come, but my resolution was fully prepared for it.
10008{_}2850{_}I should not have cared greatly if I had had to shoot the man--as I certainly should have done had he disobeyed.
10008{_}2851{_}There would then have been one less to deal with in the final accounting, which strangely enough I now for a moment never doubted would come.
10008{_}2852{_}I had not before aimed at a man's life, so you can see to what tensity the baffling mystery had strung me.
10008{_}2853{_}Perdosa hesitated a fraction of an instant.
10008{_}2854{_}I really think he might have chanced it, but Handy Solomon, who had been watching me closely, growled at him.
10008{_}2855{_}"Drop it, you fool!"
10008{_}2856{_}he said.
10008{_}2857{_}Perdosa let fall the knife.
10008{_}2858{_}"Now, get at that cable," I commanded, still at white heat.
10008{_}2859{_}I stood over him until he was well at work, then turned back to set tasks for the other men.
10008{_}2860{_}Handy Solomon met me halfway.
10008{_}2861{_}"Begging your pardon, Mr. Eagen," said he, "I want a word with you."
10008{_}2862{_}"I have nothing to say to you," I snapped, still excited.
10008{_}2863{_}"It ain't reasonable not to hear a man's say," he advised in his most conciliatory manner, "I'm talking for all of us."
10008{_}2864{_}He paused a moment, took my silence for consent, and went ahead.
10008{_}2865{_}"Begging your pardon, Mr. Eagen," said he, "we ain't going to do any more useless work.
10008{_}2866{_}There ain't no laziness about us, but we ain't going to be busy at nothing.
10008{_}2867{_}All the camp work and the haulin' and cuttin' and cleanin' and the rest of it, we'll do gladly.
10008{_}2868{_}But we ain't goin' to pound any more cable, and you can kiss the Book on that."
10008{_}2869{_}"You mean to mutiny?"
10008{_}2870{_}I asked.
10008{_}2871{_}He made a deprecatory gesture.
10008{_}2872{_}"Put us aboard ship, sir, and let us hear the Old Man give his orders, and you'll find no mutiny in us.
10008{_}2873{_}But here ashore it's different.
10008{_}2874{_}Did the Old Man give orders to pound the cable?"
10008{_}2875{_}"I represent the captain," I stammered.
10008{_}2876{_}He caught the evasion.
10008{_}2877{_}"I thought so.
10008{_}2878{_}Well, if you got any kick on us, please, sir, go get the Old Man.
10008{_}2879{_}If he says to our face, pound cable, why pound cable it is.
10008{_}2880{_}Ain't that right, boys?"
10008{_}2881{_}They murmured something.
10008{_}2882{_}Perdosa deliberately dropped his hammer and joined the group.
10008{_}2883{_}My hand strayed again toward the sawed-off Colt's 45.
10008{_}2884{_}"I wouldn't do that," said Handy Solomon, almost kindly.
10008{_}2885{_}"You couldn't kill us all.
10008{_}2886{_}And w'at good would it do?
10008{_}2887{_}I asks you that.
10008{_}2888{_}I can cut down a chicken with my knife at twenty feet.
10008{_}2889{_}You must surely see, sir, that I could have killed you too easy while you were covering Pancho there.
10008{_}2890{_}This ain't got to be a war, Mr. Eagen, just because we don't want to work without any sense to it."
10008{_}2891{_}There was more of the same sort.
10008{_}2892{_}I had plenty of time to see my dilemma.
10008{_}2893{_}Either I would have to abandon my attempt to keep the men busy, or I would have to invoke the authority of Captain Selover.
10008{_}2894{_}To do the latter would be to destroy it.
10008{_}2895{_}The master had become a stuffed figure, a bogie with which to frighten, an empty bladder that a prick would collapse.
10008{_}2896{_}With what grace I could muster, I had to give in.
10008{_}2897{_}"You'll have to have it your own way, I suppose," I snapped.
10008{_}2898{_}Thrackles grinned, and Pulz started to say something, but Handy Solomon, with a peremptory gesture, and a black scowl, stopped him short.
10008{_}2899{_}"Now that's what I calls right proper and handsome!"
10008{_}2900{_}he cried admiringly.
10008{_}2901{_}"We reely had no right to expect that, boys, as seamen, from our first officer!
10008{_}2902{_}You can kiss the Book on it, that very few crews have such kind masters.
10008{_}2903{_}Mr. Eagen has the right, and we signed to it all straight, to work us as he pleases; and w'at does he do?
10008{_}2904{_}Why, he up and gives us a week shore leave, and then he gives us light watches, and all the time our pay goes on just the same.
10008{_}2905{_}Now that's w'at I calls right proper and handsome conduct, or the devil's a preacher, and I ventures with all respect to propose three cheers for Mr.
10008{_}2906{_}Eagen."
10008{_}2907{_}They gave them, grinning broadly.
10008{_}2908{_}The villain stood looking at me, a sardonic gleam in the back of his eye.
10008{_}2909{_}Then he gave a little hitch to his red head covering, and sauntered away humming between his teeth.
10008{_}2910{_}I stood watching him, choked with rage and indecision.
10008{_}2911{_}The humming broke into words.
10008{_}2912{_}"'Oh, quarter, oh, quarter!'
10008{_}2913{_}the jolly pirates cried.
10008{_}2914{_}_Blow high, blow low!
10008{_}2915{_}What care we_?
10008{_}2916{_}But the quarter that we gave them was to sink them in the sea,      _Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e_."
10008{_}2917{_}"Here, you swab," he cried to Thrackles, "and you, Pancho!
10008{_}2918{_}get some wood, lively!
10008{_}2919{_}And Pulz, bring us a pail of water.
10008{_}2920{_}Doctor, let's have duff to celebrate on."
10008{_}2921{_}The men fell to work with alacrity.
10008{_}2922{_}XI  THE CORROSIVE   That evening I smoked in a splendid isolation while the men whispered apart.
10008{_}2923{_}I had nothing to do but smoke, and to chew my cud, which was bitter.
10008{_}2924{_}There could be no doubt, however I may have saved my face, that command had been taken from me by that rascal, Handy Solomon.
10008{_}2925{_}I was in two minds as to whether or not I should attempt to warn Darrow or the doctor.
10008{_}2926{_}Yet what could I say?
10008{_}2927{_}and against whom should I warn them?
10008{_}2928{_}The men had grumbled, as men always do grumble in idleness, and had perhaps talked a little wildly; but that was nothing.
10008{_}2929{_}The only indisputable fact I could adduce was that I had allowed my authority to slip through my fingers.
10008{_}2930{_}And adequately to excuse that, I should have to confess that I was a writer and no handler of men.
10008{_}2931{_}I abandoned the unpleasant train of thought with a snort of disgust, but it had led me to another.
10008{_}2932{_}In the joy and uncertainty of living I had practically lost sight of the reason for my coming.
10008{_}2933{_}With me it had always been more the adventure than the story; my writing was a by-product, a utilisation of what life offered me.
10008{_}2934{_}I had set sail possessed by the sole idea of ferreting out Dr. Schermerhorn's investigations, but the gradual development of affairs had ended by absorbing my every faculty.
10008{_}2935{_}Now, cast into an eddy by my change of fortunes, the original idea regained its force.
10008{_}2936{_}I was out of the active government of affairs, with leisure on my hands, and my thoughts naturally turned with curiosity again to the laboratory in the valley.
10008{_}2937{_}Darrow's "devil fires" were again painting the sky.
10008{_}2938{_}I had noticed them from time to time, always with increasing wonder.
10008{_}2939{_}The men accepted them easily as only one of the unexplained phenomena of a sailor's experience, but I had not as yet hit on a hypothesis that suited me.
10008{_}2940{_}They were not allied to the aurora; they differed radically from the ordinary volcanic emanations; and scarcely resembled any electrical displays I had ever seen.
10008{_}2941{_}The night was cool; the stars bright: I resolved to investigate.
10008{_}2942{_}Without further delay I arose to my feet and set off into the darkness.
10008{_}2943{_}Immediately one of the group detached himself from the fire and joined me.
10008{_}2944{_}"Going for a little walk, sir?"
10008{_}2945{_}asked Handy Solomon sweetly.
10008{_}2946{_}"That's quite right and proper.
10008{_}2947{_}Nothin' like a little walk to get you fit and right for your bunk."
10008{_}2948{_}He held close to my elbow.
10008{_}2949{_}We got just as far as the stockade in the bed of the arroyo.
10008{_}2950{_}The lights we could make out now across the zenith; but owing to the precipitance of the cliffs, and the rise of the arroyo bed, it was impossible to see more.
10008{_}2951{_}Handy Solomon felt the defences carefully.
10008{_}2952{_}"A man would think, sir, it was a cannibal island," he observed.
10008{_}2953{_}"All so tight and tidy-like here.
10008{_}2954{_}It would take a ship's guns to batter her down.
10008{_}2955{_}A man might dig under these here two gate logs, if no one was against him.
10008{_}2956{_}Like to try it, sir?"
10008{_}2957{_}"No," I answered gruffly.
10008{_}2958{_}From that time on I was virtually a prisoner; yet so carefully was my surveillance accomplished that I could place my finger on nothing definite.
10008{_}2959{_}Someone always accompanied me on my walks; and in the evening I was herded as closely as any cattle.
10008{_}2960{_}Handy Solomon took the direction of affairs off my hands.
10008{_}2961{_}You may be sure he set no very heavy tasks.
10008{_}2962{_}The men cut a little wood, carried up a few pails of water--that was all.
10008{_}2963{_}Lacking incentive to stir about, they came to spend most of their time lying on their backs watching the sky.
10008{_}2964{_}This in turn bred a languor which is the sickest, most soul- and temper-destroying affair invented by the devil.
10008{_}2965{_}They could not muster up energy enough to walk down the beach and back, and yet they were wearied to death of the inaction.
10008{_}2966{_}After a little they became irritable toward one another.
10008{_}2967{_}Each suspected the other of doing less than he should.
10008{_}2968{_}You who know men will realise what this meant.
10008{_}2969{_}The atmosphere of our camp became surly.
10008{_}2970{_}I recognised the precursor of its becoming dangerous.
10008{_}2971{_}One day on a walk in the hills I came on Thrackles and Pulz lying on their stomachs gazing down fixedly at Dr. Schermerhorn's camp.
10008{_}2972{_}This was nothing extraordinary, but they started guiltily to their feet when they saw me, and made off, growling under their breaths.
10008{_}2973{_}All this that I have told you so briefly, took time.
10008{_}2974{_}It was the eating through of men's spirits by that worst of corrosives, idleness.
10008{_}2975{_}I conceive it unnecessary to weary you with the details----  The situation was as yet uneasy but not alarming.
10008{_}2976{_}One evening I overheard the beginning of an absurd plot to gain entrance to the Valley--that was as far as detail went.
10008{_}2977{_}I became convinced at last that I should in some way warn Percy Darrow.
10008{_}2978{_}That seems a simple enough proposition, does it not?
10008{_}2979{_}But if you will stop to think one moment of the difficulties of my position, you will see that it was not as easy as at first it appears.
10008{_}2980{_}Darrow still visited us in the evening.
10008{_}2981{_}The men never allowed me even the chance of private communication while he was with us.
10008{_}2982{_}One or two took pains to stretch out between us.
10008{_}2983{_}Twice I arose when the assistant did, resolved to accompany him part way back.
10008{_}2984{_}Both times men resolutely escorted us, and as resolutely separated us from the opportunity of a single word apart.
10008{_}2985{_}The crew never threatened me by word or look.
10008{_}2986{_}But we understood each other.
10008{_}2987{_}I was not permitted to row out to the _Laughing Lass_ without escort.
10008{_}2988{_}Therefore I never attempted to visit her again.
10008{_}2989{_}The men were not anxious to do so, their awe of the captain made them only too glad to escape his notice.
10008{_}2990{_}That empty shell of a past reputation was my only hope.
10008{_}2991{_}It shielded the arms and ammunition.
10008{_}2992{_}As I look back on it now, the period seems to me to be one of merely potential trouble.
10008{_}2993{_}The men had not taken the pains to crystallise their ideas.
10008{_}2994{_}I really think their compelling emotion was that of curiosity.
10008{_}2995{_}They wanted to _see_.
10008{_}2996{_}It needed a definite impulse to change that desire to one of greed.
10008{_}2997{_}The impulse came from Percy Darrow and his idle talk of voodoos.
10008{_}2998{_}As usual he was directing his remarks to the sullen Nigger.
10008{_}2999{_}"Voodoos?"
10008{_}3000{_}he said.
10008{_}3001{_}"Of course there are.
10008{_}3002{_}Don't fool yourself for a minute on that.
10008{_}3003{_}There are good ones and bad ones.
10008{_}3004{_}You can tame them if you know how, and they will do anything you want them to."
10008{_}3005{_}Pulz chuckled in his throat.
10008{_}3006{_}"You don't believe it?"
10008{_}3007{_}drawled the assistant turning to him.
10008{_}3008{_}"Well, it's so.
10008{_}3009{_}You know that heavy box we are so careful of?
10008{_}3010{_}Well, that's got a tame voodoo in it."
10008{_}3011{_}The others laughed.
10008{_}3012{_}"What he like?"
10008{_}3013{_}asked the Nigger gravely.
10008{_}3014{_}"He's a fine voodoo, with wavery arms and green eyes, and red glows."
10008{_}3015{_}Watching narrowly its effect he swung off into one of the genuine old crooning voodoo songs, once so common down South, now so rarely heard.
10008{_}3016{_}No one knows what the words mean--they are generally held to be charm-words only--a magic gibberish.
10008{_}3017{_}But the Nigger sprang across the fire like lightning, his face altered by terror, to seize Darrow by the shoulders.
10008{_}3018{_}"Doan you!
10008{_}3019{_}Doan you!"
10008{_}3020{_}he gasped, shaking the assistant violently back and forth.
10008{_}3021{_}"Dat he King Voodoo song!
10008{_}3022{_}Dat call him all de voodoo--all!"
10008{_}3023{_}He stared wildly about in the darkness as though expecting to see the night thronged.
10008{_}3024{_}There was a moment of confusion.
10008{_}3025{_}Eager for any chance I hissed under my breath; "Danger!
10008{_}3026{_}Look out!"
10008{_}3027{_}I could not tell whether or not Darrow heard me.
10008{_}3028{_}He left soon after.
10008{_}3029{_}The mention of the chest had focussed the men's interest.
10008{_}3030{_}"Well," Pulz began, "we've been here on this spot o' hell for a long time."
10008{_}3031{_}"A year and five months," reckoned Thrackles.
10008{_}3032{_}"A man can do a lot in that time."
10008{_}3033{_}"If he's busy."
10008{_}3034{_}"They've been busy."
10008{_}3035{_}"Yes."
10008{_}3036{_}"Wonder what they've done?"
10008{_}3037{_}There was no answer to this, and the sea lawyer took a new tack.
10008{_}3038{_}"I suppose we're all getting double wages."
10008{_}3039{_}"That's so."
10008{_}3040{_}"And that's say four hunder' for us and Mr. Eagen here.
10008{_}3041{_}I suppose the Old Man don't let the schooner go for nothing."
10008{_}3042{_}"Two hundred and fifty a month," said I, and then would have had the words back.
10008{_}3043{_}They cried out in prolonged astonishment.
10008{_}3044{_}"Seventeen months," pursued the logician after a few moments.
10008{_}3045{_}He scratched with a stub of lead.
10008{_}3046{_}"That makes over eleven thousand dollars since we've been out.
10008{_}3047{_}How much do you suppose his outfit stands him?"
10008{_}3048{_}he appealed to me.
10008{_}3049{_}"I'm sure I can't tell you," I replied shortly.
10008{_}3050{_}"Well, it's a pile of money, anyway."
10008{_}3051{_}Nobody said anything for some time.
10008{_}3052{_}"Wonder what they've done?"
10008{_}3053{_}Pulz asked again.
10008{_}3054{_}"Something that pays big."
