10008{_}3055{_}Thrackles supplied the desired answer.
10008{_}3056{_}"Dat chis'----" suggested Perdosa.
10008{_}3057{_}"Voodoo----" muttered the Nigger.
10008{_}3058{_}"That's to scare us out," said Handy Solomon, with vast contempt.
10008{_}3059{_}"That's what makes me sure it _is_ the chest."
10008{_}3060{_}Pulz muttered some of the jargon of alchemy.
10008{_}3061{_}"That's it," approved Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3062{_}"If we could get----"  "We wouldn't know how to use it," interrupted Pulz.
10008{_}3063{_}"The book----" said Thrackles.
10008{_}3064{_}"Well, the book----" asserted Pulz pugnaciously.
10008{_}3065{_}"How do you know what it will be?
10008{_}3066{_}It may be the Philosopher's Stone and it may be one of these other damn things.
10008{_}3067{_}And then where'd we be?"
10008{_}3068{_}It was astounding to hear this nonsense bandied about so seriously.
10008{_}3069{_}And yet they more than half believed, for they were deep-sea men of the old school, and this was in print.
10008{_}3070{_}Thrackles voiced approximately the general attitude.
10008{_}3071{_}"Philosopher's stone or not, something's up.
10008{_}3072{_}The old boy took too good care of that box, and he's spending too much money, and he's got hold of too much hell afloat to be doing it for his health."
10008{_}3073{_}"You know w'at I t'ink?"
10008{_}3074{_}smiled Perdosa.
10008{_}3075{_}"He mak' di'mon's.
10008{_}3076{_}He _say_ dat."
10008{_}3077{_}The Nigger had entered one of his black, brooding moods from which these men expected oracles.
10008{_}3078{_}"Get him ches'," he muttered.
10008{_}3079{_}"I see him full--full of di'mon's!"
10008{_}3080{_}They listened to him with vast respect, and were visibly impressed.
10008{_}3081{_}So deep was the sense of awe that Handy Solomon unbent enough to whisper to me:  "I don't take any stock in the Nigger's talk _ordinarily_.
10008{_}3082{_}He's a hell of a fool nigger.
10008{_}3083{_}But when his eye looks like that, then you want to listen close.
10008{_}3084{_}He sees things then.
10008{_}3085{_}Lots of times he's seen things.
10008{_}3086{_}Even last year--the _Oyama_--he told about her three days ahead.
10008{_}3087{_}That's why we were so ready for her," he chuckled.
10008{_}3088{_}Nothing more developed for a long time except a savage fight between Pulz and Perdosa.
10008{_}3089{_}I hunted sheep, fished, wandered about--always with an escort tired to death before he started.
10008{_}3090{_}The thought came to me to kill this man and so to escape and make cause with the scientists.
10008{_}3091{_}My common sense forbade me.
10008{_}3092{_}I begin to think that common sense is a very foolish faculty indeed.
10008{_}3093{_}It taught me the obvious--that all this idle, vapouring talk was common enough among men of this class, so common that it would hardly justify a murder, would hardly explain an unwarranted intrusion on those who employed me.
10008{_}3094{_}How would it look for me to go to them with these words in my mouth:  "The captain has taken to drinking to dull the monotony.
10008{_}3095{_}The crew think you are an alchemist and are making diamonds.
10008{_}3096{_}Their interest in this fact seemed to me excessive, so I killed one of them, and here I am."
10008{_}3097{_}"And who are you?"
10008{_}3098{_}they could ask.
10008{_}3099{_}"I am a reporter," would be my only truthful reply.
10008{_}3100{_}You can see the false difficulties of my position.
10008{_}3101{_}I do not defend my attitude.
10008{_}3102{_}Undoubtedly a born leader of men, like Captain Selover at his best, would have known how to act with the proper decision both now and in the inception of the first mutiny.
10008{_}3103{_}At heart I never doubted the reality of the crisis.
10008{_}3104{_}Even Percy Darrow saw the surliness of the men's attitudes, and with his usual good sense divined the cause.
10008{_}3105{_}"You chaps are getting lazy," said he, "why don't you do something?
10008{_}3106{_}Where's the captain?"
10008{_}3107{_}They growled something about there being nothing to do, and explained that the captain preferred to live aboard.
10008{_}3108{_}"Don't blame him," said Darrow, "but he might give us a little of his squeaky company occasionally.
10008{_}3109{_}Boys, I'll tell you something about seals.
10008{_}3110{_}The old bull seals have long, stiff whiskers--a foot long.
10008{_}3111{_}Do you know there's a market for those whiskers?
10008{_}3112{_}Well, there is.
10008{_}3113{_}The Chinese mount them in gold and use them for cleaners for their long pipes.
10008{_}3114{_}Each whisker is worth from six bits to a dollar and a quarter.
10008{_}3115{_}Why don't you kill a few bull seal for the 'trimmings'?"
10008{_}3116{_}"Nothin' to do with a voodoo?"
10008{_}3117{_}grunted Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3118{_}Darrow laughed amusedly.
10008{_}3119{_}"No, this is the truth," he assured.
10008{_}3120{_}"I'll tell you what: I'll give you boys six bits apiece for the whisker hairs, and four bits for the galls.
10008{_}3121{_}I expect to sell them at a profit."
10008{_}3122{_}Next morning they shook off their lethargy and went seal-hunting.
10008{_}3123{_}I was practically commanded to attend.
10008{_}3124{_}This attitude had been growing of late: now it began to take a definite form.
10008{_}3125{_}"Mr. Eagan, don't you want to go hunting?"
10008{_}3126{_}or "Mr. Eagen, I guess I'll just go along with you to stretch my legs," had given way to, "We're going fishing: you'd better come along."
10008{_}3127{_}I had known for a long time that I had lost any real control of them; and that perhaps humiliated me a little.
10008{_}3128{_}However, my inexperience at handling such men, and the anomalous character of my position to some extent consoled me.
10008{_}3129{_}In the filaments brushed across the face of my understanding I could discover none so strong as to support an overt act on my part.
10008{_}3130{_}I cannot doubt, that had the affair come to a focus, I should have warned the scientists even at the risk of my life.
10008{_}3131{_}In fact, as I shall have occasion to show you, I did my best.
10008{_}3132{_}But at the moment, in all policy I could see my way to little besides acquiescence.
10008{_}3133{_}We killed seals by sequestrating the bulls, surrounding them, and clubbing them at a certain point of the forehead.
10008{_}3134{_}It was surprising to see how hard they fought, and how quickly they succumbed to a blow properly directed.
10008{_}3135{_}Then we stripped the mask with its bristle of long whiskers, took the gall, and dragged the carcass into the surf where it was devoured by fish.
10008{_}3136{_}At first the men, pleased by the novelty, stripped the skins.
10008{_}3137{_}The blubber, often two or three inches in thickness, had then to be cut away from the pelt, cube by cube.
10008{_}3138{_}It was a long, an oily, and odoriferous job.
10008{_}3139{_}We stunk mightily of seal oil; our garments were shiny with it, the very pores of our skins seemed to ooze it.
10008{_}3140{_}And even after the pelt was fairly well cleared, it had still to be tanned.
10008{_}3141{_}Percy Darrow suggested the method, but the process was long, and generally unsatisfactory.
10008{_}3142{_}With the acquisition of the fifth greasy, heavy, and ill-smelling piece of fur the men's interest in peltries waned.
10008{_}3143{_}They confined themselves in all strictness to the "trimmings."
10008{_}3144{_}Percy Darrow showed us how to clean the whiskers.
10008{_}3145{_}The process was evil.
10008{_}3146{_}The masks were, quite simply, to be advanced so far in the way of putrefaction that the bristles would part readily from their sockets.
10008{_}3147{_}The first batch the men hung out on a line.
10008{_}3148{_}A few moments later we heard a mighty squawking, and rushed out to find the island ravens making off with the entire catch.
10008{_}3149{_}Protection of netting had to be rigged.
10008{_}3150{_}We caught seals for a month or so.
10008{_}3151{_}There was novelty in it, and it satisfied the lust for killing.
10008{_}3152{_}As time went on, the bulls grew warier.
10008{_}3153{_}Then we made expeditions to outlying rocks.
10008{_}3154{_}Later Handy Solomon approached me on another diplomatic errand.
10008{_}3155{_}"The seals is getting shy, sir," said he.
10008{_}3156{_}"They are," said I.
10008{_}3157{_}"The only way to do is to shoot them," said he.
10008{_}3158{_}"Quite like," I agreed.
10008{_}3159{_}A pause ensued.
10008{_}3160{_}"We've got no cartridges," he insinuated.
10008{_}3161{_}"And you've taken charge of my rifle," I pointed out.
10008{_}3162{_}"Oh, not a bit, sir," he cried.
10008{_}3163{_}"Thrackles, he just took it to clean it--you can have it whenever you want it, sir."
10008{_}3164{_}"I have no cartridges--as you have observed," said I.
10008{_}3165{_}"There's plenty aboard," he suggested.
10008{_}3166{_}"And they're in very good hands there," said I.
10008{_}3167{_}He ruminated a moment, polishing the steel of his hook against the other arm of his shirt.
10008{_}3168{_}Suddenly he looked up at me with a humorous twinkle.
10008{_}3169{_}"You're afraid of us!"
10008{_}3170{_}he accused.
10008{_}3171{_}I was silent, not knowing just how to meet so direct an attack.
10008{_}3172{_}"No need to be," he continued.
10008{_}3173{_}I said nothing.
10008{_}3174{_}He looked at me shrewdly; then stood off on another tack.
10008{_}3175{_}"Well, sir, I didn't mean just that.
10008{_}3176{_}I didn't mean you was really scared of us.
10008{_}3177{_}But we're gettin' to know each other, livin' here on this old island, brothers-like.
10008{_}3178{_}There ain't no officers and men ashore--is there, now, sir?
10008{_}3179{_}When we gets back to the old _Laughing Lass_, then we drops back into our dooty again all right and proper.
10008{_}3180{_}You can kiss the Book on that.
10008{_}3181{_}Old Scrubs, he knows that.
10008{_}3182{_}He don't want no shore in his.
10008{_}3183{_}_He_ knows enough to stay aboard, where we'd all rather be."
10008{_}3184{_}He stopped abruptly, spat, and looked at me.
10008{_}3185{_}I wondered whither this devious diplomacy led us.
10008{_}3186{_}"Still, in one way, an officer's an officer, and a seaman's a seaman, thinks you, and discipline must be held up among mates ashore or afloat, thinks you.
10008{_}3187{_}Quite proper, sir.
10008{_}3188{_}And I can see you think that the arms is for the afterguard except in case of trouble.
10008{_}3189{_}Quite proper.
10008{_}3190{_}You can do the shooting, and you can keep the cartridges always by you.
10008{_}3191{_}Just for discipline, sir."
10008{_}3192{_}The man's boldness in so fully arming me was astonishing, and his carelessness in allowing me aboard with Captain Selover astonished me still more.
10008{_}3193{_}Nevertheless I promised to go for the desired cartridges, fully resolved to make an appeal.
10008{_}3194{_}A further consideration of the elements of the game convinced me, however, of the fellow's shrewdness.
10008{_}3195{_}It was no more dangerous to allow me a rifle--under direct surveillance--for the purposes of hunting, than to leave me my sawed--off revolver, which I still retained.
10008{_}3196{_}The arguments he had used against my shooting Perdosa were quite as cogent now.
10008{_}3197{_}As to the second point, I, finding the sun unexpectedly strong, returned from the cove for my hat, and so overheard the following between Thrackles and his leader:  "What's to keep him from staying aboard?"
10008{_}3198{_}cried Thrackles, protesting.
10008{_}3199{_}"Well, he might," acknowledged Handy Solomon, "and then are we the worse off?
10008{_}3200{_}You ain't going to make a boat attack against Old Scrubs, are you?"
10008{_}3201{_}Thrackles hesitated.
10008{_}3202{_}"You can kiss the Book on it, you ain't," went on Handy Solomon easily, "nor me, nor Pulz, nor the Greaser, nor the Nigger, nor none of us all together.
10008{_}3203{_}We've had our dose of that.
10008{_}3204{_}Well, if he goes aboard and _stays_, where are we the worse off?
10008{_}3205{_}I asks you that.
10008{_}3206{_}But he won't.
10008{_}3207{_}This is w'ats goin' to happen.
10008{_}3208{_}Says he to Old Scrubs, 'Sir, the men needs you to bash in their heads.'
10008{_}3209{_}'Bash 'em in yourself,' says he, 'that's w'at you're for.'
10008{_}3210{_}And if he should come ashore, w'at could he do?
10008{_}3211{_}I asks you that.
10008{_}3212{_}We ain't disobeyed no orders dooly delivered.
10008{_}3213{_}We're ready to pull halliards at the word.
10008{_}3214{_}No, let him go aboard, and if he peaches to the Old Man, why all the better, for it just gets the Old Man down on him."
10008{_}3215{_}"How about Old Scrubs----"  "Don't you believe none in luck?"
10008{_}3216{_}asked Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3217{_}"Aye."
10008{_}3218{_}"Well, so do I, with w'at that law-crimp used to call joodicious assistance."
10008{_}3219{_}I rowed out to the _Laughing Lass_ very thoughtful, and a little shaken by the plausible argument.
10008{_}3220{_}Captain Selover was lying dead drunk across the cabin table.
10008{_}3221{_}I did my best to waken him, but failed, took a score of cartridges--no more--and departed sadly.
10008{_}3222{_}Nothing could be gained by staying aboard; every chance might be lost.
10008{_}3223{_}Besides, an opening to escape in the direction of the laboratory might offer--I, as well as they, believed in luck judiciously assisted.
10008{_}3224{_}In the ensuing days I learned much of the habits of seals.
10008{_}3225{_}We sneaked along the cliff tops until over the rookeries; then lay flat on our stomachs and peered cautiously down on our quarry.
10008{_}3226{_}The seals had become very wary.
10008{_}3227{_}A slight jar, the fall of a pebble, sometimes even sounds unnoticed by ourselves, were enough to send them into the water.
10008{_}3228{_}There they lined up just outside the surf, their sleek heads glossy with the wet, their calm, soft eyes fixed unblinkingly on us.
10008{_}3229{_}It was useless to shoot them in the water: they sank at once.
10008{_}3230{_}When, however, we succeeded in gaining an advantageous position, it was necessary to shoot with extreme accuracy.
10008{_}3231{_}A bullet directly through the back of the head would kill cleanly.
10008{_}3232{_}A hit anywhere else was practically useless, for even in death the animals seemed to retain enough blind instinctive vitality to flop them into the water.
10008{_}3233{_}There they were lost.
10008{_}3234{_}Each rookery consisted of one tremendous bull who officiated apparently as the standing army; a number of smaller bulls, his direct descendants; the cows, and the pups.
10008{_}3235{_}The big bull held his position by force of arms.
10008{_}3236{_}Occasionally other, unattached, bulls would come swimming by.
10008{_}3237{_}On arriving opposite the rookery the stranger would utter a peculiar challenge.
10008{_}3238{_}It was never refused by the resident champion, who promptly slid into the sea, and engaged battle.
10008{_}3239{_}If he conquered, the stranger went on his way.
10008{_}3240{_}If, however, the stranger won, the big bull immediately struck out to sea, abandoning his rookery, while the new-comer swam in and attempted to make his title good with all the younger bulls.
10008{_}3241{_}I have seen some fierce combats out there in the blue water.
10008{_}3242{_}They gashed each other deep----  You can see by this how our hunting was never at an end.
10008{_}3243{_}On Tuesday we would kill the boss bull of a certain establishment.
10008{_}3244{_}By Thursday, at latest, another would be installed.
10008{_}3245{_}I learned curious facts about seals in those days.
10008{_}3246{_}The hunting did not appeal to me particularly, because it seemed to me useless to kill so large an animal for so small a spoil.
10008{_}3247{_}Still, it was a means to my all-absorbing end, and I confess that the stalking, the lying belly down on the sun-warmed grass over the surge and under the clear sky, was extremely pleasant.
10008{_}3248{_}While awaiting the return of the big bull often we had opportunity to watch the others at their daily affairs, and even the unresponsive Thrackles was struck with their almost human intelligence.
10008{_}3249{_}Did you know that seals kiss each other, and weep tears when grieved?
10008{_}3250{_}The men often discussed among themselves the narrow, dry cave.
10008{_}3251{_}There the animals were practically penned in.
10008{_}3252{_}They agreed that a great killing could be made there, but the impossibility of distinguishing between the bulls and the cows deterred them.
10008{_}3253{_}The cave was quite dark.
10008{_}3254{_}Immerced in our own affairs thus, the days, weeks, and months went by.
10008{_}3255{_}Events had slipped beyond my control.
10008{_}3256{_}I had embarked on a journalistic enterprise, and now that purpose was entirely out of my reach.
10008{_}3257{_}Up the valley Dr. Schermerhorn and his assistant were engaged in some experiment of whose very nature I was still ignorant.
10008{_}3258{_}Also I was likely to remain so.
10008{_}3259{_}The precautions taken against interference by the men were equally effective against me.
10008{_}3260{_}As if that were not enough, any move of investigation on my part would be radically misinterpreted, and to my own danger, by the men.
10008{_}3261{_}I might as well have been in London.
10008{_}3262{_}However, as to my first purpose in this adventure I had evolved another plan, and therefore was content.
10008{_}3263{_}I made up my mind that on the voyage home, if nothing prevented, I would tell my story to Percy Darrow, and throw myself on his mercy.
10008{_}3264{_}The results of the experiment would probably by then be ready for the public, and there was no reason, as far as I could see, why I should not get the "scoop" at first hand.
10008{_}3265{_}Certainly my sincerity would be without question; and I hoped that two years or more of service such as I had rendered would tickle Dr. Schermerhorn's sense of his own importance.
10008{_}3266{_}So adequate did this plan seem, that I gave up thought on the subject.
10008{_}3267{_}My whole life now lay on the shores.
10008{_}3268{_}I was not again permitted to board the _Laughing Lass_.
10008{_}3269{_}Captain Selover I saw twice at a distance.
10008{_}3270{_}Both times he seemed to be rather uncertain.
10008{_}3271{_}The men did not remark it.
10008{_}3272{_}The days went by.
10008{_}3273{_}I relapsed into that state so well known to you all, when one seems caught in the meshes of a dream existence which has had no beginning and which is destined never to have an end.
10008{_}3274{_}We were to hunt seals, and fish, and pry bivalves from the rocks at low tide, and build fires, and talk, and alternate between suspicion and security, between the danger of sedition and the insanity of men without defined purpose, world without end forever.
10008{_}3275{_}XII  "OLD SCRUBS" COMES ASHORE   The inevitable happened.
10008{_}3276{_}One noon Pulz looked up from his labour of pulling the whiskers from the evil-smelling masks.
10008{_}3277{_}"How many of these damn things we got?"
10008{_}3278{_}he inquired.
10008{_}3279{_}"About three hunder' and fifty," Thrackles replied.
10008{_}3280{_}"Well, we've got enough for me.
10008{_}3281{_}I'm sick of this job.
10008{_}3282{_}It stinks."
10008{_}3283{_}They looked at each other.
10008{_}3284{_}I could see the disgust rising in their eyes, the reek of rotten blubber expanding their nostrils.
10008{_}3285{_}With one accord they cast aside the masks.
10008{_}3286{_}"It ain't such a hell of a fortune," growled Pulz, his evil little white face thrust forward.
10008{_}3287{_}"There's other things worth all the seal trimmin's of the islands."
10008{_}3288{_}"Diamon's," gloomed the Nigger.
10008{_}3289{_}"You've hit it, Doctor," cut in Solomon.
10008{_}3290{_}There we were again, back to the old difficulty, only worse.
10008{_}3291{_}Idleness descended on us again.
10008{_}3292{_}We grew touchy on little things, as a misplaced plate, a shortage of firewood, too deep a draught at the nearly empty bucket.
10008{_}3293{_}The noise of bickering became as constant as the noise of the surf.
10008{_}3294{_}If we valued peace, we kept our mouths shut.
10008{_}3295{_}The way a man spat, or ate, or slept, or even breathed became a cause of irritation to every other member of the company.
10008{_}3296{_}We stood the outrage as long as we could; then we objected in a wild and ridiculous explosion which communicated its heat to the object of our wrath.
10008{_}3297{_}Then there was a fight.
10008{_}3298{_}It needed only liquor to complete the deplorable state of affairs.
10008{_}3299{_}Gradually the smaller things came to worry us more and more.
10008{_}3300{_}A certain harmless singer of the cricket or perhaps of the tree-toad variety used to chirp his innocent note a short distance from our cabin.
10008{_}3301{_}For all I know he had done so from the moment of our installation, but I had never noticed him before.
10008{_}3302{_}Now I caught myself listening for his irregular recurrence with every nerve on the quiver.
10008{_}3303{_}If he delayed by ever so little, it was an agony; yet when he did pipe up, his feeble strain struck to my heart cold and paralysing like a dagger.
10008{_}3304{_}And with every advancing minute of the night I became broader awake, more tense, fairly sweating with nervousness.
10008{_}3305{_}One night--good God, was it only last week?
10008{_}3306{_}... it seems ages ago, another existence ... a state cut off from this by the wonder of a transmigration, at least ... Last week!
10008{_}3307{_}I did not sleep at all.
10008{_}3308{_}The moon had risen, had mounted the heavens, and now was sailing overhead.
10008{_}3309{_}By the fretwork of its radiance through the chinks of our rudely-built cabin I had marked off the hours.
10008{_}3310{_}A thunderstorm rumbled and flashed, hull down over the horizon.
10008{_}3311{_}It was many miles distant, and yet I do not doubt that its electrical influence had dried the moisture of our equanimity, leaving us rattling husks for the winds of destiny to play upon.
10008{_}3312{_}Certainly I can remember no other time, in a rather wide experience, when I have felt myself more on edge, more choked with the restless, purposeless nervous energy that leaves a man's tongue parched and his eyes staring.
10008{_}3313{_}And still that infernal cricket, or whatever it was, chirped.
10008{_}3314{_}I had thought myself alone in my vigil, but when finally I could stand it no longer, and kicked aside my covering with an oath of protest, I was surprised to hear it echoed from all about me.
10008{_}3315{_}"Damn that cricket!"
10008{_}3316{_}I cried.
10008{_}3317{_}And the dead shadows stirred from the bunks, and the hollow-eyed victims of insomnia crept out to curse their tormentor.
10008{_}3318{_}We organised an expedition to hunt him down.
10008{_}3319{_}It was ridiculous enough, six strong men prowling for the life of one poor little insect.
10008{_}3320{_}We did not find him, however, though we succeeded in silencing him.
10008{_}3321{_}But no sooner were we back in our bunks than he began it again, and such was the turmoil of our nerves that day found us sitting wan about a fire, hugging our knees.
10008{_}3322{_}We were so genuinely emptied, not so much by the cricket as by the two years of fermentation, that not one of us stirred toward breakfast, in fact not one of us moved from the listless attitude in which day found him, until after nine o'clock.
10008{_}3323{_}Then we pulled ourselves together and cooked coffee and salt horse.
10008{_}3324{_}As a significant fact, the Nigger left the dishes unwashed, and no one cared.
10008{_}3325{_}Handy Solomon finally shook himself and arose.
10008{_}3326{_}"I'm sick of this," said he, "I'm goin' seal-hunting."
10008{_}3327{_}They arose without a word.
10008{_}3328{_}They were sick of it, too, sick to death.
10008{_}3329{_}We were a silent, gloomy crew indeed as we thrust the surf boat afloat, clambered in, and shipped the oars.
10008{_}3330{_}No one spoke a word; no one had a comment to make, even when we saw the rookery slide into the water while we were still fifty yards from the beach.
10008{_}3331{_}We pulled back slowly along the coast.
10008{_}3332{_}Beyond the rock we made out the entrance to the dry cave.
10008{_}3333{_}"There's seal in there," cried Handy Solomon, "lots of 'em!"
10008{_}3334{_}He thrust the rudder over, and we headed for the cave.
10008{_}3335{_}No one expressed an opinion.
10008{_}3336{_}As it was again high tide, we rowed in to the steep shore inside the cave's mouth and beached the boat.
10008{_}3337{_}The place was full of seals; we could hear them bellowing.
10008{_}3338{_}"Two of you stand here," shouted Handy Solomon, "and take them as they go out.
10008{_}3339{_}We'll go in and scare 'em down to you."
10008{_}3340{_}"They'll run over us," screamed Pulz.
10008{_}3341{_}"No, they won't.
10008{_}3342{_}You can dodge up the sides when they go by."
10008{_}3343{_}This was indeed well possible, so we gripped our clubs and ventured into the darkness.
10008{_}3344{_}We advanced four abreast, for the cave was wide enough for that.
10008{_}3345{_}As we penetrated, the bellowing and barking became more deafening.
10008{_}3346{_}It was impossible to see anything, although we _felt_ an indistinguishable tumbling mass receding before our footsteps.
10008{_}3347{_}Thrackles swore violently as he stumbled over a laggard.
10008{_}3348{_}With uncanny abruptness the black wall of darkness in front of us was alive with fiery eyeballs.
10008{_}3349{_}The seals had reached the end of the cave and had turned toward us.
10008{_}3350{_}We, too, stopped, a little uncertain as to how to proceed.
10008{_}3351{_}The first plan had been to get behind the band and to drive it slowly toward the entrance to the cave.
10008{_}3352{_}This was now seen to be impossible.
10008{_}3353{_}The cavern was too narrow; its sides at this point too steep, and the animals too thickly congested.
10008{_}3354{_}Our eyes, becoming accustomed to the twilight, now began to make out dimly the individual bodies of the seals and the general configuration of the rocks.
10008{_}3355{_}One big boulder lay directly in our path, like an island in the shale of the cave's floor.
10008{_}3356{_}Perdosa stepped to the top of it for a better look.
10008{_}3357{_}The men attempted to communicate their ideas of what was to be done, but could not make themselves heard above the uproar.
10008{_}3358{_}I could see their faces contorting with the fury of being baffled.
10008{_}3359{_}A big bull made a dash to get by; all the herd flippered after him.
10008{_}3360{_}If he had won past they would have followed as obstinately as sheep, and nothing could have stopped them, but the big bull went down beneath the clubs.
10008{_}3361{_}Thrackles hit the animal two vindictive blows after it had succumbed.
10008{_}3362{_}This settled the revolt, and we stood as before.
10008{_}3363{_}Pulz and Handy Solomon tried to converse by signs, but evidently failed, for their faces showed angry in the twilight.
10008{_}3364{_}Perdosa, on his rock, rolled and lit a cigarette.
10008{_}3365{_}Thrackles paced to and fro, and the Nigger leaned on his club, farther down the cave.
10008{_}3366{_}They had been left at the entrance, but now in lack of results had joined their companions.
10008{_}3367{_}Now Thrackles approached and screamed himself black trying to impart some plan.
10008{_}3368{_}He failed; but stooped and picked up a stone and threw it into the mass of seals.
10008{_}3369{_}The others understood.
10008{_}3370{_}A shower of stones followed.
10008{_}3371{_}The animals milled like cattle, bellowed the louder, but would not face their tormentors.
10008{_}3372{_}Finally an old cow flopped by in a panic.
10008{_}3373{_}I thought they would have let her go, but she died a little beyond the bull.
10008{_}3374{_}No more followed, although the men threw stones as fast and hard as they were able.
10008{_}3375{_}Their faces were livid with anger, like that of an evil-tempered man with an obstinate horse.
10008{_}3376{_}Suddenly Handy Solomon put his head down, and with a roar distinctly audible even above the din that filled the cave, charged directly into the herd.
10008{_}3377{_}I saw the beasts cringe before him; I saw his club rising and falling indiscriminately; and then the whole back of the cave seemed to rise and come at us.
10008{_}3378{_}This was no chance of sport now, but a struggle for very life.
10008{_}3379{_}We realised that once down there would be no hope, for while the seals were more anxious to escape than to fight, we knew that their jaws were powerful.
10008{_}3380{_}There was no time to pick and choose.
10008{_}3381{_}We hit out with all the strength and quickness we possessed.
10008{_}3382{_}It was like a bad dream, like struggling with an elusive hydra-headed monster, knee high, invulnerable.
10008{_}3383{_}We hit, but without apparent effect.
10008{_}3384{_}New heads rose, the press behind increased.
10008{_}3385{_}We gave ground.
10008{_}3386{_}We staggered, struggling desperately to keep our feet.
10008{_}3387{_}How long this lasted I cannot tell.
10008{_}3388{_}It seemed hours.
10008{_}3389{_}I know my arms became leaden from swinging my club; my eyes were full of sweat; my breath gasped.
10008{_}3390{_}A sharp pain in my knee nearly doubled me to the ground and yet I remember clamping to the thought that I must keep my feet, keep my feet at any cost.
10008{_}3391{_}Then all at once I recalled the fact that I was armed.
10008{_}3392{_}I jerked out the short-barrelled Colt's 45 and turned it loose in their faces.
10008{_}3393{_}Whether the flash and detonation frightened them; whether Perdosa, still clinging to his rock, managed to turn their attention by his flanking efforts, or whether, quite simply, the wall of dead finally turned them back, I do not know, but with one accord they gave over the attempt.
10008{_}3394{_}I looked at once for Handy Solomon, and was surprised to see him still alive, standing upright on a ledge the other side of the herd.
10008{_}3395{_}His clothing was literally torn to shreds, and he was covered with blood.
10008{_}3396{_}But in this plight he was not alone, for when I turned toward my companions they, too, were tattered, torn, and gory.
10008{_}3397{_}We were a dreadful crew, standing there in the half-light, our chests heaving, our rags dripping red.
10008{_}3398{_}For perhaps ten seconds no one moved.
10008{_}3399{_}Then with a yell of demoniac rage my companions clambered over the rampart of dead seals and attacked the herd.
10008{_}3400{_}The seals were now cowed and defenceless.
10008{_}3401{_}It was a slaughter, and the most debauching and brutal I have ever known.
10008{_}3402{_}I had hit out with the rest when it had been a question of defence, but from this I turned aside in a sick loathing.
10008{_}3403{_}The men seemed possessed of devils, and of their unnatural energy.
10008{_}3404{_}Perdosa cast aside the club and took to his natural weapon, the knife.
10008{_}3405{_}I can see him yet rolling over and over embracing a big cow, his head jammed in an ecstasy of ferocity between the animal's front flippers, his legs clasped to hold her body, only his right arm rising and falling as he plunged his knife again and again.
10008{_}3406{_}She struggled, turning him over and under, wept great tears, and fairly whined with terror and pain.
10008{_}3407{_}Finally she was still, and Perdosa staggered to his feet, only to stare about him drunkenly for a moment before throwing himself with a screech on another victim.
10008{_}3408{_}The Nigger alone did not jump into the turmoil.
10008{_}3409{_}He stood just down the cave, his club ready.
10008{_}3410{_}Occasionally a disorganised rush to escape would be made.
10008{_}3411{_}The Nigger's lips snarled, and with a truly mad enjoyment he beat the poor animals back.
10008{_}3412{_}I pressed against the wall horrified, fascinated, unable either to interfere or to leave.
10008{_}3413{_}A close, sticky smell took possession of the air.
10008{_}3414{_}After a little a tiny stream, growing each moment, began to flow past my feet.
10008{_}3415{_}It sought its channel daintily, as streamlets do, feeling among the stones in eddies, quiet pools, miniature falls, and rapids.
10008{_}3416{_}For the moment I did not realise what it could be.
10008{_}3417{_}Then the light caught it down where the Nigger waited, and I saw it was red.
10008{_}3418{_}At first the racket of the seals was overpowering.
10008{_}3419{_}Now, gradually, it was losing volume.
10008{_}3420{_}I began to hear the blasphemies, ferocious cries, screams of anger hurled against the cave walls by the men.
10008{_}3421{_}The thick, sticky smell grew stronger; the light seemed to grow dimmer, as though it could not burn in that fetid air.
10008{_}3422{_}A seal came and looked up at me, big tears rolling from her eyes; then she flippered aimlessly away, out of her poor wits with terror.
10008{_}3423{_}The sight finished me.
10008{_}3424{_}I staggered down the length of the black tunnel to the boat.
10008{_}3425{_}After a long interval a little three months' pup waddled down to the water's edge, caught sight of me, and with a squeal of fright dived far.
10008{_}3426{_}Poor little devil!
10008{_}3427{_}I would not have hurt him for worlds.
10008{_}3428{_}As far as I know this was the only survivor of all that herd.
10008{_}3429{_}The men soon appeared, one by one, tired, sleepy-eyed, glutted, walking in a cat-like trance of satiety.
10008{_}3430{_}They were blood and tatters from head to foot, and from drying red masks peered their bloodshot eyes.
10008{_}3431{_}Not a word said they, but tumbled into the boat, pushed off, and in a moment we were floating in the full sunshine again.
10008{_}3432{_}We rowed home in an abstraction.
10008{_}3433{_}For the moment Berserker rage had burned itself out.
10008{_}3434{_}Handy Solomon continually wetted his lips, like an animal licking its chops.
10008{_}3435{_}Thrackles stared into space through eyes drugged with killing.
10008{_}3436{_}No one spoke.
10008{_}3437{_}We landed in the cove, and were surprised to find it in shadow.
10008{_}3438{_}The afternoon was far advanced.
10008{_}3439{_}Over the hill we dragged ourselves, and down to the spring.
10008{_}3440{_}There the men threw themselves flat and drank in great gulps until they could drink no more.
10008{_}3441{_}We built a fire, but the Nigger refused to cook.
10008{_}3442{_}"Someone else turn," he growled, "I cook aboard ship."
10008{_}3443{_}Perdosa, who had hewed the fuel, at once became angry.
10008{_}3444{_}"I cut heem de wood!"
10008{_}3445{_}he said, "I do my share; eef I cut heem de wood you mus' cook heem de grub!"
10008{_}3446{_}But the Nigger shook his head, and Perdosa went into an ecstasy of rage.
10008{_}3447{_}He kicked the fire to pieces; he scattered the unburned wood up and down the beach; he even threw some of it into the sea.
10008{_}3448{_}"Eef you no cook heem de grub, you no hab my wood!"
10008{_}3449{_}he shrieked, with enough oaths to sink his soul.
10008{_}3450{_}Finally Pulz interfered.
10008{_}3451{_}"Here you damn foreigners," said he, "quit it!
10008{_}3452{_}Let up, I say!
10008{_}3453{_}We got to eat.
10008{_}3454{_}You let that wood alone, or you'll pick it up again!"
10008{_}3455{_}Perdosa sprang at him with a screech.
10008{_}3456{_}Pulz was small but nimble, and understood rough and tumble fighting.
10008{_}3457{_}He met Perdosa's rush with two swift blows--a short arm jab and an upper-cut.
10008{_}3458{_}Then they clinched, and in a moment were rolling over and over just beyond the wash of the surf.
10008{_}3459{_}The row waked the Nigger from his sullen abstraction.
10008{_}3460{_}He seemed to come to himself with a start; his eye fell surprisedly on the combatants, then lit up with an unholy joy.
10008{_}3461{_}He drew his knife and crept down on the fighters.
10008{_}3462{_}It was too good an opportunity to pay off the Mexican.
10008{_}3463{_}But Thrackles interfered sharply.
10008{_}3464{_}"Come off!"
10008{_}3465{_}he commanded.
10008{_}3466{_}"None o' that!"
10008{_}3467{_}"Go to hell!"
10008{_}3468{_}growled the Nigger.
10008{_}3469{_}A great rage fell on them all, blind and terrible, like that leading to the slaughter of the seals.
10008{_}3470{_}They fought indiscriminately, hitting at each other with fists and knives.
10008{_}3471{_}It was difficult to tell who was against whom.
10008{_}3472{_}The sound of heavy breathing, dull blows, the tear of cloth; and grunts of punishment received; the swirl of the sand, the heave of struggling bodies, all riveted my attention, so that I did not see Captain Ezra Selover until he stood almost at my elbow.
10008{_}3473{_}"Stop!"
10008{_}3474{_}he shrieked in his high, falsetto voice.
10008{_}3475{_}And would you believe it, even through the blood haze of their combat the men heard him, and heeded.
10008{_}3476{_}They drew reluctantly apart, got to their feet, stood looking at him through reeking brows half submissive and half defiant.
10008{_}3477{_}The bull-headed Thrackles even took a half step forward, but froze in his tracks when Old Scrubs looked at him.
10008{_}3478{_}"I hire you men to fight when I tell you to, and only then," said the captain sternly.
10008{_}3479{_}"What does this mean?"
10008{_}3480{_}He menaced them one after another with his eyes, and one after another they quailed.
10008{_}3481{_}All their plottings, their threats, their dangerousness dissipated like mist before the command of this one resolute man.
10008{_}3482{_}These pirates who had seemed so dreadful to me, now were nothing more than cringing schoolboys before their master.
10008{_}3483{_}And then suddenly to my horror I, watching closely, saw the captain's eye turn blank.
10008{_}3484{_}I am sure the men must have felt the change, though certainly they were too far away to see it, for they shifted by ever so little from their first frozen attitude.
10008{_}3485{_}The captain's hand sought his pocket, and they froze again, but instead of the expected revolver, he produced a half-full brandy bottle.
10008{_}3486{_}The change in his eyes had crept into his features.
10008{_}3487{_}They had turned foolishly amiable, vacant, confiding.
10008{_}3488{_}"'llo boys," said he appealingly, "you good fellowsh, ain't you?
10008{_}3489{_}Have a drink.
10008{_}3490{_}'S good stuff.
10008{_}3491{_}Good ol' bottl'," he lurched, caught himself, and advanced toward them, still with the empty smile.
10008{_}3492{_}They stared at him for ten seconds, quite at a loss.
10008{_}3493{_}Then:  "By God, he's drunk!"
10008{_}3494{_}Handy Solomon breathed, scarcely louder than a whisper.
10008{_}3495{_}There was no other signal given.
10008{_}3496{_}They sprang as with a single impulse.
10008{_}3497{_}One instant I saw clear against the waning daylight the bulky, foolish-swaying form of Captain Selover: the next it had disappeared, carried down and obliterated by the rush of attacking bodies.
10008{_}3498{_}Knives gleamed ruddy in the sunset.
10008{_}3499{_}There was no struggle.
10008{_}3500{_}I heard a deep groan.
10008{_}3501{_}Then the murderers rose slowly to their feet.
10008{_}3502{_}XIII  I MAKE MY ESCAPE   I had plenty of time to run away.
10008{_}3503{_}I do not know why I did not do so; but the fact stands that I remained where I was until they had finished Captain Selover.
10008{_}3504{_}Then I took to my heels, but was soon cornered.
10008{_}3505{_}I drew my revolver, remembered that I had emptied it in the seal cave--and had time for no more coherent mental processes.
10008{_}3506{_}A smothering weight flung itself on me, against which I struggled as hard as I could, shrinking in anticipation from the thirsty plunge of the knives.
10008{_}3507{_}However, though the weight increased until further struggle was impossible, I was not harmed, and in a few moments found myself, wrists and ankles tied, beside a roaring fire.
10008{_}3508{_}While I collected myself I heard the grate of a boat being shoved off from the cove, and a few moments later made out lights aboard the _Laughing Lass_.
10008{_}3509{_}The looting party returned very shortly.
10008{_}3510{_}Their plundering had gone only as far as liquor and arms.
10008{_}3511{_}Thrackles let down from the cliff top a keg at the end of a line.
10008{_}3512{_}Perdosa and the Nigger each carried an armful of the 30-40 rifles.
10008{_}3513{_}The keg was rolled to the fire and broached.
10008{_}3514{_}The men got drunk, wildly drunk, but not helplessly so.
10008{_}3515{_}A flame communicated itself to them through the liquor.
10008{_}3516{_}The ordinary characteristics of their composition sprung into sharper relief.
10008{_}3517{_}The Nigger became more sullen; Perdosa more snake-like; Pulz more viciously evil; Thrackles more brutal; while Handy Solomon staggering from his seat to the open keg and back again, roaring fragments of a chanty, his red headgear contrasting with his smoky black hair and his swarthy hook-nosed countenance--he needed no further touch.
10008{_}3518{_}Their evil passions were all awake, and the plan, so long indefinite, developed like a photographer's plate.
10008{_}3519{_}"That's one," said Thrackles.
10008{_}3520{_}"One gone to hell."
10008{_}3521{_}"And now the diamonds," muttered Pulz.
10008{_}3522{_}"There's a ship upon the windward, a wreck upon the lee,       _Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e_,"  roared Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3523{_}"Damn it all, boys, it's the best night's work we ever did.
10008{_}3524{_}The stuff's ours.
10008{_}3525{_}Then it's me for a big stone house in Frisco O!"
10008{_}3526{_}"Frisco, hell," sneered Pulz, "that's all you know.
10008{_}3527{_}You ought to travel.
10008{_}3528{_}Paris for me and a little gal to learn the language from."
10008{_}3529{_}"I get heem a fine _caballo_, an' fine saddle, an' fine clo's," breathed Perdosa sentimentally.
10008{_}3530{_}"I ride, and the silver jingle, and the _senorita_ look----"  Thrackles was for a ship and the China trade.
10008{_}3531{_}"What you want, Doctor?"
10008{_}3532{_}they demanded of the silent Nigger.
10008{_}3533{_}But the Nigger only rolled his eyes and shook his head.
10008{_}3534{_}By and by he arose and disappeared in the dusk and was no more seen.
10008{_}3535{_}"Dam' fool," muttered Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3536{_}"Well, here's to crime!"
10008{_}3537{_}He drank a deep cup of the raw rum, and staggered back to his seat on the sands.
10008{_}3538{_}"'I am not a man-o'-war, nor a privateer,' said he.
10008{_}3539{_}_Blow high, blow low!
10008{_}3540{_}What care we_!
10008{_}3541{_}'But I am a jolly pirate and I'm sailing for my fee,'       _Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e_."
10008{_}3542{_}he sang.
10008{_}3543{_}"We'll land in Valparaiso and we'll go every man his way; and we'll sink the old _Laughing Lass_ so deep the mermaids can't find her."
10008{_}3544{_}Thrackles piled on more wood and the fire leaped high.
10008{_}3545{_}"Let's get after 'em,' said he.
10008{_}3546{_}"To-morrow's jes' 's good," muttered Pulz.
10008{_}3547{_}"Les' hav' 'nother drink."
10008{_}3548{_}"We'll stay here 'n see if our ol' frien' Percy don' show up," said Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3549{_}He threw back his head and roared forth a volume of sound toward the dim stars.
10008{_}3550{_}"Broadside to broadside the gallant ships did lay,       _Blow high, blow low!
10008{_}3551{_}What care we_?
10008{_}3552{_}'Til the jolly man-o'-war shot the pirate's mast away,       _Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e_."
10008{_}3553{_}I saw near me a live coal dislodged from the fire when Thrackles had thrown on the armful of wood.
10008{_}3554{_}An idea came to me.
10008{_}3555{_}I hitched myself to the spark, and laid across it the rope with which my wrists were tied.
10008{_}3556{_}This, behind my back, was not easy to accomplish, and twice I burned my wrists before I succeeded.
10008{_}3557{_}Fortunately I was at the edge of illumination, and behind the group.
10008{_}3558{_}I turned over on my side so that my back was toward the fire.
10008{_}3559{_}Then rapidly I cast loose my ankle lashings.
10008{_}3560{_}Thus I was free, and selecting a moment when universal attention was turned toward the rum barrel, I rolled over a sand dune, got to my hands and knees, and crept away.
10008{_}3561{_}Through the coarse grass I crept thus, to the very entrance of the arroyo, then rose to my feet.
10008{_}3562{_}In the middle distance the fire leaped red.
10008{_}3563{_}Its glow fell intermittently on the surges rolling in.
10008{_}3564{_}The men staggered or lay prone, either as gigantic silhouettes or as tatterdemalions painted by the light.
10008{_}3565{_}The keg stood solid and substantial, the hub about which reeled the orgy.
10008{_}3566{_}At the edge of the wash I could make out something prone, dim, limp, thrown constantly in new positions of weariness as the water ebbed and flowed beneath it, now an arm thrown out, now cast back, as though Old Scrubs slept feverishly.
10008{_}3567{_}The drunkards were getting noisy.
10008{_}3568{_}Handy Solomon still reeled off the verses of, his song.
10008{_}3569{_}The others joined in, frightfully off the key; or punctuated the performance by wild staccato yells.
10008{_}3570{_}"Their coffin was their ship and their grave it was the sea,       _Blow high, blow low!
10008{_}3571{_}What care we_?
10008{_}3572{_}And the quarter that we gave them was to sink them in the sea,       _Down on the coast of the high Barbare-e-e,_"  bellowed Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3573{_}I turned and plunged into the cool darkness of the canon.
10008{_}3574{_}XIV  AN ADVENTURE IN THE NIGHT   Ten seconds after entering the arroyo I was stumbling along in an absolute blackness.
10008{_}3575{_}It almost seemed to me that I could reach out my hands and touch it, as one would touch a wall.
10008{_}3576{_}Or perhaps not exactly that, for a wall is hard, and this darkness was soft and yielding, in the manner of enveloping hangings.
10008{_}3577{_}Directly above me was a narrow, jagged, and irregular strip of sky with stars.
10008{_}3578{_}I splashed in the brook, finding its waters strangely warm, rustled through the grasses, my head back, chin out, hands extended as one makes his way through a house at night.
10008{_}3579{_}There were no sounds except the tinkle of the sulphurous stream: successive bends in the canon wall had shut off even the faintest echoes of the bacchanalia on the beach.
10008{_}3580{_}The way seemed much longer than by daylight.
10008{_}3581{_}Already in my calculation I had traversed many times the distance, when, with a jump at the heart, I made out a glow ahead, and in front of it the upright logs of the stockade.
10008{_}3582{_}To my surprise the gate was open.
10008{_}3583{_}I ascended the gentle slope to the valley's level--and stumbled over a man lying prostrate, shivering violently, and moaning.
10008{_}3584{_}I bent over to discover whom it might be.
10008{_}3585{_}As I did so a brilliant light seemed to fill the valley, throwing an illumination on the man at my feet.
10008{_}3586{_}I saw it was the Nigger, and perceived at the same instant that he was almost beside himself with terror.
10008{_}3587{_}His eyes rolled, his teeth chattered, his frame contracted in a strong convulsion, and the black of his complexion had faded to a washed-out dirty grey, revolting to contemplate.
10008{_}3588{_}He felt my touch and sprang to his feet, clutching me by the shoulder as a man clutching rescue.
10008{_}3589{_}"My Gawd!"
10008{_}3590{_}he shivered.
10008{_}3591{_}"Look!
10008{_}3592{_}Dar it is again!"
10008{_}3593{_}He fell to pattering in a tongue unknown to me--charms, spells, undoubtedly, to exorcise the devils that had hold of him.
10008{_}3594{_}I followed the direction of his gaze, and myself cried out.
10008{_}3595{_}The doctor's laboratory stood in plain sight between the two columns of steam blown straight upward through the stillness of the evening.
10008{_}3596{_}It seemed bursting with light.
10008{_}3597{_}Every little crack leaked it in generous streams, while the main illumination appeared fairly to bulge the walls outward.
10008{_}3598{_}This was in itself nothing extraordinary, and indicated only the activity of those within, but while I looked an irregular patch of incandescence suddenly splashed the cliff opposite.
10008{_}3599{_}For a single instant the very substance of the rock glowed white hot; then from the spot a shower of spiteful flakes shot as from a pyrotechnic, and the light was blotted out as suddenly as it came.
10008{_}3600{_}At the same moment it appeared at another point, exhibited the same phenomena, died, flashed out at still a third place, and so was repeated here and there with bewildering rapidity until the walls of the valley crackled and spat sparks.
10008{_}3601{_}Abruptly the darkness fell.
10008{_}3602{_}As abruptly it was broken again by a similar exhibition; only this time the fire was blue.
10008{_}3603{_}Blue was followed by purple, purple by red.
10008{_}3604{_}Then ensued the briefest possible pause, in which a figure moved across the bars of light escaping through the chinks of the laboratory, and then the whole valley blazed with patches of vari-coloured fire.
10008{_}3605{_}It was not a reflection: it was actual physical conflagration of the solid rock, in irregular areas.
10008{_}3606{_}Some of the fire shapes were most fantastic.
10008{_}3607{_}And with the unexpectedness of a bursting shell the surface of the ground before our feet crackled into a ghastly blue flame.
10008{_}3608{_}The Nigger uttered a cry in his throat and disappeared.
10008{_}3609{_}I felt a sharp breath on my neck, an ejaculation of surprise at my very ear.
10008{_}3610{_}It was startling enough to scare the soul out of a man, but I held fast and was just about to step forward, when my collar was twisted tight from behind.
10008{_}3611{_}I raised both hands, felt steel, and knew that I was in the grasp of Handy Solomon's claw.
10008{_}3612{_}The sailor had me foul.
10008{_}3613{_}I did my best to twist around, to unbutton the collar, but in vain.
10008{_}3614{_}I felt my wind leaving me, the ghastly blue light was shot with red.
10008{_}3615{_}Distinctly I heard the man's sharp intaken breath as some new phenomenon met his eye, and his great oath as he swore.
10008{_}3616{_}"By the mother of God!"
10008{_}3617{_}he cried, "it's the devil."
10008{_}3618{_}Then I was jerked off my feet, and the next I knew I was lying on my back, very wet, on the beach; the day was breaking, and the men, quite sober, were talking vehemently.
10008{_}3619{_}It was impossible to make out what they said, but as Handy Solomon and the Nigger were the centre of discussion, I could imagine the subject.
10008{_}3620{_}I felt very stiff and sore and hazy in my mind.
10008{_}3621{_}My neck was lame from the dragging and my tongue dry from the choking.
10008{_}3622{_}For some time I lay in a half-torpor watching the lilac of dawn change to the rose of sunrise, utterly indifferent to everything.
10008{_}3623{_}They had thrown me down across the first rise of the little sand dunes back of the tide sands, and from it I could at once look out over the sea full of the restless shadows of dawn, and the land narrowing to the mouth of the arroyo.
10008{_}3624{_}I remember wondering whether Captain Selover were up yet.
10008{_}3625{_}Then with a sharp stab at the heart I remembered.
10008{_}3626{_}The thought was like a dash of cold water in clearing my faculties.
10008{_}3627{_}I raised my head.
10008{_}3628{_}Seaward a white gull had caught the first rays of the sun beyond the cliffs.
10008{_}3629{_}Landward--I saw with a choke in my throat--a figure emerging from the arroyo.
10008{_}3630{_}At the sight I made a desperate attempt to move, but with the effort discovered that I was again bound.
10008{_}3631{_}My stirring thus called Pulz's attention.
10008{_}3632{_}Before I could look away he had followed the direction of my gaze.
10008{_}3633{_}The discussion instantly ceased.
10008{_}3634{_}They waited in grim silence.
10008{_}3635{_}I did not know what to do.
10008{_}3636{_}Percy Darrow, carrying some sort of large book, was walking rapidly toward us.
10008{_}3637{_}Perdosa had disappeared.
10008{_}3638{_}Thrackles after an instant came and sat beside me and clapped his big hand over my mouth.
10008{_}3639{_}It was horrible.
10008{_}3640{_}When within a hundred paces or so, I could see that Darrow laboured under some great excitement.
10008{_}3641{_}His usual indifferent saunter had, as I have indicated, given way to a firm and decided step; his ironical eye glistened; his sallow cheek glowed.
10008{_}3642{_}"Boys," he shouted cheerfully.
10008{_}3643{_}"The time's up.
10008{_}3644{_}We've succeeded.
10008{_}3645{_}We'll sail just as soon as the Lord'll let us get ready.
10008{_}3646{_}Rustle the stuff aboard.
10008{_}3647{_}The doctor'll be down in a short time, and we ought to be loaded by night."
10008{_}3648{_}Handy Solomon and Pulz laid hand on two of the rifles near by and began surreptitiously to fill their magazines.
10008{_}3649{_}The Nigger shook his knife free of the scabbard and sat with it in his left hand, concealed by his body.
10008{_}3650{_}I could feel Thrackles's muscles stiffen.
10008{_}3651{_}Another fifty paces and it would be no longer necessary to stop my mouth.
10008{_}3652{_}The thought made me desperate.
10008{_}3653{_}I had failed as a leader of these men, and I had been forced to stand by at debauching, cruel, and murderous affairs, but now it is over I thank Heaven the reproach cannot be made against me that at any time I counted the consequences to myself.
10008{_}3654{_}Thrackles's hand lay heavy across my mouth.
10008{_}3655{_}I bit it to the bone, and as he involuntarily snatched it away, I rolled over toward the sea.
10008{_}3656{_}Thus for an instant I had my mouth free.
10008{_}3657{_}"Run!
10008{_}3658{_}Run!"
10008{_}3659{_}I shouted.
10008{_}3660{_}"For God's sake----"  Thrackles leaped upon me and struck me heavily upon the mouth, then sprang for a rifle.
10008{_}3661{_}I managed to struggle back to the dune, whence I could see.
10008{_}3662{_}XV  FIVE HUNDRED YARDS' RANGE   Percy Darrow, with the keenness that always characterised his mental apprehension, had understood enough of my strangled cry.
10008{_}3663{_}He had not hesitated nor delayed for an explanation, but had turned track and was now running as fast as his long legs would carry him back toward the opening of the ravine.
10008{_}3664{_}My companions stood watching him, but making no attempt either to shoot or to follow.
10008{_}3665{_}For a moment I could not understand this, then remembered the disappearance of Perdosa.
10008{_}3666{_}My heart jumped wildly, for the Mexican had been gone quite long enough to have cut off the assistant's escape.
10008{_}3667{_}I could not doubt that he would pick off his man at close range as soon as the fugitive should have reached the entrance to the arroyo.
10008{_}3668{_}There can be no question that he would have done so had not his Mexican impatience betrayed him.
10008{_}3669{_}He shot too soon.
10008{_}3670{_}Percy Darrow stopped in his tracks.
10008{_}3671{_}Although we heard the bullet sing by us, for an instant we thought he was hit.
10008{_}3672{_}Then Perdosa fired a second time, again without result.
10008{_}3673{_}Darrow turned sharp to the left and began desperately to scale the steep cliffs.
10008{_}3674{_}I once took part in a wild boar hunt on the coast of California.
10008{_}3675{_}Our dogs had penned a small band at the head of a narrow _barranca_, from which a single steep trail led over the hill.
10008{_}3676{_}We, perched on another hill some three or four hundred yards away, shot at the animals as they toiled up the trail.
10008{_}3677{_}The range was long, but we had time, for the severity of the climb forced the boars to a foot pace.
10008{_}3678{_}It was exactly like that.
10008{_}3679{_}Percy Darrow had two hundred feet of ascent to make.
10008{_}3680{_}He could go just so fast; must consume just so much time in his snail-like progress up the face of the hill.
10008{_}3681{_}During that time he furnished an excellent target, and the loose sandstone showed where each shot struck.
10008{_}3682{_}A significant indication was that the men did not take the trouble to get nearer, for which manoeuvre they would have had time in plenty, but distributed themselves leisurely for a shooting match.
10008{_}3683{_}"First shot," claimed Handy Solomon, and without delay fired off-hand.
10008{_}3684{_}A puff of dust showed to the right.
10008{_}3685{_}"Nerve no good," he commented, "jerked her just as I pulled."
10008{_}3686{_}Pulz fired from the knee.
10008{_}3687{_}The dust this time puffed below.
10008{_}3688{_}"Thought she'd carry up at that distance," he muttered.
10008{_}3689{_}The Nigger, too, missed, and Thrackles grinned triumphantly.
10008{_}3690{_}"I get a show," said he.
10008{_}3691{_}He spread his massive legs apart, drew a deep breath, and raised his weapon.
10008{_}3692{_}It lay in his grasp steady as a log, and I saw that Percy Darrow's fate was in the hands of that dangerous class of natural marksman that possesses no nerves.
10008{_}3693{_}But for the second time my teeth saved his life.
10008{_}3694{_}The trigger guard slipped against Thrackles's lacerated hand almost at the instant of discharge.
10008{_}3695{_}He missed; and the bullet went wide.
10008{_}3696{_}Darrow had climbed a matter of twenty feet.
10008{_}3697{_}Now the seamen distributed themselves for more leisurely and accurate marksmanship.
10008{_}3698{_}Handy Solomon lay flat on his stomach, resting the rifle muzzle across the top of a sand dune.
10008{_}3699{_}Pulz sat down, an elbow on either knee for the greater steadiness.
10008{_}3700{_}The Nigger knelt; but Thrackles remained on his feet.
10008{_}3701{_}No rest could be steadier than the stone-like rigidity of his thick arms.
10008{_}3702{_}The firing now became miscellaneous.
10008{_}3703{_}No one paid any attention to anyone else.
10008{_}3704{_}Each discovered what I could have told them, that even the human figure at five hundred yards is a small mark for a strange rifle.
10008{_}3705{_}The constant correction of elevation, however, brought the puffs of dust always closer, and I could not but realise that the doctrine of chances must bring home some of the bullets.
10008{_}3706{_}I soon discovered by way of comfort that only Thrackles and Handy Solomon really understood firearms; and of those two Thrackles alone had had much experience at long range.
10008{_}3707{_}He told me afterward he had hunted otter.
10008{_}3708{_}About halfway up the cliff Thrackles fired his fifth shot.
10008{_}3709{_}No dust followed the discharge; and I saw Percy Darrow stagger and almost lose his hold.
10008{_}3710{_}The men yelled savagely, but the assistant pulled himself together and continued his crawling.
10008{_}3711{_}The sun had been shining in our faces.
10008{_}3712{_}I could imagine its blurring effect on the sights.
10008{_}3713{_}Now abruptly it was blotted out, and a semi-twilight fell.
10008{_}3714{_}We all looked up, in spite of ourselves.
10008{_}3715{_}An opaque veil had been drawn quite across the heavens, through which we could not make out even the shape of the sun.
10008{_}3716{_}It was like a thunder cloud except that its under surface instead of being the usual grey-black was a deep earth-brown.
10008{_}3717{_}As we looked up, a deep bellow stirred the air, which had fallen quite still, long forks of lightning shot horizontally from the direction of the island's interior, and flashes of dull red were reflected from the canopy of cloud.
10008{_}3718{_}The men stared with their mouths open.
10008{_}3719{_}Undoubtedly the change had been some time in preparation, but all had been so absorbed in the affair of the doctor's assistant that no one had noticed.
10008{_}3720{_}It came to our consciousness with the suddenness of a theatrical change.
10008{_}3721{_}A dull roaring commenced, grew in volume, and then a great explosion shook the very ground under our feet.
10008{_}3722{_}We stared at each other, our faces whitening.
10008{_}3723{_}"What kind of hell has broke loose?"
10008{_}3724{_}muttered Pulz.
10008{_}3725{_}The Nigger fell flat on his face, uttering deep lamentations.
10008{_}3726{_}"Voodoo!
10008{_}3727{_}Voodoo!"
10008{_}3728{_}he groaned.
10008{_}3729{_}A gentle shower of white flakes began, powdering the surface of everything.
10008{_}3730{_}Far out to sea we could make out the sun on the water.
10008{_}3731{_}Gradually the roaring died down; the lightning ceased.
10008{_}3732{_}Comparative peace ensued.
10008{_}3733{_}We looked again toward the cliff.
10008{_}3734{_}Percy Darrow had not for one instant ceased to climb.
10008{_}3735{_}He was just topping the edge of the bluff.
10008{_}3736{_}Handy Solomon, with a cry of rage, seized another rifle and emptied the magazine at him as fast as the lever could be worked.
10008{_}3737{_}The dust flew wild in a half dozen places.
10008{_}3738{_}Darrow drew himself up to the sky line, raised his hat ironically, and disappeared.
10008{_}3739{_}[Illustration: The firing now became miscellaneous.
10008{_}3740{_}No one paid any attention to any one else.]
10008{_}3741{_}"Damn his soul!"
10008{_}3742{_}cried Handy Solomon, his face livid.
10008{_}3743{_}He threw his rifle to the beach and danced on it in an ecstasy of rage.
10008{_}3744{_}"What do we care," growled Thrackles, "he's no good to us.
10008{_}3745{_}W'at I want to know is, wat's up here, anyhow!"
10008{_}3746{_}"Didn't you never see a volcano go off, you swab?"
10008{_}3747{_}snapped Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3748{_}"Easy with your names, mate.
10008{_}3749{_}No, I never did.
10008{_}3750{_}We better get out."
10008{_}3751{_}"Without the chest?"
10008{_}3752{_}"S'pose we go up the gulch and get it, then," suggested Thrackles.
10008{_}3753{_}But at this Handy Solomon drew back in evident terror.
10008{_}3754{_}"Up that hole of hell?"
10008{_}3755{_}he objected.
10008{_}3756{_}"Not I.
10008{_}3757{_}You an' Pulz go."
10008{_}3758{_}They wrangled over it, Pulz joining.
10008{_}3759{_}Perdosa, shaken to the soul, crept in, and made a bee-line for the rum barrel.
10008{_}3760{_}He and the Nigger were frankly scared.
10008{_}3761{_}They had the nervous jumps at every little noise or unexpected movement; and even the natural explanation of these phenomena gave them very little reassurance.
10008{_}3762{_}I knew that Darrow would hurry as fast as he could back to the valley by way of the upper hills; I knew that he had there several sporting rifles; and I hoped greatly that he and Dr. Schermerhorn might accomplish something before the men had recovered their wits to the point of foreseeing his probable attack.
10008{_}3763{_}The uncanny cloud in the heavens, the weird half-light, and the explosions, which now grew more frequent, had their strong effect in spite of explanation.
10008{_}3764{_}The men were not really afraid to venture in quest of the supposed treasure; but they were in a frame of mind that dreaded the first plunge.
10008{_}3765{_}And time was going by.
10008{_}3766{_}But the fates were against us, as always in this ill-starred voyage.
10008{_}3767{_}I, watching from my sand dune, saw a second figure emerge from the arroyo's mouth.
10008{_}3768{_}It appeared to stagger as though hurt; and every eight or ten paces it stopped and rested in a bent-over position.
10008{_}3769{_}The murky light was too dim for me to make out details; but after a moment a rift in the veil enabled me to identify Dr. Schermerhorn carrying, with great difficulty, the chest.
10008{_}3770{_}XVI  THE MURDER   I took no chances, but began at once to shout, as soon as I saw the men had noticed his coming.
10008{_}3771{_}It was impossible for me to tell whether or not Dr. Schermerhorn heard me.
10008{_}3772{_}If he did, he misunderstood my intention, for he continued painfully to advance.
10008{_}3773{_}The only result I gained was to get myself well gagged with my own pocket handkerchief, and thrown in a hollow between the dunes.
10008{_}3774{_}Thence I could hear Handy Solomon speaking fiercely and rapidly.
10008{_}3775{_}"Now you let me run this," he commanded; "we got to find out somethin'.
10008{_}3776{_}It ain't no good to us without we knows--and we want to find out how he's got the rest hid."
10008{_}3777{_}They assented.
10008{_}3778{_}"I'm goin' out to help him carry her in," announced the seaman.
10008{_}3779{_}A long pause ensued, in which I watched the deep canopy of red-black thicken overhead.
10008{_}3780{_}A strange and unearthly light had fallen on the world, and the air was quite still.
10008{_}3781{_}After a while I heard Handy Solomon and Dr. Schermerhorn join the group.
10008{_}3782{_}"There you are, Perfessor," cried Handy Solomon, in tones of the greatest heartiness, "I'll put her right there, and she'll be as safe as a babby at home.
10008{_}3783{_}She's heavy, though."
10008{_}3784{_}Dr. Schermerhorn laughed a pleased and excited laugh.
10008{_}3785{_}I could tell by the tone of his voice that he was strung high, and guessed that his triumph needed an audience.
10008{_}3786{_}"You may say so well!"
10008{_}3787{_}he said.
10008{_}3788{_}"It iss heafy; and it iss heafy with the world-desire, the great substance than can do efferything.
10008{_}3789{_}Where iss Percy?"
10008{_}3790{_}"He's gone aboard."
10008{_}3791{_}"We must embark.
10008{_}3792{_}The time is joost right.
10008{_}3793{_}A day sooner and the egsperiment would haf been spoilt; but now"--he laughed--"let the island sink, we do not care.
10008{_}3794{_}We must embark hastily."
10008{_}3795{_}"It'll take a man long time to carry down all your things, Perfessor."
10008{_}3796{_}"Oh, led them go!
10008{_}3797{_}The eruption has alretty swallowed them oop.
10008{_}3798{_}The lava iss by now a foot deep in the valley.
10008{_}3799{_}Before long it flows here, so we must embark."
10008{_}3800{_}"But you've lost all them vallyable things, Perfessor," said Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3801{_}"Now, I call that hard luck."
10008{_}3802{_}Dr. Schermerhorn snapped his fingers.
10008{_}3803{_}"They do not amoundt to that!"
10008{_}3804{_}he cried.
10008{_}3805{_}"Here, here, in this leetle box iss all the treasure!
10008{_}3806{_}Here iss the labour of ten years!
10008{_}3807{_}Here iss the _Laughing Lass_, and the crew, and all the equipmendt comprised.
10008{_}3808{_}Here iss the world!"
10008{_}3809{_}"I'm a plain seaman, Perfessor, and I suppose I got to believe you; but she's a main small box for all that."
10008{_}3810{_}"With that small box you can haf all your wishes," asserted the Professor, still in the German lyric strain over his triumph.
10008{_}3811{_}"It iss the box of enchantments.
10008{_}3812{_}You haf but to will the change you would haf taig place--it iss done.
10008{_}3813{_}The substance of the rocks, the molecule--all!"
10008{_}3814{_}"Could a man make diamonds?"
10008{_}3815{_}asked Pulz abruptly.
10008{_}3816{_}I could hear the sharp intake of the men's breathing as they hung on the reply.
10008{_}3817{_}"Much more wonderful changes than that it can accomplish," replied the doctor, with an indulgent laugh.
10008{_}3818{_}"That change iss simple.
10008{_}3819{_}Carbon iss coal; carbon iss diamond.
10008{_}3820{_}You see?
10008{_}3821{_}One has but to change the form, not the substance."
10008{_}3822{_}"Then it'll change coal to diamonds?"
10008{_}3823{_}asked Handy Solomon.
10008{_}3824{_}"Yes, you gather my meanings--"  I heard a sharp squeak like a terrified mouse.
10008{_}3825{_}Then a long, dreadful silence; then two dull, heavy blows, spaced with deliberation.
10008{_}3826{_}A moment later I caught a glimpse of Handy Solomon bent forward to the labour of dragging a body toward the sea, his steel claw hooked under the angle of the jaw as a man handles a fish.
10008{_}3827{_}Pulz came and threw off my bonds and gag.
10008{_}3828{_}"Come along!"
10008{_}3829{_}said he.
10008{_}3830{_}All kept looking fearfully toward the arroyo.
10008{_}3831{_}A dense white steam marked its course.
10008{_}3832{_}The air was now heavy with portent.
10008{_}3833{_}Successive explosions, some light, some severe, shook the foundations of the island.
10008{_}3834{_}Great rocks and boulders bounded down the hills.
10008{_}3835{_}The flashes of lightning had become more frequent.
10008{_}3836{_}We moved, exaggerated to each other's vision by the strange light, uncouth and gigantic.
10008{_}3837{_}"Let's get out of this!"
10008{_}3838{_}cried Thrackles.
10008{_}3839{_}We turned at the word and ran, Thrackles staggering under the weight of the chest.
10008{_}3840{_}All our belongings we abandoned, and set out for the _Laughing Lass_ with only the tatters in which we stood.
10008{_}3841{_}Luckily for us a great part of the ship's stores had been returned to her hold after the last thorough scrubbing, so we were in subsistence, but all our clothes, all our personal belongings, were left behind us on the beach.
10008{_}3842{_}For after once we had topped the cliff that led over to the cove, I doubt if any consideration on earth would have induced us to return to that accursed place.
10008{_}3843{_}The row out to the ship was wet and dangerous.
10008{_}3844{_}Seismic disturbances were undoubtedly responsible for high pyramidic waves that lifted and fell without onward movement.
10008{_}3845{_}We fairly tumbled up out of the dory, which we did not hoist on deck, but left at the end of the painter to beat her sides against the ship.
10008{_}3846{_}XVII  THE OPEN SEA   Our haste, however, availed us little, for there was no wind at all.
10008{_}3847{_}We lay for over two hours under the weird light, over-canopied by the red- brown cloud, while the explosions shook the foundations of the world.
10008{_}3848{_}Nobody ventured below.
10008{_}3849{_}The sails flapped idly from the masts: the blocks and spars creaked: the three-cornered waves rose straight up and fell again as though reaching from the deep.
10008{_}3850{_}When the men first began to sweat the sails up, evidently in preparation for an immediate departure, I objected vehemently.
10008{_}3851{_}"You aren't going to leave him on the island," I cried.
10008{_}3852{_}"He'll die of starvation."
10008{_}3853{_}They did not answer me; but after a little more, when my expostulations had become more positive, Handy Solomon dropped the halliard, and drew me to one side.
10008{_}3854{_}"Look here, you," he snarled, "you'd better just stow your gab.
10008{_}3855{_}You're lucky to be here yourself, let alone botherin' your thick head about anybody else, and you can kiss the Book on that!
10008{_}3856{_}Do you know why you ain't with them carrion?"
10008{_}3857{_}He jerked his thumb toward the beach.
10008{_}3858{_}"It's because Solomon Anderson's your friend.
10008{_}3859{_}Thrackles would have killed you in a minute 'count of his bit hand.
10008{_}3860{_}I got you your chance.
10008{_}3861{_}Now don't you be a fool, for I ain't goin' to stand between you and them another time.
10008{_}3862{_}Besides, he won't last long if that volcano keeps at it."
10008{_}3863{_}He left me.
10008{_}3864{_}Whatever truth lay in his assumption of friendship, and I doubted there existed much of either truth or friendship in him, I saw the common sense of his advice.
10008{_}3865{_}I was in no position to dictate a course of action.
10008{_}3866{_}After the sails were on her we gathered at the starboard rail to watch the shore.
10008{_}3867{_}There the hills ran into inky blackness, as the horizon sometimes merges into a thunder squall.
10008{_}3868{_}A dense white steam came from the creek bed within the arroyo.
10008{_}3869{_}The surges beat on the shore louder than the ordinary, and the foam, even in these day hours, seemed to throw up a faint phosphorescence.
10008{_}3870{_}Frequent earthquakes oscillated the landscape.
10008{_}3871{_}We watched, I do not know for what, our eyes straining into the murk of the island.
10008{_}3872{_}Nobody thought of the chest, which lay on the cabin table aft.
10008{_}3873{_}I contributed maliciously my bit to their fear.
10008{_}3874{_}"These volcanic islands sometimes sink entirely," I suggested, "and in that case we'd be carried down by the suction."
10008{_}3875{_}It was intended merely to increase their uneasiness, but, strangely enough, after a few moments it ended by imposing itself on my own fears.
10008{_}3876{_}I began to be afraid the island would sink, began to watch for it, began to share the fascinated terror of these men.
10008{_}3877{_}The suspense after a time became unbearable, for while the portent-- whether physical or moral we were too far under its influence to distinguish--grew momentarily, our own souls did not expand in due correspondence.
10008{_}3878{_}We talked of towing, of kedging out, of going to any extreme, even to small boats.
10008{_}3879{_}Then just as we were about to move toward some accomplishment, a new phenomenon chained our attention to the shore.
10008{_}3880{_}In the mouth of the arroyo appeared a red glow.
10008{_}3881{_}A moment later a wave of lava, white-hot, red, iridescent, cooling to a black crust cracked in incandescence, rolled majestically out over the grassy plain.
10008{_}3882{_}Each instant it grew in volume, until the ravine must have been flowing half full.
10008{_}3883{_}Before its scorching the grasses even at the edge of the sea were smoking, and our camp had already burst into flames.
10008{_}3884{_}We had to shield our faces against the heat, and the wooden railing under our hands was growing warm.
10008{_}3885{_}Pulz turned an ashy countenance toward us.
10008{_}3886{_}"My God," he screamed.
10008{_}3887{_}"What's going to happen when she hits the sea?"
10008{_}3888{_}She hit the sea, and immediately a great cloud of steam arose, and the hissing as of a thousand serpents.
10008{_}3889{_}We felt the strong suction under our keel, and staggered under the jerk of the ship's cable as she swung toward the beach.
10008{_}3890{_}The paint was beginning to crackle along the rail.
10008{_}3891{_}We could see nothing for the scalding white veil that enveloped us; we could hear nothing for the roar of steam, the bombardment of explosions, and the crash of thunder; but our nostrils were assaulted by a most unearthly medley of smells.
10008{_}3892{_}"Hell's loose," growled Thrackles.
10008{_}3893{_}We were clinging hard as the ship reeled.
10008{_}3894{_}Huge surges were racing in from seaward, growing larger with each successive billow.
10008{_}3895{_}Handy Solomon raised his head, listened intently, and struck his forehead.
10008{_}3896{_}"Wind," he screamed at the top of his voice, and jumped for the halliards.
10008{_}3897{_}Thrackles followed him, but no one else moved.
10008{_}3898{_}In an instant the two were back, striking and kicking savagely, rousing their companions to the danger.
10008{_}3899{_}We all laid into the canvas like mad, and in no time had snugged down to a staysail and the peak of our mainsail.
10008{_}3900{_}Thrackles drew his knife and jumped for the cable, while Handy Solomon, his eyes snapping, seized the wheel.
10008{_}3901{_}We finished just in time.
10008{_}3902{_}I was turning away after tying the last gasket on the foresail, when the deck up-ended and tipped me headforemost into the starboard scupper.
10008{_}3903{_}At the same time a smother of salt water blew over the port rail, now far above me, to drench me as thoroughly as though I had fallen overboard.
10008{_}3904{_}I brushed out my eyes to find the ship smack on her beam ends, and the wind howling by from the sea.
10008{_}3905{_}I had company enough in the scuppers.
10008{_}3906{_}Only Handy Solomon clung desperately to the wheel, jamming his weight to port in the hope she might pay up: Thrackles, too, his eye squinted along some bearing of his own, was waiting for her to drag.
10008{_}3907{_}Presently it became evident that she was doing so, whereupon he drew his knife across our hawser.
10008{_}3908{_}"My God," chattered Pulz at my ear.
10008{_}3909{_}"If we go ashore--"  He did not need to finish.
10008{_}3910{_}Unless the _Laughing Lass_ could recover before the squall had driven her to leeward a scant half mile, we should be cooked alive in the boiling cauldron at the shore's edge.
10008{_}3911{_}For an interminable time, as it seemed to me, we lay absolutely motionless.
10008{_}3912{_}The scene is stamped indelibly on my memory--the bulwarks high above me, the steep, sleek deck, the piratical figure tense at the wheel, the snarling water racing from beneath us, the lurid glow to landward crawling up on us inch by inch like a hungry wild beast.
10008{_}3913{_}Then almost imperceptibly the brave schooner righted.
10008{_}3914{_}The strained lines on Handy Solomon's carven features relaxed little by little.
10008{_}3915{_}Thrackles, staring over the side, let out a mighty roar.
10008{_}3916{_}"Steerage way," he shouted, and executed an awkward clog dance on the reeling deck.
10008{_}3917{_}She moved forward, there was no doubt of that, for gradually we were eating toward the wind--but we made considerable leeway as well.
10008{_}3918{_}Handy Solomon, taut as the weather rigging, took his little advantages one by one like precious gifts.
10008{_}3919{_}Light there was none; the land was blotted out by the steam and murk which had crept to sea and now was hurled back by the wind.
10008{_}3920{_}All we could do was to hang there, tasting the copper of excitement, waiting for these different forces to adjust themselves.
10008{_}3921{_}Inch by inch we crept forward: foot by foot we made leeway.
10008{_}3922{_}The intensest of the lava glow worked its way from directly abeam to the quarter.
10008{_}3923{_}By this we knew we must be nearly opposite the cove.
10008{_}3924{_}At once a new doubt sprang up in our minds.
10008{_}3925{_}A moment ago all the energy of our desires had gone up in the ambition to avoid being cast on the beach.
10008{_}3926{_}Now we saw that that was not enough.
10008{_}3927{_}It was necessary to squeeze around the point where lay the _Golden Horn_, in order to avoid the fate that had overtaken her.
10008{_}3928{_}Handy Solomon yelled something at us.
10008{_}3929{_}We could not hear, but our own knowledge told us what it must be, and with one accord we turned to on the foresail.
10008{_}3930{_}With the peak of it hoisted we moved a trifle faster, though the schooner lay over at a perilous angle.
10008{_}3931{_}A moment later the fogs parted to show us the cliffs looming startlingly near.
10008{_}3932{_}There were the donkey engine and the works we had constructed for wrecking--and there beside them, watching us reflectively, stood Percy Darrow.
10008{_}3933{_}For ten minutes we stared at him fascinated, during which time the ship laboured against the staggering winds, gained and lost in its buffeting with the great surges.
10008{_}3934{_}The breakers hurling themselves in wild abandon against the rocks sent their back-wash of tumbling peaks to our very bilges.
10008{_}3935{_}The few remains of the _Golden Horn_, alternately drenched and draining, seemed to picture to us our inevitable end.
10008{_}3936{_}I think we had all selected the same two points for our "bearings," a rock and a drop of the cliff bolder than the ordinary.
10008{_}3937{_}If the rock opened from the cliff to eastward, we were lost; if it remained stationary, we were at least holding our own; if it opened out to westward, we were saved.
