10008{_}5086{_}Past circumstances have rendered me--well--perhaps suspicious is not too strong a word."
10008{_}5087{_}They noticed that he held a revolver in his hand.
10008{_}5088{_}Captain Parkinson came forward a step.
10008{_}5089{_}The host half raised his weapon.
10008{_}5090{_}Then he dropped it abruptly.
10008{_}5091{_}"Navy men!"
10008{_}5092{_}he said, in an altered voice.
10008{_}5093{_}"I beg your pardon.
10008{_}5094{_}I could not see at first.
10008{_}5095{_}My name is Percy Darrow."
10008{_}5096{_}"I am Captain Parkinson of the United States cruiser _Wolverine_," said the commander.
10008{_}5097{_}"This is Mr. Barnett, Mr. Darrow.
10008{_}5098{_}Dr. Trendon, Mr.
10008{_}5099{_}Darrow."
10008{_}5100{_}They shook hands all around.
10008{_}5101{_}"Like some damned silly afternoon tea," Trendon said later, in retailing it to the mess.
10008{_}5102{_}A pause followed.
10008{_}5103{_}"Won't you step in, gentlemen?"
10008{_}5104{_}said Darrow, "May I offer you the makings of a cigarette?"
10008{_}5105{_}"Wouldn't you be robbing yourself?"
10008{_}5106{_}inquired the captain, with a twinkle.
10008{_}5107{_}"Oh, you found the diary, then," said Darrow easily.
10008{_}5108{_}"Rather silly of me to complain so.
10008{_}5109{_}But really, in conditions like these, tobacco becomes a serious problem."
10008{_}5110{_}"So one might imagine," said Trendon drily.
10008{_}5111{_}He looked closely at Darrow.
10008{_}5112{_}The man's eyes were light and dancing.
10008{_}5113{_}From the nostrils two livid lines ran diagonally.
10008{_}5114{_}Such lines one might make with a hard blue pencil pressed strongly into the flesh.
10008{_}5115{_}The surgeon moved a little nearer.
10008{_}5116{_}"Can you give me any news of my friend Thrackles?"
10008{_}5117{_}asked Darrow lightly.
10008{_}5118{_}"Or the esteemed Pulz?
10008{_}5119{_}Or the scholarly and urbane Robinson of Ethiopian extraction?"
10008{_}5120{_}"Dead," said the captain.
10008{_}5121{_}"Ah, a pity," said the other.
10008{_}5122{_}He put his hand to his forehead.
10008{_}5123{_}"I had thought it probable."
10008{_}5124{_}His face twitched.
10008{_}5125{_}"Dead?
10008{_}5126{_}Very good.
10008{_}5127{_}In fact ... really ... er ...
10008{_}5128{_}amusing."
10008{_}5129{_}He began to laugh, quite to himself.
10008{_}5130{_}It was not a pleasant laugh to hear.
10008{_}5131{_}Trendon caught and shook him by the shoulder.
10008{_}5132{_}"Drop it," he said.
10008{_}5133{_}Darrow seemed not to hear him.
10008{_}5134{_}"Dead, all dead!"
10008{_}5135{_}he repeated.
10008{_}5136{_}"And I've outlasted 'em!
10008{_}5137{_}God damn 'em, I've outlasted 'em!"
10008{_}5138{_}And his mirth broke forth in a strangely shocking spasm.
10008{_}5139{_}Trendon lifted a hand and struck him so powerfully between the shoulder blades that he all but plunged forward on his face.
10008{_}5140{_}"Quit it!"
10008{_}5141{_}he ordered again.
10008{_}5142{_}"Get hold of yourself!"
10008{_}5143{_}Darrow turned and gripped him.
10008{_}5144{_}The surgeon winced with the pain of his grasp.
10008{_}5145{_}"I can't," gasped the maroon, between paroxysms.
10008{_}5146{_}"I've been living in hell.
10008{_}5147{_}A black, shaking, shivering hell, for God knows how long.... What do you know?
10008{_}5148{_}Have you ever been buried alive?"
10008{_}5149{_}And again the agony of laughter shook him.
10008{_}5150{_}"This, then," muttered the doctor, and the hypodermic needle shot home.
10008{_}5151{_}During the return Darrow lay like a log in the bottom of the gig.
10008{_}5152{_}The opiate had done its work.
10008{_}5153{_}Consciousness was mercifully dead within him.
10008{_}5154{_}VII  THE SURVIVORS   Rest and good food quickly brought Percy Darrow back to his normal poise.
10008{_}5155{_}One inspection satisfied Dr. Trendon that all was well with him.
10008{_}5156{_}He asked to see the captain, and that gentleman came to Ives's room, which had been assigned to the rescued man.
10008{_}5157{_}"I hope you've been able to make yourself comfortable," said the commander, courteously.
10008{_}5158{_}"It would be strange indeed if I could not," returned Darrow, smiling.
10008{_}5159{_}"You forget that you have set a savage down in the midst of luxury."
10008{_}5160{_}"Make yourself free of Ives's things," invited Captain Parkinson.
10008{_}5161{_}"Poor fellow; he will not use them again, I fear."
10008{_}5162{_}"One of your men lost?"
10008{_}5163{_}asked Darrow.
10008{_}5164{_}"Ah, the young officer whose body I found on the beach, perhaps?"
10008{_}5165{_}"No; but we have to thank you for that burial," said the captain.
10008{_}5166{_}Darrow made a swift gesture.
10008{_}5167{_}"Oh, if thanks are going," he cried, and paused in hopelessness of adequate expression.
10008{_}5168{_}"This has been a bitter cruise for us," continued the captain.
10008{_}5169{_}He sighed and was silent for a moment.
10008{_}5170{_}"There is much to tell and to be told," he resumed.
10008{_}5171{_}"Much," agreed the other, gravely.
10008{_}5172{_}"You will want to see Slade first, I presume," said the captain.
10008{_}5173{_}"One of your officers whom I have not yet had the pleasure of meeting?"
10008{_}5174{_}The captain stared.
10008{_}5175{_}"Slade," he said.
10008{_}5176{_}"Ralph Slade."
10008{_}5177{_}"Apparently there's a missing link.
10008{_}5178{_}Or--I fear I was not wholly myself yesterday for a time.
10008{_}5179{_}Possibly something occurred that I did not quite take in."
10008{_}5180{_}"Perhaps we'd better wait," said Captain Parkinson, with obvious misgiving.
10008{_}5181{_}"You're not quite rested.
10008{_}5182{_}You will feel more like--"  "If you don't mind," said Darrow composedly, "I'd like to get at this thing now.
10008{_}5183{_}I'm in excellent understanding, I assure you."
10008{_}5184{_}"Very well.
10008{_}5185{_}I am speaking of the man who acted as mate in the _Laughing Lass_.
10008{_}5186{_}The journalist who--good heavens!
10008{_}5187{_}What arrant stupidity!
10008{_}5188{_}I have to beg your pardon, Mr. Darrow.
10008{_}5189{_}It has just occurred to me.
10008{_}5190{_}He called himself Eagen with you."
10008{_}5191{_}"Eagen!
10008{_}5192{_}What is this?
10008{_}5193{_}Is Eagen alive?"
10008{_}5194{_}"And on this ship.
10008{_}5195{_}We picked him up in an open boat."
10008{_}5196{_}"And you say he calls himself Slade?"
10008{_}5197{_}"He is Ralph Slade, adventurer and journalist.
10008{_}5198{_}Mr. Barnett knows him and vouches for him."
10008{_}5199{_}"And he was on our island under an assumed name," said Darrow in tones that had the smoothness and the rasp of silk.
10008{_}5200{_}"Rather annoying.
10008{_}5201{_}Not good form, quite, even for a pirate."
10008{_}5202{_}"Yet, I believe he saved your life," suggested the captain.
10008{_}5203{_}Darrow looked up sharply.
10008{_}5204{_}"Why, yes," he admitted.
10008{_}5205{_}"So he did.
10008{_}5206{_}I had hoped--" He checked himself.
10008{_}5207{_}"I had thought that all of the crew went the same way.
10008{_}5208{_}You didn't find any of the others?"
10008{_}5209{_}"None."
10008{_}5210{_}Darrow got to his feet.
10008{_}5211{_}"I think I'd like to see Eagen--Slade--whatever he calls himself."
10008{_}5212{_}"I don't know," began the captain.
10008{_}5213{_}"It might not be--" He hesitated and stopped.
10008{_}5214{_}Darrow drew back a little, misinterpreting the other's attitude.
10008{_}5215{_}"Do I understand that I am under restraint?"
10008{_}5216{_}he asked stiffly.
10008{_}5217{_}"Certainly not.
10008{_}5218{_}Why should you be?"
10008{_}5219{_}"Well," returned the other contemplatively, "it really might be regarded as a subject for investigation.
10008{_}5220{_}Of course I know only a small part of it.
10008{_}5221{_}But there have certainly been suspicious circumstances.
10008{_}5222{_}Piracy there has been: no doubt of that.
10008{_}5223{_}Murder, too, if my intuitions are not at fault.
10008{_}5224{_}Or at least, a disappearance to be accounted for.
10008{_}5225{_}Robbery can't be denied.
10008{_}5226{_}And there's a dead body or two to be properly accredited."
10008{_}5227{_}He looked the captain in the eye.
10008{_}5228{_}"Well?"
10008{_}5229{_}"You'll find my story highly unsatisfactory in detail, I fancy.
10008{_}5230{_}I merely want to know whether I'm to present it as a defence, or only an explanation."
10008{_}5231{_}"We shall be glad to hear your story when you are ready to tell it--after you have seen Mr.
10008{_}5232{_}Slade."
10008{_}5233{_}"Thank you," said Darrow simply.
10008{_}5234{_}"You have heard his?"
10008{_}5235{_}"Yes.
10008{_}5236{_}It needs filling in."
10008{_}5237{_}"When may I see him?"
10008{_}5238{_}"That's for Dr. Trendon to say.
10008{_}5239{_}He came to us almost dead.
10008{_}5240{_}I'll find out."
10008{_}5241{_}The surgeon reported Slade much better, but all a-quiver with excitement.
10008{_}5242{_}"Hate to put the strain on him," said he.
10008{_}5243{_}"But he'll be in a fever till he gets this thing off his mind.
10008{_}5244{_}Send Mr. Darrow to him."
10008{_}5245{_}After a moment's consideration Darrow said: "I should like to have you and Dr. Trendon present, Captain Parkinson, while I ask Eagen one or two questions."
10008{_}5246{_}"Understand one thing, Mr. Darrow," said Trendon briefly.
10008{_}5247{_}"This is not to be an inquisition."
10008{_}5248{_}"Ah," said Darrow, unmoved.
10008{_}5249{_}"I'm to be neither defendant nor prosecutor."
10008{_}5250{_}"You are to respect the condition of Dr. Trendon's patient, sir," said Captain Parkinson, with emphasis.
10008{_}5251{_}"Outside of that, your attitude toward a man who has twice thought of your life before his own is for you to determine."
10008{_}5252{_}No little cynicism lurked in Darrow's tones as he said:  "You have confidence in Mr. Slade, alias Eagen."
10008{_}5253{_}"Yes," replied Captain Parkinson, in a tone that closed that topic.
10008{_}5254{_}"Still, I should be glad to have you gentlemen present, if only for a moment," insisted Darrow, presently.
10008{_}5255{_}"Perhaps it would be as well--on account of the patient," said the surgeon significantly.
10008{_}5256{_}"Very well," assented the captain.
10008{_}5257{_}The three went to Slade's cabin.
10008{_}5258{_}He was lying propped up in his bunk.
10008{_}5259{_}Trendon entered first, followed by the captain, then Darrow.
10008{_}5260{_}"Here's your prize, Slade," said the surgeon.
10008{_}5261{_}Darrow halted, just inside the door.
10008{_}5262{_}With an eager light in his face Slade leaned forward and stretched out his hand.
10008{_}5263{_}"I couldn't believe it until I saw you, old man," he cried.
10008{_}5264{_}Darrow's eyebrows went up.
10008{_}5265{_}Before Slade had time to note that there was no response to his outstretched hand, the surgeon had jumped in and pushed him roughly back upon his pillow.
10008{_}5266{_}"What did you promise?"
10008{_}5267{_}he growled.
10008{_}5268{_}"You were to lie still, weren't you?
10008{_}5269{_}And you'll do it, or out we go."
10008{_}5270{_}"How are you, Eagen?"
10008{_}5271{_}drawled Darrow.
10008{_}5272{_}"Not Eagen.
10008{_}5273{_}I'm done with that.
10008{_}5274{_}They've told you, haven't they?"
10008{_}5275{_}Darrow nodded.
10008{_}5276{_}"Are you the only survivor?"
10008{_}5277{_}he inquired.
10008{_}5278{_}"Except yourself."
10008{_}5279{_}"The Nigger?
10008{_}5280{_}Pulz?
10008{_}5281{_}Thrackles?
10008{_}5282{_}The captain?
10008{_}5283{_}All drowned?"
10008{_}5284{_}"Not the captain.
10008{_}5285{_}They murdered him."
10008{_}5286{_}"Ah," said Darrow softly.
10008{_}5287{_}"And you--I beg your pardon--your--er--friends disposed of the doctor in the same way?"
10008{_}5288{_}"Handy Solomon," replied Slade with shaking lips.
10008{_}5289{_}"Hell's got that fiend, if there's a hell for human fiends.
10008{_}5290{_}They threw the doctor's body in the surf."
10008{_}5291{_}"You didn't notice whether there were any papers?"
10008{_}5292{_}"If there were they must have been destroyed with the body when the lava poured down the valley into the sea."
10008{_}5293{_}"The lava: of course," assented Darrow, with elaborate nonchalance.
10008{_}5294{_}"Well, he was a kind old boy.
10008{_}5295{_}A cheerful, simple, wise old child."
10008{_}5296{_}"I would have given my right hand to save him," cried Slade.
10008{_}5297{_}"It was so sudden--so damnable--"  "Better to have saved him than me," said Darrow.
10008{_}5298{_}He spoke with the first touch of feeling that he exhibited.
10008{_}5299{_}"I have to thank you for my life, Eagen--I beg your pardon: Slade.
10008{_}5300{_}It's hard to remember."
10008{_}5301{_}Dr. Trendon arose, and Captain Parkinson with him.
10008{_}5302{_}"Give you two hours, Mr. Darrow," said the surgeon.
10008{_}5303{_}"No more.
10008{_}5304{_}If he seems exhausted, give him one of these powders.
10008{_}5305{_}I'll look in in an hour."
10008{_}5306{_}At the end of an hour he returned.
10008{_}5307{_}Slade was lying back on his pillow.
10008{_}5308{_}Darrow was talking, eagerly, confidentially.
10008{_}5309{_}In another hour he came out.
10008{_}5310{_}"The whole thing is clear," he said to Captain Parkinson.
10008{_}5311{_}"I am ready to report to you."
10008{_}5312{_}"This evening," said the captain.
10008{_}5313{_}"The mess will want to hear."
10008{_}5314{_}"Yes, they will want to hear," assented Darrow.
10008{_}5315{_}"You've had Slade's story.
10008{_}5316{_}I'll take it up where he left off, and he'll check me.
10008{_}5317{_}Mine's as incredible as--as Slade's was.
10008{_}5318{_}And it's as true."
10008{_}5319{_}VIII  THE MAKER OF MARVELS   As they had gathered to hear Ralph Slade's tale, so now the depleted mess of the _Wolverine_ grouped themselves for Percy Darrow's sequel.
10008{_}5320{_}Slade himself sat directly across from the doctor's assistant.
10008{_}5321{_}Before him lay a paper covered with jotted notes.
10008{_}5322{_}Trendon slouched low in the chair on Slade's right.
10008{_}5323{_}Captain Parkinson had the other side.
10008{_}5324{_}Convenient to Darrow's hand lay the material for cigarettes.
10008{_}5325{_}As he talked he rolled cylinder after cylinder, and between sentences consumed them in long, satisfying puffs.
10008{_}5326{_}"First you will want to learn of the fate of your friends and shipmates," he began.
10008{_}5327{_}"They are dead.
10008{_}5328{_}One of them, Mr. Edwards, fell to my hands to bury, as you know.
10008{_}5329{_}He lies beside Handy Solomon.
10008{_}5330{_}The others we shall probably not see: any one of a score of ocean currents may have swept them far away.
10008{_}5331{_}The last great glow that you saw was the signal of their destruction.
10008{_}5332{_}So the work of a great scientist, a potent benefactor of the race, a gentle and kindly old heart, has brought about the death of your friends and of my enemies.
10008{_}5333{_}The innocent and the guilty ... the murderer with his plunder, the officer following his duty ... one and the same end ... a paltry thing our vaunted science is in the face of such tangled fates."
10008{_}5334{_}He spoke low and bitterly.
10008{_}5335{_}Then he squared his shoulders and his manner became businesslike.
10008{_}5336{_}"Interrupt me when any point needs clearing up," he said.
10008{_}5337{_}"It's a blind trail at best.
10008{_}5338{_}You've the right to see it as plain as I can make it--with Slade's help.
10008{_}5339{_}Cut right in with your questions: There'll be plenty to answer and some never will be answered....  "Now let me get this thing laid out clearly in my own mind.
10008{_}5340{_}You first saw the glow--let me see--"  "Night of June 2d," said Barnett.
10008{_}5341{_}"June 2d," agreed Darrow.
10008{_}5342{_}"That was the end of Solomon, Thrackles & Co. A very surprising end to them, if they had time to think," he added grimly.
10008{_}5343{_}"Surprising enough, from the survivor's viewpoint," said Slade.
10008{_}5344{_}"Doubtless.
10008{_}5345{_}They've had that story from you; I needn't go over it.
10008{_}5346{_}This ship picked up the _Laughing Lass_, deserted, and put your first crew aboard.
10008{_}5347{_}That night, was it not, you saw the second pillar of fire?"
10008{_}5348{_}Barnett nodded.
10008{_}5349{_}"So your men met their death.
10008{_}5350{_}Then came the second finding of the empty schooner.... Captain Parkinson, they must have been brave men who faced the unknown terrors of that prodigy."
10008{_}5351{_}"They volunteered, sir," said the Captain, with simple pride.
10008{_}5352{_}Darrow bowed with a suggestion of reverence in the slow movement of his head.
10008{_}5353{_}"And that night--or was it two nights later?--you saw the last appearance of the portent.
10008{_}5354{_}Well, I shall come to that.... Slade has told you how they lived on the beach.
10008{_}5355{_}With us in the valley it was different.
10008{_}5356{_}Almost from the first I was alone.
10008{_}5357{_}The doctor ceased to be a companion.
10008{_}5358{_}He ceased to be human, almost.
10008{_}5359{_}A machine, that's what he was.
10008{_}5360{_}His one human instinct was--well, distrust.
10008{_}5361{_}His whole force of being was centred on his discovery.
10008{_}5362{_}It was to make him the foremost scientist of the world; the foremost individual entity of his time--of all time, possibly.
10008{_}5363{_}Even to outline it to you would take too much time.
10008{_}5364{_}Light, heat, motive power in incredible degrees and under such control as has never been known: these were to be the agencies at his call.
10008{_}5365{_}The push of a button, the turn of a screw--oh, he was to be master of such power as no monarch ever wielded!
10008{_}5366{_}Riches--pshaw!
10008{_}5367{_}Riches were the least of it.
10008{_}5368{_}He could create them, practically.
10008{_}5369{_}But they would be superfluous.
10008{_}5370{_}Power: unlimited, absolute power was his goal.
10008{_}5371{_}With his end achieved he could establish an autocracy, a dynasty of science: whatever he chose.
10008{_}5372{_}Oh, it was a rich-hued, golden, glowing dream; a dream such as men's souls don't formulate in these stale days--not our kind of men.
10008{_}5373{_}The Teutonic mysticism--you understand.
10008{_}5374{_}And it was all true.
10008{_}5375{_}Oh, quite."
10008{_}5376{_}"Do you mean us to understand that he had this power you describe?"
10008{_}5377{_}asked Captain Parkinson.
10008{_}5378{_}"In his grasp.
10008{_}5379{_}Then comes a practical gentleman with a steel hook.
10008{_}5380{_}A follower of dreams, too, in his way.
10008{_}5381{_}Conflicting interests--you know how it is.
10008{_}5382{_}One well-aimed blow from the more practical dreamer, and the greater vision passes....
10008{_}5383{_}I'm getting ahead of myself.
10008{_}5384{_}Just a moment."
10008{_}5385{_}His cigarette glowed fiercely in the dimness before he took up his tale again.
10008{_}5386{_}"You all know who Dr. Schermerhorn was.
10008{_}5387{_}None of you know--I don't know myself, though I've been his factotum for ten years--along how many varied lines of activity that mind played.
10008{_}5388{_}One of them was the secret of energy: concentrated, resistless energy.
10008{_}5389{_}Man's contrivances were too puny for him.
10008{_}5390{_}The most powerful engines he regarded as toys.
10008{_}5391{_}For a time high explosives claimed his attention.
10008{_}5392{_}He wanted to harness them.
10008{_}5393{_}Once he got to the point of practical experiment.
10008{_}5394{_}You can see the ruins yet: a hole in southern New Jersey.
10008{_}5395{_}Nobody ever understood how he escaped.
10008{_}5396{_}But there he was on his feet across a ten-foot fence in a ploughed field--yes, he flew the fence-- and running, running furiously in the opposite direction, when the dust cleared away.
10008{_}5397{_}Someone stopped him finally.
10008{_}5398{_}Told him the danger was over.
10008{_}5399{_}'Yet, I will not return,' he said firmly, and fainted away.
10008{_}5400{_}That disgusted him with high explosives.
10008{_}5401{_}What secrets he discovered he gave to the government.
10008{_}5402{_}They were not without value, I believe."
10008{_}5403{_}"They were not, indeed," corroborated Barnett.
10008{_}5404{_}"Next his interest turned to the natural phenomena of high energy.
10008{_}5405{_}He studied lightning in an open steel network laboratory, with few results save a succession of rheumatic attacks, and an improved electric interrupter, since adopted by one of the great telegraph companies.
10008{_}5406{_}The former obliged him to stop these experiments, and the invention he considered trivial.
10008{_}5407{_}Probably the great problem of getting at the secret of energy led him into his attempts to study the mysterious electrical waves radiated by lightning flashes; at any rate he was soon as deep into the subject of electrical science as his countryman, Hertz, had ever been.
10008{_}5408{_}He used to tell me that he often wondered why he hadn't taken up this line before--the world of energy he now set out to explore, waves in that tremendous range between those we hear and those we see.
10008{_}5409{_}It was natural that he should then come to the most prominent radio-active elements, uranium, thorium, and radium.
10008{_}5410{_}But though his knowledge surpassed that of the much-exploited authorities, he was never satisfied with any of his results.
10008{_}5411{_}"'Pitchblende; no!'
10008{_}5412{_}he would exclaim.
10008{_}5413{_}'It has not the great power.
10008{_}5414{_}The mines are not deep enough, yet!'
10008{_}5415{_}"Then suddenly the great idea that was to bring him success, and cost him his life, came to him.
10008{_}5416{_}The bowels of the earth must hold the secret!
10008{_}5417{_}He took up volcanoes....
10008{_}5418{_}Does all this sound foolish?
10008{_}5419{_}It was not if you knew the man.
10008{_}5420{_}He was a mighty enthusiast, a born martyr.
10008{_}5421{_}Not cold-blooded, like the rest of us.
10008{_}5422{_}The fire was in his veins.... A light, please.
10008{_}5423{_}Thank you.
10008{_}5424{_}"We chased volcanoes.
10008{_}5425{_}There was a theory under it all.
10008{_}5426{_}He believed that volcanic emanations are caused by a mighty and uncomprehended energy, something that achieves results ascribable neither to explosions nor heat, some eternal, inner source.... Radium, if you choose, only he didn't call it that.
10008{_}5427{_}Radium itself, as known to our modern scientists, he regarded as the harmless plaything of people with time hanging heavy on their hands.
10008{_}5428{_}He wasn't after force in pin-point quantities: he wanted bulk results.
10008{_}5429{_}Yet I believe that, after all, what he sought was a sort of higher power of radium.
10008{_}5430{_}The phenomena were related.
10008{_}5431{_}And he had some of that concentrated essence of pitchblende in the chest when we started.
10008{_}5432{_}Oh, not much: say about twenty thousand dollars' worth.
10008{_}5433{_}Maybe thirty.
10008{_}5434{_}For use?
10008{_}5435{_}No; rather for comparison, I judge.
10008{_}5436{_}"Yes, we chased volcanoes.
10008{_}5437{_}I became used to camping between sample hells of all known varieties.
10008{_}5438{_}I got so that the fumes of a sulphur match seemed like a draught of pure, fresh air.
10008{_}5439{_}Wherever any of the earth's pimples showed signs of coming to a head, there were we, taking part in the trouble.
10008{_}5440{_}By and by the doctor got so thoroughly poisoned that he had to lay off.
10008{_}5441{_}Back to Philadelphia we came.
10008{_}5442{_}There an aged seafaring person, temporarily stranded, mulcted the Professor of a dollar--an undertaking that required no art--and in the course of his recital touched upon yonder little cesspool of infernal iniquities.
10008{_}5443{_}An uncharted volcanic island: one that he could have all for his own; you may guess whether Dr. Schermerhorn was interested.
10008{_}5444{_}"'That iss for which we haf so-long-in-vain sought, Percy,' he said to me in his quaint, link-chain style of speech.
10008{_}5445{_}'A leedle prifate volcano- laboratory to ourselves to have.
10008{_}5446{_}Totally unknown: undescribed, not-on-the- chart-to-be-found.
10008{_}5447{_}To-morrow we start.
10008{_}5448{_}I make a list of the things-to- get.'
10008{_}5449{_}"He began his list, as I remember, with three dozen undershirts, a gallon of pennyroyal for insect bites, a box of assorted fish hooks, thirty pounds of tea, and a case of carpet tacks.
10008{_}5450{_}When I hadn't anything else to worry over, I used to lie awake at night and speculate on the purpose of those carpet tacks.
10008{_}5451{_}He had something in mind: if there was anything on which he prided himself, it was his practical bent.
10008{_}5452{_}But the list never got any further: it ceased short of one page in the ledger, as you may have noticed.
10008{_}5453{_}I outfitted by telegraph on the way across the continent.
10008{_}5454{_}"The doctor didn't ask me whether I'd go.
10008{_}5455{_}He took it for granted.
10008{_}5456{_}That's probably why I didn't back out.
10008{_}5457{_}Nor did I tell him that the three life insurance companies which had foolishly and trustingly accepted me as a risk merely on the strength of a good constitution were making frantic efforts to compromise on the policies.
10008{_}5458{_}They felt hurt, those companies: my healthy condition had ceased to appeal to them.
10008{_}5459{_}What's a good constitution between earthquakes?
10008{_}5460{_}No, there was no use telling the doctor.
10008{_}5461{_}It would only have worried him.
10008{_}5462{_}Besides, I didn't believe that the island was there.
10008{_}5463{_}I thought it was a myth of that stranded ancient mariner's imagination.
10008{_}5464{_}When it rose to sight at the proper spot, none were more astounded than the bad risk who now addresses you.
10008{_}5465{_}"Yet, I must say for the island that it came handsomely up to specifications.
10008{_}5466{_}Down where you were, Slade.
10008{_}5467{_}you didn't get a real insight into its disposition.
10008{_}5468{_}But in back of us there was any kind of action for your money.
10008{_}5469{_}Geysers, hell-spouts, fuming fissures, cunning little craterlets with half-portions of molten lava ready to serve hot; more gases than you could create in all the world's chemical laboratories: in fact, everything to make the place a paradise for Old Nick--and Dr. Schermerhorn.
10008{_}5470{_}He brought along in his precious chest, besides the radium, some sort of raw material: also, as near as I could make out, a sort of cage or guardianship scheme for his concentrated essence of cussedness, when he should get it out of the volcano.
10008{_}5471{_}"In the first seven months he puttered around the little fumers, with an occasional excursion up to the main crater.
10008{_}5472{_}It was my duty to follow on and drag him away when he fell unconscious.
10008{_}5473{_}Sometimes I would try to get him before he was quite gone.
10008{_}5474{_}Then he would become indignant, and fight me.
10008{_}5475{_}Perhaps that helped to lose me his confidence.
10008{_}5476{_}More and more he withdrew into himself.
10008{_}5477{_}There were days when he spoke no word to me.
10008{_}5478{_}It was lonely.
10008{_}5479{_}Do you know why I used to visit you at the beach, Slade?
10008{_}5480{_}I suppose you thought I was keeping watch on you.
10008{_}5481{_}It wasn't that, it was loneliness.
10008{_}5482{_}In a way, it hurt me, too: for one couldn't help but be fond of the old boy; and at times it seemed as if he weren't quite himself.
10008{_}5483{_}Pardon me, if I may trouble you for the matches?
10008{_}5484{_}Thanks....  "Matters went very wrong at times: the doctor fumed like his little craters; growled out long-winded, exhaustive German imprecations: wouldn't even eat.
10008{_}5485{_}Then again the demon of work would drive him with thong and spur: he would rush to his craters, to his laboratories, to his ledger for the purpose of entering unintelligible commentaries.
10008{_}5486{_}He had some peculiar contrivance, like a misshapen retort, with which he collected gases from the craterlets.
10008{_}5487{_}Whenever I'd hear one of those smash, I knew it was a bad day.
10008{_}5488{_}"Meantime, the volcano also became--well, what you might call temperamental.
10008{_}5489{_}"It got to be a year and a quarter--a year and a half.
10008{_}5490{_}I wondered whether we should ever get away.
10008{_}5491{_}My tobacco was running short.
10008{_}5492{_}And the bearing of the men was becoming fidgetty.
10008{_}5493{_}My visits to the beach became quite interesting--to me.
10008{_}5494{_}One day the doctor came running out of his laboratory with so bright a face that I ventured to ask him about departure.
10008{_}5495{_}"'Not so long, now, Percy,' he said, in his old, kind manner.
10008{_}5496{_}'Not so long.
10008{_}5497{_}The first real success.
10008{_}5498{_}It iss made.
10008{_}5499{_}We have yet under-entire- control to bring it, but it iss made.'
10008{_}5500{_}"'And about time, sir,' said I.
10008{_}5501{_}'If we don't do something soon we may have trouble with the men.'
10008{_}5502{_}"'So?'
10008{_}5503{_}said he in surprise.
10008{_}5504{_}'But they could do nothing.
10008{_}5505{_}Nothing.'
10008{_}5506{_}He wagged his great head confidently.
10008{_}5507{_}'We are armed.'
10008{_}5508{_}"'Oh, yes, armed.
10008{_}5509{_}So are they.'
10008{_}5510{_}"'We are armed,' he repeated obstinately.
10008{_}5511{_}'Such as no man was ever armed, are we armed.'
10008{_}5512{_}"He checked himself abruptly and walked away.
10008{_}5513{_}Well, I've since wondered what would have happened had the men attacked us.
10008{_}5514{_}It would have been worth seeing, and--and surprising.
10008{_}5515{_}Yes: I'm quite certain it would have been surprising.
10008{_}5516{_}Perhaps, too, I might have learned more of the Great Secret ... and yet, I don't know.
10008{_}5517{_}It's all dark ... a hint here ... theory ... mere glints of light.... Where did I put.... Ah, thank you."
10008{_}5518{_}IX  THE ACHIEVEMENT   For some moments Darrow sat gazing fixedly at the table before him.
10008{_}5519{_}His cigarette tip glowed and failed.
10008{_}5520{_}Someone suggested drinks.
10008{_}5521{_}The captain asked Darrow what he would have, but the question went unnoted.
10008{_}5522{_}"How I passed the next six months I could hardly tell you," he began again, quite abruptly.
10008{_}5523{_}"At times I was bored--fearfully bored.
10008{_}5524{_}Yet the element of mystery, of uncertainty, of underlying peril, gave a certain zest to the affair.
10008{_}5525{_}In the periods of dulness I found some amusement in visiting the lower camp and baiting the Nigger.
10008{_}5526{_}Slade will have told you about him; he possessed quite a fund of bastard Voodooism: he possessed more before I got through with him.
10008{_}5527{_}Yes; if he had lived to return to his country, I fancy he would have added considerably to Afro-American witch- lore.
10008{_}5528{_}You remember the vampire bats, Slade?
10008{_}5529{_}And the devil-fires?
10008{_}5530{_}Naturally I didn't mention to you that the devil-fire business wasn't altogether as clear to me as I pretended.
10008{_}5531{_}It wasn't, though.
10008{_}5532{_}But at the time it served very well as an amusement.
10008{_}5533{_}All the while I realised that my self- entertainment was not without its element of danger, too: I remember glances not altogether friendly but always a little doubtful, a little awed.
10008{_}5534{_}Even Handy Solomon, practical as he was, had a scruple or two of superstition in his make-up, on which one might work.
10008{_}5535{_}Only Eagen--Slade, I mean--was beyond me there.
10008{_}5536{_}You puzzled me not a little in those days, Slade.
10008{_}5537{_}Well....  "Did I say that I was sometimes annoyed by the doctor's attitude?
10008{_}5538{_}Yes: it seemed that he might have given me a little more of his confidence; but one can't judge such a man as he was.
10008{_}5539{_}Among the ordinary affairs of life he had relied on me for every detail.
10008{_}5540{_}Now he was independent of me.
10008{_}5541{_}Independent!
10008{_}5542{_}I doubt if he remembered my existence at times.
10008{_}5543{_}Even in his blackest moods of depression he was sufficient unto himself.
10008{_}5544{_}It was strange.... How he did rage the day the chemicals from Washington went wrong!
10008{_}5545{_}I was washing my shirt in the hot water spring when he came bolting out of the laboratory and keeled me over.
10008{_}5546{_}I came out pretty indignant.
10008{_}5547{_}Apologise?
10008{_}5548{_}Not at all.
10008{_}5549{_}He just sputtered.
10008{_}5550{_}His nearest approach to coherence seemed to indicate a desire that I should go back to Washington at once and destroy a perfectly reputable firm of chemists.
10008{_}5551{_}Finally he calmed down and took it out in entering it in his daily record.
10008{_}5552{_}He was quite proud of that daily record and remembered to write in it on an average of once a week.
10008{_}5553{_}"Then the chest went wrong.
10008{_}5554{_}Whether it had rusted a bit, or whether the chemicals had got in their work on the hinges, I don't know; but one day the Professor, of his own initiative, recognised my existence by lugging his box out in the open and asking me to fix it.
10008{_}5555{_}Previously he had emptied it.
10008{_}5556{_}It was rather a complicated thing, with an inner compartment over which was a hollow cover, opening along one rim.
10008{_}5557{_}That, I conjectured, was designed to hold some chemical compound or salt.
10008{_}5558{_}There were many minor openings, too, each guarded by a similar hollow door.
10008{_}5559{_}My business was with the heavy top cover.
10008{_}5560{_}"'It should shut and open softly, gently,' explained the Professor.
10008{_}5561{_}'So.
10008{_}5562{_}Not with-a-grating-sound-to-be-accompanied,' he added, with his curious effect of linked phraseology.
10008{_}5563{_}"Half a day's work fixed it.
10008{_}5564{_}The lid would stand open of itself until tipped at a considerable angle, when it would fall and lock.
10008{_}5565{_}Only on the outer shell was there a lock: that one was a good bit of craftsmanship.
10008{_}5566{_}"'So, Percy, my boy,' said the doctor kindly.
10008{_}5567{_}'That will with-sufficient- safety guard our treasure.
10008{_}5568{_}When we obtain it, Percy.
10008{_}5569{_}When it entirely- finished-and-completed shall be.'
10008{_}5570{_}"'And when will that be?'
10008{_}5571{_}I asked.
10008{_}5572{_}"'God knows,' he said cheerfully.
10008{_}5573{_}'It progresses.'
10008{_}5574{_}"Whenever I went strolling at night, he would produce his curious lights.
10008{_}5575{_}Sometimes they were fairly startling.
10008{_}5576{_}One fact I made out by accident, looking down from a high place.
10008{_}5577{_}They did not project from the laboratory.
10008{_}5578{_}He always worked in the open when the light was to be produced.
10008{_}5579{_}Once the experiment took a serious turn.
10008{_}5580{_}The lights had flickered and gone.
10008{_}5581{_}Dr. Schermerhorn had returned to his laboratory.
10008{_}5582{_}I came up the arroyo as he flung the door open and rushed out.
10008{_}5583{_}He was a grotesque figure, clad in an undershirt and a worn pair of trousers, fastened with an old bit of tarred rope in lieu of his suspenders, which I had been repairing.
10008{_}5584{_}About his waist flickered a sort of aura of radiance which was extinguished as he flung himself headforemost into the cold spring.
10008{_}5585{_}I hauled him out.
10008{_}5586{_}He seemed dazed.
10008{_}5587{_}To my questions he replied only by mumblings, the burden of which was:  "'I do not understand.
10008{_}5588{_}It is a not-to-be-comprehended accident.'
10008{_}5589{_}It appears that he didn't quite know why he had taken to the water.
10008{_}5590{_}Or if he did, he didn't want to tell.
10008{_}5591{_}"Next day he was as good as new.
10008{_}5592{_}Just as silent as before, but it was a smiling, satisfied silence.
10008{_}5593{_}So it went for weeks, for months, with the accesses of depression and anger always rarer.
10008{_}5594{_}Then came an afternoon when, returning from a stalk after sheep, I heard strange and shocking noises from the laboratory.
10008{_}5595{_}Strict as was the embargo which kept me outside the door, I burst in, only to be seized in a suffocating grip.
10008{_}5596{_}Of a sudden I realised that I was being embraced.
10008{_}5597{_}The doctor flourished a hand above my head and jigged with ponderous steps.
10008{_}5598{_}The dismal noises continued to emanate from his mouth.
10008{_}5599{_}He was singing.
10008{_}5600{_}I wish I could give you a notion of the amazement, the paralysing wonder with which.... No, you did not know Dr. Schermerhorn: you would not understand....  "We polkaed into the open.
10008{_}5601{_}There he cast me loose.
10008{_}5602{_}He stopped singing and burst into a rhapsody of disjointed words.
10008{_}5603{_}Mostly German, it was--a wondrous jumble of the scientific and poetic.
10008{_}5604{_}'Eureka' occurred at intervals.
10008{_}5605{_}Then he would leap in the air.
10008{_}5606{_}It was weird, it was distressing.
10008{_}5607{_}Crazy?
10008{_}5608{_}Oh, quite.
10008{_}5609{_}For the time, you understand.
10008{_}5610{_}If any of us should suddenly become the most potent individual in the world, wouldn't he be apt to lose balance temporarily?
10008{_}5611{_}One must make allowances.
10008{_}5612{_}There was excuse for the doctor.
10008{_}5613{_}He had reached the goal.
10008{_}5614{_}"'Percy, you shall be rewarded,' he said.
10008{_}5615{_}'You haf like-a-trump-card stuck by me.
10008{_}5616{_}You shall haf riches, gold, what you will.
10008{_}5617{_}You are young; your blood runs red.
10008{_}5618{_}With such riches nothing is beyond you.
10008{_}5619{_}You could the ancient-tombs-of-Egypt explore.
10008{_}5620{_}It is open to you such collections-as- have-never-been-gathered to make.
10008{_}5621{_}What shall it be?
10008{_}5622{_}Scarabs?
10008{_}5623{_}Missals?
10008{_}5624{_}Prehistoric implements?
10008{_}5625{_}Amuse yourself, _mein kind_.
10008{_}5626{_}We shall be able the- bills-with-usurious-interest to pay.
10008{_}5627{_}What will you haf?'
10008{_}5628{_}"I said I'd like a vacation, if convenient.
10008{_}5629{_}"'Presently,' he replied.
10008{_}5630{_}'There yet remains the guardianship to be perfected.
10008{_}5631{_}Then to-a-world-astonished-and-respectful we return.
10008{_}5632{_}To-night we celebrate.
10008{_}5633{_}I play you a rubber of pinochle.'
10008{_}5634{_}"We played.
10008{_}5635{_}With the greatest secret of science resting at our elbows, we played.
10008{_}5636{_}The doctor won; my mind was not strictly on the game.
10008{_}5637{_}In the morning the doctor sang once more....
10008{_}5638{_}I shall never hear its like again.
10008{_}5639{_}Was it a week, or a month, after that?...
10008{_}5640{_}I cannot remember.
10008{_}5641{_}I fancy I was excited.
10008{_}5642{_}Then, too, there was something in the atmosphere about the laboratory ...
10008{_}5643{_}I don't know; imagination, possibly.
10008{_}5644{_}Once we had a little manifestation: the night that the Nigger and Slade were terrified by the rock fires.
10008{_}5645{_}Days of excitement and pleasant work, with the little volcano grumbling more sulkily all the time ...
10008{_}5646{_}I have spent worse days.
10008{_}5647{_}"Such indifference as the doctor displayed toward the volcano I have never known.
10008{_}5648{_}If I ventured to warn him he would assure me that there was no cause for alarm.
10008{_}5649{_}I think he regarded that little hell's kitchen as merely a feed-spout for his vast enterprise.
10008{_}5650{_}He felt a sort of affection toward it; he was tolerant of its petty fits of temper.
10008{_}5651{_}That he completed his work before the destruction came was sheer luck.
10008{_}5652{_}Nothing else.
10008{_}5653{_}The day before the outburst he came to me with a tiny phial of complicated design.
10008{_}5654{_}"'Percy, I will at-a-reasonable-price sell this to you,' he said.
10008{_}5655{_}"'How much?'
10008{_}5656{_}I inquired, responding to his playfulness.
10008{_}5657{_}"'A bargain,' he cried gaily.
10008{_}5658{_}'Five millions dollars.
10008{_}5659{_}No!
10008{_}5660{_}Shall I upon-a- needy-friend hard-press?
10008{_}5661{_}Never.
10008{_}5662{_}One million.
10008{_}5663{_}One little million dollars.'
10008{_}5664{_}"'I haven't that amount with me,' I began.
10008{_}5665{_}"'Of no account,' he declared airily.
10008{_}5666{_}'Soon we shall haf many more times as that.
10008{_}5667{_}Gif me your C.O.
10008{_}5668{_}D.'  "'My I. O.
10008{_}5669{_}U.?'
10008{_}5670{_}I inquired.
10008{_}5671{_}"'It makes no matter.
10008{_}5672{_}See.
10008{_}5673{_}I will gif it to you gratis.'
10008{_}5674{_}"He handed me the metal contrivance.
10008{_}5675{_}It was closed.
10008{_}5676{_}"'Inside iss a little, such a very little.
10008{_}5677{_}Not yet iss it arranged the motive-power to give-forth.
10008{_}5678{_}One more change-to-be-made that shall require.
10008{_}5679{_}But the other phenomena are all in this little half-grain comprised.
10008{_}5680{_}Later I shall tell you more.
10008{_}5681{_}Take it.
10008{_}5682{_}It iss without price.'
10008{_}5683{_}He laid his hand on my shoulder.
10008{_}5684{_}'Like the love of friends,' he said gently."
10008{_}5685{_}Feeling in his upper waistcoat pocket, Darrow brought out a phial, so tiny that it rolled in the palm of his hand.
10008{_}5686{_}He contemplated it, lost in thought.
10008{_}5687{_}"Radium?"
10008{_}5688{_}queried Barnett, with the keen interest of the scientist.
10008{_}5689{_}"God knows what it is," said Darrow, rousing himself.
10008{_}5690{_}"Not the perfected product; the doctor said that when he gave it to me.
10008{_}5691{_}If I could remember one-tenth of what he told me that night!
10008{_}5692{_}It is like a disordered dream, a phantasmagoria of monstrous powers, lit up with an intolerable, almost an infernal radiance.
10008{_}5693{_}This much I did gather: that Dr. Schermerhorn had achieved what the greatest minds before him had barely outlined.
10008{_}5694{_}Yes, and more.
10008{_}5695{_}Becquerel, the Curies, Rutherford--they were playing with the letters of the Greek alphabet, Alphas, Gammas, and Rhos, while the simple, gentle old boy that I served had read the secret.
10008{_}5696{_}From the molten eruptions of the racked earth he had taken gases and potencies that are nameless.
10008{_}5697{_}By what methods of combination and refining I do not know, he produced something that was to be the final word of power.
10008{_}5698{_}Control-- control--that was all that lacked.
10008{_}5699{_}"Reduced to its simplest terms, it meant this: the doctor had something as much greater than radium as radium is greater than the pitchblende of which a thousand tons are melted down to the one ounce of extract.
10008{_}5700{_}And the incredible energies of this he proposed to divide into departments of activity.
10008{_}5701{_}One manifestation should be light, a light that would illuminate the world.
10008{_}5702{_}Another was to make motive power so cheap that the work of the world could be done in an hour out of the day.
10008{_}5703{_}Some idea he had of healing properties.
10008{_}5704{_}Yes; he was to cure mankind.
10008{_}5705{_}Or kill, kill as no man had ever killed, did he choose.
10008{_}5706{_}The armies and navies of the powers would be at his mercy.
10008{_}5707{_}Magnetism was to be his slave.
10008{_}5708{_}Aerial navigation, transmutation of metals, the screening of gravity--does this sound like delirium?
10008{_}5709{_}Sometimes I think it was.
10008{_}5710{_}"That night he turned over to me the key of the large chest and his ledger.
10008{_}5711{_}The latter he bade me read.
10008{_}5712{_}It was a complete jumble.
10008{_}5713{_}You have seen it.... We were up a good part of the night with our pet volcano.
10008{_}5714{_}It was suffering from internal disturbances.
10008{_}5715{_}'So,' the doctor would say indulgently, when a particularly active rock came bounding down our way.
10008{_}5716{_}'Little play-antics-to-exhibit now that the work iss finished.'
10008{_}5717{_}"In the morning he insisted on my leaving him alone and going down to give the orders.
10008{_}5718{_}I took the ledger, intending to send it aboard.
10008{_}5719{_}It saved my life possibly: Solomon's bullet deflected slightly, I think, in passing through the heavy paper.
10008{_}5720{_}Slade has told you about my flight.
10008{_}5721{_}I ought to have gone straight up the arroyo....
10008{_}5722{_}Yet I could hardly have made it....
10008{_}5723{_}I did not see him again, the doctor.
10008{_}5724{_}My last glimpse ... the old man--I remember now how the grey had spread through his beard--he was growing old--it had been ageing labour.
10008{_}5725{_}He stood there at his laboratory door and the mountain spouted and thundered behind.
10008{_}5726{_}"'We will a name-to-suit-properly gif it,' he said, as I left him.
10008{_}5727{_}'It shall make us as the gods.
10008{_}5728{_}We will call it celestium.'
10008{_}5729{_}"I left him there smiling.
10008{_}5730{_}Smiling happily.
10008{_}5731{_}The greatest force of his age--if he had lived.
10008{_}5732{_}Very wise, very simple--a kind old child.
10008{_}5733{_}May I trouble you for a light?
10008{_}5734{_}Thanks."
10008{_}5735{_}X  THE DOOM   "Nothing remained but to search for his body.
10008{_}5736{_}I was sure they had killed him and taken the chest.
10008{_}5737{_}I had little expectation of finding him, dead or alive.
10008{_}5738{_}None after I saw the stream of lava pouring into the sea.
10008{_}5739{_}One saves his own life by instinct, I suppose.
10008{_}5740{_}There I was.
10008{_}5741{_}I had to live.
10008{_}5742{_}It did not matter much, but I continued to do it by various shifts.
10008{_}5743{_}That last day on the headland the fumes nearly got me.
10008{_}5744{_}You may have noted the rather excited scrawl in the back of the ledger?
10008{_}5745{_}Yes, I thought I was gone that time.
10008{_}5746{_}But I got to the cave.
10008{_}5747{_}It was low tide.
10008{_}5748{_}Then the earthquake, and I was walled in.... Mr. Barnett's very accurate explosives--Slade's insistence--your risking your lives as you did, mites on the crust of a red-hot cheese--I hope you know how I feel about it all.
10008{_}5749{_}One can't thank a man properly for the life....  "Oh, the pirates.
10008{_}5750{_}Necessarily it must be a matter of theory, but I think we have it right.
10008{_}5751{_}Slade and I built it up.
10008{_}5752{_}For what it's worth, here it is.
10008{_}5753{_}Let me see: you sighted the glow on the night of the 2d.
10008{_}5754{_}Next day came the deserted ship.
10008{_}5755{_}It must have puzzled you outrageously."
10008{_}5756{_}"It did," said Captain Parkinson, drily.
10008{_}5757{_}"Not an easy problem, even with all the data at hand.
10008{_}5758{_}You, of course, had none.
10008{_}5759{_}On Slade's showing, Handy Solomon and his worthy associates thought they had a chest full of riches when they got the doctor's treasure; believed they owned the machinery for making diamonds or gold or what-not of ready-to-hand wealth.
10008{_}5760{_}It's fair to assume a certain eagerness on their part.
10008{_}5761{_}Disturbed weather keeps them busy until they're well out from the island.
10008{_}5762{_}Then to the chest.
10008{_}5763{_}Opening it isn't so easy: I had the key, you know."
10008{_}5764{_}He brought a curious and delicately wrought skeleton from his pocket.
10008{_}5765{_}"Tipped with platinum," he observed.
10008{_}5766{_}"Rather a gem of a key, I think.
10008{_}5767{_}You see, there must have been some action, even through the keyhole, or he wouldn't have used a metal of this kind.
10008{_}5768{_}But the crew was rich in certain qualities, it seems, which I failed, stupidly, to recognise in my acquaintance with them.
10008{_}5769{_}Both Pulz and Perdosa appear to have been handy men where locks were concerned.
10008{_}5770{_}First Pulz sneaks down and has his turn at the chest.
10008{_}5771{_}He gets it open.
10008{_}5772{_}Small profit for him in that: the next we know of him he is scandalising Handy Solomon by having a fit on the deck."
10008{_}5773{_}"That is what I couldn't figure out to save my life," said Slade eagerly.
10008{_}5774{_}"If you recollect, I told you of the Professor's plunge in the cold spring, in a sort of paroxysm, one day," said Darrow.
10008{_}5775{_}"That was the physiological action of the celestium.
10008{_}5776{_}At other times, I have seen him come out and deliberately roll in the creek, head under.
10008{_}5777{_}Once he explained that the medium he worked in caused a kind of uncontrollable longing for water; something having none of the qualities of burning or thirst, but an irresistible temporary mania.
10008{_}5778{_}It worried him a good deal; he didn't understand it.
10008{_}5779{_}That, then, was what ailed Pulz.
10008{_}5780{_}When he opened the chest there was, as I surmise, a trifling quantity of this stuff lying in the inner lid.
10008{_}5781{_}It wasn't the celestium itself, as I imagine, but a sort of by- product with the physiological and radiant effects of the real thing, and it had been set there on guard, a discouragement to the spirit of investigation, as it were.
10008{_}5782{_}So, when the top was lifted, our little guardian gets in its work, producing the light phenomenon that so puzzled Slade, and inspiring Pulz with a passion for the rolling wave, which is only interrupted by Handy Solomon's tackling him.
10008{_}5783{_}As he fled he must have pulled down the cover."
10008{_}5784{_}"He did," said Slade.
10008{_}5785{_}"I heard the clang.
10008{_}5786{_}But I saw the radiance on the clouds.
10008{_}5787{_}And the whole thickness of a solid oak deck was in between the sky and the chest."
10008{_}5788{_}"Oh, a little thing like an oak deck wouldn't interrupt the kind of rays the doctor used.
10008{_}5789{_}He had his own method of screening, you understand.
10008{_}5790{_}However, this inconsiderable guardian affair must have used itself up, which true celestium wouldn't have done.
10008{_}5791{_}So when Perdosa sets his genius for lock-picking to the task, the inner box, full of the genuine article, has no warning sign-post, so to speak.
10008{_}5792{_}Everything's peaceful until they raise the compound-filled hollow layer of the inner cover, which serves to interrupt the action.
10008{_}5793{_}Then comes the general exit and the superior fireworks."
10008{_}5794{_}"That's when the rays ran through the ship," said Slade.
10008{_}5795{_}"It seemed to follow the deck-lines."
10008{_}5796{_}"The stuff had a strange affinity for tar," said Darrow.
10008{_}5797{_}"I told you of the circle of fire about Professor Schermerhorn's waist the day he gave me such a scare.
10008{_}5798{_}That was the celestium working on the tarred rope he wore for a belt.
10008{_}5799{_}It made a livid circle on his skin.
10008{_}5800{_}Did I tell you of his experiments with pitch?
10008{_}5801{_}It doesn't matter.
10008{_}5802{_}Where was I?"
10008{_}5803{_}"At the place where we all jumped," said Slade.
10008{_}5804{_}"Oh, yes.
10008{_}5805{_}And you dove into the small boat, trying to reach the water."
10008{_}5806{_}"Wait a bit," said Barnett.
10008{_}5807{_}"If that was the exhibition of radiance we saw, it died out in a few minutes.
10008{_}5808{_}How was that?
10008{_}5809{_}Did they close the chest before they ran?"
10008{_}5810{_}"Probably not," replied Darrow.
10008{_}5811{_}"Slade spoke of Pulz taking to the maintop and being shaken out by the sudden shock of a wave.
10008{_}5812{_}That may have been a volcanic billow.
10008{_}5813{_}Whatever it was, it undoubtedly heeled the ship sufficiently to bring down both lids, which were rather delicately balanced."
10008{_}5814{_}"Yes, for Billy Edwards found the chest closed and locked," said Barnett.
10008{_}5815{_}"Of course; it was a spring lock.
10008{_}5816{_}You sent Mr. Edwards and his men aboard.
10008{_}5817{_}No such experts as Pulz or Perdosa were in your crew.
10008{_}5818{_}Consequently it took longer to get the chest open.
10008{_}5819{_}When at length the lid was raised, there was a repetition of the tragedy.
10008{_}5820{_}Mr. Edwards and his men leaped.
10008{_}5821{_}Probably they were paralysed almost before they struck the water.
10008{_}5822{_}Your bos'n, whom Slade picked up, was the only one who had time even to grab a life preserver before the impulse toward water became irresistible.
10008{_}5823{_}There was no element of fright, you understand: no desertion of their post.
10008{_}5824{_}They were dragged as by the sweep of a tornado."
10008{_}5825{_}Darrow spoke direct to Captain Parkinson.
10008{_}5826{_}"If there is any feeling among you other than sorrow for their death, it is unjust and unworthy."
10008{_}5827{_}"Thank you, Mr. Darrow," returned the captain quietly.
10008{_}5828{_}"We found the chest closed again when the empty ship came back," observed Barnett.
10008{_}5829{_}"Being masterless, the schooner began to yaw," continued Darrow.
10008{_}5830{_}"The first time she came about would have heeled her enough to shut the chest.
10008{_}5831{_}Now came the turn of your other men."
10008{_}5832{_}"Ives and McGuire," said the Captain, as Darrow paused.
10008{_}5833{_}"The glow came again that night, and the next day we picked up Slade," said Barnett.
10008{_}5834{_}"You know what the glow meant for your companions," said Darrow.
10008{_}5835{_}"But the ship.
10008{_}5836{_}The _Laughing Lass_, man.
10008{_}5837{_}She's vanished.
10008{_}5838{_}No one has seen her since."
10008{_}5839{_}"You are wrong there," said Darrow.
10008{_}5840{_}"I have seen her."
10008{_}5841{_}In a common impulse the little circle leaned to him.
10008{_}5842{_}"Yes, I have seen her.
10008{_}5843{_}I wish I had not.
10008{_}5844{_}Let me bring my story back to the cave on the island.
10008{_}5845{_}After the volcanic gases had driven me to the refuge, I sat near the mouth of the cave looking out into the darkness.
10008{_}5846{_}That was the night of the 7th, the night you saw the last glow.
10008{_}5847{_}It was very dark, except for occasional bursts of fire from the crater.
10008{_}5848{_}Judge of my incredulous amazement when, in an access of this illumination, I saw plainly a schooner hardly a mile off shore, coming in under bare poles."
10008{_}5849{_}"Under bare poles?"
10008{_}5850{_}cried Slade.
10008{_}5851{_}"The halliards must have disintegrated from some slow action of the celestium.
10008{_}5852{_}It could be destructive: terrifically destructive.
10008{_}5853{_}You shall judge.
10008{_}5854{_}There was the schooner, naked as your hand.
10008{_}5855{_}Possibly I might have thought it a hallucination but for what came after.
10008{_}5856{_}Darkness fell again.
10008{_}5857{_}I supposed then that Handy Solomon's crew were managing--or mismanaging--the _Laughing Lass_ without the aid of their leader, whom I had satisfactorily buried.
10008{_}5858{_}I hoped they would come ashore on the rocks.
10008{_}5859{_}Yes I was vengeful ... then.
10008{_}5860{_}"Of a sudden there sprang from the darkness a ship of light.
10008{_}5861{_}You have all seen those great electric effects at expositions.
10008{_}5862{_}Someone touches a button ... you know.
10008{_}5863{_}It was like that.
10008{_}5864{_}Only that the piercingly brilliant jewelled wonder of a ship was set in the midst of a swirl of vari-coloured radiance such as I can't begin to describe.
10008{_}5865{_}You saw it from a distance.
10008{_}5866{_}Imagine what it was, coming close upon you that way--dead on, out of the night.
10008{_}5867{_}A living glory, a living terror...."  His voice sank.
10008{_}5868{_}With a shaking hand he fumbled amid his cigarette papers.
10008{_}5869{_}"It came on.
10008{_}5870{_}A human figure, glowing like a diamond ablaze, leaped out from it; another shot down from the foremast.
10008{_}5871{_}I don't know how many I saw go.
10008{_}5872{_}It was like a theatric effect, unreal, unconvincing, incredible.
10008{_}5873{_}The end fitted it."
10008{_}5874{_}Darrow's eye roved.
10008{_}5875{_}It fell upon a quaintly modelled ship, hung above the door.
10008{_}5876{_}"What's that?"
10008{_}5877{_}he cried.
10008{_}5878{_}"Fool thing some Malay gave me," grunted Trendon.
10008{_}5879{_}"Pretended to be grateful because I cut his foot off.
10008{_}5880{_}No good.
10008{_}5881{_}Go on with the story."
10008{_}5882{_}"No good?
10008{_}5883{_}You don't care what happens to it?"
10008{_}5884{_}"Meant to heave it overboard before now," growled the other.
10008{_}5885{_}Someone handed it down to Darrow.
10008{_}5886{_}"If I had something to hold enough water," muttered he, "I'd like to float it.
10008{_}5887{_}I'd like to see for myself how it worked out.
10008{_}5888{_}I'd like to see that devil-work in action."
10008{_}5889{_}He spoke feverishly.
10008{_}5890{_}"Boy, fill the portable rubber tub in Mr. Forsythe's cabin and bring it here," ordered the captain.
10008{_}5891{_}"That will do."
10008{_}5892{_}said Darrow, recovering himself.
10008{_}5893{_}He floated the model in the tub.
10008{_}5894{_}"Now, I don't know how this will come out," he said.
10008{_}5895{_}"Nor do I know why the _Laughing Lass_ met her fate under Ives and McGuire, and not before.
10008{_}5896{_}Perhaps the chest lay open longer ... long enough, anyway.
10008{_}5897{_}We'll try it."
10008{_}5898{_}From his pocket he took a curious small phial.
10008{_}5899{_}"Is that what Dr. Schermerhorn gave you?"
10008{_}5900{_}asked Slade.
10008{_}5901{_}"Yes," said Darrow.
10008{_}5902{_}He set it carefully inside the little model and slipped a lever.
10008{_}5903{_}Slade quietly turned down the light.
10008{_}5904{_}A faint glow shot up.
10008{_}5905{_}It grew bright and eddied in lovely, variant colours.
10008{_}5906{_}As if set to a powder train, it ran through the ship.
10008{_}5907{_}The pale faces of the spectators shone ghastly in its radiance.
10008{_}5908{_}From someone burst a sudden gasp.
10008{_}5909{_}"There is not enough for danger," said Darrow, quietly.
10008{_}5910{_}"As a point of interest," grunted Trendon.
10008{_}5911{_}Everyone looked at his outstretched hand.
10008{_}5912{_}A little pocket compass lay in the palm.
10008{_}5913{_}The needle spun madly, projecting blue, vivid sparklings.
10008{_}5914{_}"My God!"
10008{_}5915{_}cried Slade, and covered his eyes for a moment.
10008{_}5916{_}He snatched away his hands as a suppressed cry went up from the others.
10008{_}5917{_}"As I expected," said Darrow quietly.
10008{_}5918{_}The little craft opened out; it disintegrated.
10008{_}5919{_}All that radiance dissolved and with its going the substance upon which it shaped itself vanished.
10008{_}5920{_}The last glow showed a formless pulp, spreading upon the water.
10008{_}5921{_}"So passed the _Laughing Lass_," said Darrow solemnly.
10008{_}5922{_}"And the chest is at the bottom of the sea," said Barnett.
10008{_}5923{_}"Good place for it," muttered Trendon.
10008{_}5924{_}"In all probability it closed as the ship dissolved around it," said Darrow.
10008{_}5925{_}"Otherwise we should see the effects in the water."
10008{_}5926{_}"It might be recovered," cried Slade, excitedly.
10008{_}5927{_}"Could you chart it, Darrow?
10008{_}5928{_}Think of the possibilities--"  "Let it lie," said the captain.
10008{_}5929{_}"Has it not cost enough?
10008{_}5930{_}Let it lie."
10008{_}5931{_}The water in the tub fumed and sparkled faintly and was still.
10008{_}5932{_}Darkness fell, except where Darrow's cigarette point glowed and faded.
